Ministry of Finance Stipulates Measures for Exporting Surplus Salt to Japan 12

Merchants Must First Apply for Review: Circular Telegrams Sent to the Four Regional Transport Commissioners

(Nanjing) Regarding the case of exporting surplus salt from various regions to Japan for industrial use, the Ministry of Finance is currently reviewing it and has established four measures to suit the current actual situation:

1. If there is surplus salt in various regions, it may be exported to Japan for industrial use, but only after certification by the Japan Monopoly Bureau.

2. Merchants requesting to export must first submit a request to the local salt affairs authority, which will conduct a thorough review to ensure that they are purely Chinese merchants with genuine capital and shares. The request will then be submitted to the Ministry for review and approval, and the merchant will be officially designated as an exporter. Those who directly submit requests to the Ministry will be instructed to submit them to the relevant regional authority for review and reporting before final approval. The number of exporters will be limited to three or more in each region, on a trial basis for one year.

3. The tax rate for industrial salt exported to Japan from each region will be temporarily set at one yuan per metric ton, and a cash deposit or a reliable bank guarantee will also be collected according to the highest tax rate in each region.

4. When salt is exported, all procedures, including inspection and verification, shall still be handled in accordance with the measures for exporting Chinese salt. The above measures were telegraphed by the Ministry of Finance to the Transport Commissioners of Changlu, Shandong, Lianghuai, and Fujian early on the morning of the 11th. (11th Central News Agency Dispatch)

(Tianjin) The Ministry of Finance believes that the issue of exporting Changlu salt is too serious and has ordered the Changlu Transport Office to handle it directly. The Changlu Salt Export Bureau and the Beach Industry Management Bureau will be abolished, and the regulations will be repealed. The Transport Office will formulate new measures for exporting salt, which will be changed. (11th Special Dispatch)

(Tianjin) The Changlu Salt Export Bureau and the Changlu Beach Industry Management Bureau began closing down on the 11th. Director Liang Zhaoyuan went to Beiping to report to the Hebei-Chahar Political Council. The bureau was established two weeks ago, and the operating expenses totaled 3,000 yuan, which has been allocated by the Hebei-Chahar Political Council. Recently, Qingdao has been producing a lot of salt, and the Japanese are actively buying it there. They are no longer actively buying and transporting Changlu salt. Therefore, the export of Changlu salt to Japan has been effectively postponed. (11th Special Dispatch)

Current Commentary

A Perspective on the Attitudes of Britain and France Towards Italy 14

— Wei

When the League of Nations, based on Article 16 of the Covenant, passed the economic sanctions plan against Italy, people around the world did not believe that it could achieve the practical effect of sanctions. However, they also did not expect that the result would be the same as the Manchurian Incident. Now we know what the so-called peace, justice, and humanity in the mouths of imperialists really mean.

Under the current situation, can the major powers that control the League of Nations, such as Britain and France, truly stand up for justice, impose economic sanctions, and follow up with military sanctions? Even if the Locarno Treaty had not been declared abolished, even if the German armed forces had not entered the demilitarized zone of the Rhineland, these major powers would not be willing to fulfill this task for their despised colored races. Moreover, at this time of European turmoil?

The attitude of the British Conservative government was extremely ambiguous at the beginning of the Italo-Ethiopian War. The reason why the Conservative Party changed its past attitude at the end of last year and tried its best to impose sanctions on Italy was actually because the election period was approaching, and British public opinion was unanimously opposed to the war of aggression. In order to cater to public opinion and win the election, the Conservative Party had no choice but to advocate sanctions against Italy. Therefore, this move by the Conservative Party was not out of love for peace, nor out of love for Abyssinia. With the victory in the election, the Conservative Party's goal has been achieved, and the Conservative Party's betrayal of the League of Nations and the betrayal of Ethiopia also began. Foreign Secretary Hoare actually jointly drafted a peace plan with French Prime Minister Laval, recognizing Italy's occupation of Ethiopian land acquired in the war of aggression, and demarcating a large part of Ethiopian land for Italian immigrants and economic development. The face of the angel of peace suddenly changed into a ferocious one, which is why it aroused dissatisfaction among the people of the country and had no choice but to resign. Although the Conservative Party has suffered this setback, its fundamental policy has not changed. If Italy's attitude is not too excessive, its desires are not too extravagant, and military actions in East Africa can be kept within limits and not encroach on the British sphere of influence in the Lake Tana basin, it can be expected that the British Conservative Party will choose an appropriate time to generously give away other people's property in order to achieve so-called peace.

If the attitude of Britain is like this, what about France?

Before we discuss French policy, we must first know the difference between the left and right wings of France on Italian policy. When the British advocated sanctions, the French right-wing newspapers believed that this move would be enough to destroy the Stresa Front, drive France and Italy into opposition, and allow the German National Socialists to have the leeway to intervene in Austria-Hungary and Memel. The left-wing newspapers held a different view, saying that France must unite with Britain to ensure the safety of the Rhine River and maintain the spirit of Locarno. Although the opinions of the two factions differed greatly, they agreed on preventing the resurgence of Germany and maintaining France's security on the continent. The Laval cabinet was like this, and the Sarraut cabinet was also like this. Therefore, from former Foreign Minister Laval to the current Foreign Minister Flandin, their foreign policy is willing to maintain their coordinated relationship with Britain since the European War, and they are also willing to maintain the Stresa Front and the Franco-Italian intimacy that arose after the Rome Agreement.

Until recently, the mutual relationship between Britain, France, and Italy has undergone rapid changes. German troops are stationed in the demilitarized zone, and France's attitude towards Italy has undergone a sudden change. Italian troops have occupied the city of Gondar in Ethiopia, and the vanguard is approaching the Lake Tana basin, and Britain's attitude has undergone a sudden change. The enemy of France on the European continent is Germany, not Italy, while the enemy of Britain in the Mediterranean and Africa is Italy, not Germany. Different interests lead to different orientations. In order to prevent German revenge, France is extremely willing to maintain the Locarno tradition. Britain guarantees its security, but the British Conservative Party has never made a clear indication. France will inevitably have to turn to another great power, both Latin and a powerful support, for support. How can France please Italy? This has become the primary consideration for French politicians at present. Under this situation, France does not dare to openly offend Italy, which is to be expected. Italy will also take advantage of this opportunity, which is also natural. Italy's use of Austria to assert itself and its alliance with Germany to strengthen its voice are all meant to show the French that if they intensify sanctions, Italy will go elsewhere and become an enemy of France. In order to win over Italy, how could France not go against the British and propose a suspension of sanctions to show favor to Italy? France and Italy are colluding with each other, which will inevitably cause displeasure to the British. What Britain values is the source of the Blue Nile. Now that the Italian army has reached the Lake Tana area, if Lake Tana is controlled by Italy, the water conservancy of the cotton-growing area in the Sudanese part of Egypt will be disrupted. We have seen news that the Italian authorities have expressed respect for Egyptian interests, but the Italian respect for British interests in the Lake Tana basin has not yet been heard. The progress of the Italian army and the ambition of the Italians are all in conflict with British interests. The anxiety of the British can be imagined. British Foreign Secretary Eden pointed out the cruelty of the Italians and the efforts of the Thriteen-Nation Committee to [missing words].

If there are no special developments in the overall European situation in the future, it can be predicted that Ethiopia will be placed on the altar of the League of Nations and divided by the major powers. What is unknowable is to what extent Italy will be able to satisfy its territorial desires and to what extent Britain will retreat and be willing to give up.

Draft Articles and Schedules of the National Assembly's Two Laws 16

The Central Standing Committee's Principles and Key Points for Amending the Two Laws: Media Representatives May Account for Ten Seats

(Nanjing) The principles for the organization law and the representative election law of the National Assembly, amended by the Central Standing Committee, were submitted to the Legislative Yuan on the 11th. The special 24-member committee of the Legislative Yuan decided to hold its first meeting next week to review the draft articles and schedules of the two laws drafted by the five members including Lin Bin, in accordance with the original and amended principles set by the Central Government. After thorough investigation, the key points of the amendment principles are as follows: The number of National Assembly representatives will remain at 1,200, including 687 regional representatives, 322 professional group representatives, 58 free professional group representatives, 40 overseas Chinese representatives, 40 Mongolian and Tibetan representatives, 23 Northeast representatives, and 30 military representatives. However, Dai Chuanxian and Yu Youren have expressed opinions on the allocation of free professional group representatives and the quota allocation of a certain province for regional representatives. These have also been submitted to the Legislative Yuan for review and appropriate adjustments within the stipulated numbers for each category. Since there is no clear distinction between professional groups and industrial groups, the term "industrial groups" has been deleted from the original principles. The candidates recommended by each electoral district originally had to be reduced by one-fifth after review by the provincial government, but this has now been changed to allow the provincial government to submit opinions, and the Central Government will designate three times the number of representatives to be elected from each district. It is reported that the so-called professional groups refer to chambers of commerce, trade unions, and business associations, while free professional groups refer to associations of lawyers, journalists, accountants, engineers, and medical practitioners. The national media community can occupy about ten seats within the quota of 58 free professional group representatives, and Dai Chuanxian has advocated for an appropriate increase. In addition, the Ministry of Interior and the Ministry of Industry have separately submitted population statistics tables for various provincial districts, as well as the number of people in various professional groups and their business conditions, to the Legislative Yuan for reference. (Central News Agency Dispatch, 11th)

The Ministry of Finance Drafts Nine Types of Banking Regulations 17

All drafts have been completed and submitted to the Executive Yuan for review

(Nanjing) After the implementation of the monetary policy last year, the Ministry of Finance drafted nine fundamental banking regulations, divided into exchange, industrial, trust, savings, real estate mortgage, farmer, provincial bank, and county and city bank regulations. The Legal Affairs Committee recently completed all drafts and submitted them to the Executive Yuan for review. After legislative procedures, the Ministry of Finance plans to reorganize the Exchange Bank and the Industrial Bank into the Bank of China and the Bank of Communications, respectively. However, since the banknotes issued by these two banks and the banknotes of the Central Bank are both designated as currency, the two banks will first gradually improve their business operations in the short term, and there will be no nominal changes. The Real Estate Mortgage Bank is currently being prepared by the Construction Bank Corporation. There are still several points regarding mortgage methods that are being requested from the Ministry of Finance, so the date of establishment has not yet been determined. (Special Dispatch, 11th)

Measures for Work Reports of Various Agencies 19

The National Government Approves the Central Political Council's Letter to Send the Work of Various Agencies

(Nanjing) The measures for reporting, reviewing, and revising the format, requesting a unified implementation from May of this year, have been specially ordered to all directly subordinate agencies, ordering them to comply. The main points of the measures are: (A) The work reports of the ministries, commissions, and departments under the Executive Yuan, as well as the provincial and municipal governments and the agencies under the judicial, supervisory, and examination branches, and the military agencies under the Military Affairs Commission, shall be reviewed by the respective Yuan and Councils, and the results, together with the original report, shall be reported to the Central Political Council. The work reports of the Five Yuan and other agencies directly under the National Government shall be reviewed by the Central Political Council. (B) The format of the work reports of the agencies under the Executive Yuan shall be formulated by the Executive Yuan, paying attention to the following points: 　Circumstances of following central laws and regulations; 　Whether single-item laws and regulations conflict with central laws and regulations; 　Comparison and observation of work performance and original administrative plans; 　Whether the allocation of funds is appropriate. The format of work reports of other agencies shall be handled with reference to the regulations set by the Executive Yuan. (C) Statistics on administrative achievements should be included in the work report. (Central News Agency Dispatch, 11th)

The Ministry of Finance Requests an Order to Transfer the Management Rights of Hunan Paste Salt 21

(Nanjing) The Ministry of Finance submitted to the Executive Yuan that many paste salt companies have been established in Xiangtan, Hunan, which produces paste salt. The Hunan Department of Finance only ordered the Xiangtan Business Production and Sales Tax Bureau to collect taxes on a per-pot basis and issue licenses, allowing them to sell in Xiangtan County, but never went through the supervision and inspection procedures of the local salt affairs agencies, which is contrary to the unified system of the salt law. It is urgent to take over management to comply with the new salt law. However, according to the Hunan Provincial Government, the Xiangtan Paste Salt Mining Industry Association stated that the Hunan paste salt industry is in its early stages, with heavy profits and low margins, and requested a postponement of the takeover and tax increase to alleviate the difficulties of the merchants. The Ministry of Finance reviewed that although Hunan paste salt has gradually developed (a paste salt company has also been established in Liuyang County), the commercial strength is still weak, which is also true. It seems that the Management Bureau should take over, and the salt tax to be levied should still be collected at the original business production and sales tax rate levied by the Hunan Provincial Government, without increasing it. Furthermore, the average income of the Hunan Provincial Government from the business production and sales tax levied on these merchants in the past three years should be determined as the annual amount of the central government's non-resident expenses, which will be allocated to the Hunan Provincial Government by the national treasury on a monthly or quarterly basis, so as to eliminate the merchants' concerns about increased burdens, and the provincial government will not have to change the budget. Moreover, since Hunan paste salt is still in its early stages, the management affairs should not be too complicated, and the Xiang'an salt affairs agencies should handle it concurrently, without setting up a special bureau to save expenses. (Special Dispatch, 11th)

The Bandit Suppression Army of Shanxi Captures the Ancient Town 25

The bandits in Lishi are still being suppressed. The Datong-Puzhou Railway has been opened. The military attache of the Japanese embassy will return to Beiping via Taiyuan today.

(Taiyuan) After the siege of the counties in southern Shanxi was lifted, the remnants of the communist bandits, apart from those who were killed or captured, dispersed in different directions. According to a telegram from Xinjiang, bandits gathered in the Xixueguo area of Quanzhang Town. On the 9th, they engaged in a fierce battle with our suppression army, led by Weng brigade, in that area. More than 60 bandits were killed, more than 200 were injured, and more than 40 were captured. The bandits fled southwest, appearing to retreat towards the territory of Jishan County. Furthermore, about 3,000 to 4,000 bandits in the Guchengzhen area north of Fencheng County were attacked and defeated by the Cheng Yangsheng department on the 9th, which divided its forces from Xiangling. The bandits fled in the southwest direction. This town is a famous town in southern Shanxi, and it is heard that the losses are extremely heavy. The bandits in Lishi are still being suppressed. The passenger train on the southern section of the Datong-Puzhou Railway has been opened. The section south of Huoxian is being actively repaired and can be opened soon. The authorities have deployed heavy troops to protect the road in order to maintain north-south transportation. (Special Dispatch, 11th)

(Taiyuan) The bandits in Xiangling, Fencheng, and Xinjiang counties have been vigorously suppressed by our First Route Army and the Central Government forces. They have fled to Xiangning and Jishan counties. The forces under Yang Chengjiang and the Central Government forces under Tang Hu are pursuing and suppressing them in different directions and have dispatched teams to intercept the bandits ahead. The bandits lurking in Zhongyang and Shilou counties have been vigorously searched for by the forces under Sun Chu and have mostly fled to Xixian County. More than 1,000 bandits have gathered in the villages of Chenpo, Huanzhu, and Sanjiao, 30 miles southeast of Xixian County. In addition, more than 1,000 bandit troops have fled from Wan'anzhen, Hongdong, and joined the bandits in Xixian County. Our Chen brigade launched a fierce attack on them. The bandits in Sanjiao suffered heavy casualties. There are many local bad guys among the bandit troops in that area. (Special Dispatch, 11th)

(Taiyuan) The section of the Datong-Puzhou Railway from the south gate of Tailing to Huoxian has been repaired. On the 11th, a passenger train traveled directly from Taiyuan to Huoxian. (Central News Agency Dispatch, 11th)

(Beiping) Gao Guizi received a telegram from Suide today stating that more than 1,000 communist troops under Xu Haidong had fled across the Northeast Dagouzhen. There are also half of them near Lishi. More than 1,000 bandits under Liu Zidan have now fled to Meng County. Some have fled back to Qingjian, and some are entrenched in the Jiashan area. The 2,000-strong guerrillas of the Gu Detachment east of Wu Bei and Suide are also very active. The 8th company of the 2nd History Battalion pursued the bandits to Shizihe, defeating more than 100 bandits and capturing 13 rifles and 1 pistol. They killed the puppet regimental commander Lu Wenchang and cut off his head. It is heard that the Lu bandit is the chief of staff of Liu Zidan. (Special Dispatch, 11th)

Imai's Talk After Returning to Beiping 26

(Beiping) Imai returned to Beiping from Tianjin yesterday. According to his talk, he has met with Yan and other important people in Shanxi and inquired about the bandit suppression situation in Shanxi. The military affairs of bandit suppression in Shanxi are going smoothly. Except for the remnants in the Xingxian and Linxian areas of northern Shanxi, most of the bandits are scattered in the four rural areas near the Fencheng-Datong-Puzhou Railway line in southern Shanxi. In total, there are no more than 10,000 bandits in southwestern Shanxi. The authorities have ample capacity to prevent and suppress them. However, it will still take time to completely eliminate them. The morale in Taiyuan is stable, and the farmers in the suburbs have also started spring plowing. The statement that communist bandits were found in Suiyuan and Baotou is not accurate. (Special Dispatch, 11th)

The Remnants of the Bandits in Guizhou Province Collapsed and Fled 27

(Guiyang) Military news: The remnants of the bandits fled to Pudu River on the 8th and engaged in a fierce battle with our Liu Brigade all day. More than 500 people were killed, more than 100 were captured, and more than 200 rifles and 3 heavy machine guns were seized. The entire puppet 17th Division collapsed and dispersed. Some of the remnants were holding on to Black Mountain, and some were fleeing towards Xinji Street. Our army is still pursuing them. After the bandits retreated to Yunnan, only 8,000 people and more than 300 horses remained, and they were reduced to four divisions. Many people from Hunan Province in another newly编的division died and scattered, and most of them were newly recruited people from Guizhou Province. (Central News Agency Dispatch, 11th)

The Ministry of Finance Dispatches Personnel to Inspect Local Financial Situation 28

(Nanjing) The Ministry of Finance dispatched Zhang Tingxiu and Cui Weiwu, members of the Local Donations and Taxes Consolidation Committee, to Jiangsu; Zhang Sen to Zhejiang; and Zhang Du to Anhui to inspect the local financial situation and the elimination of dangerous, harsh, and miscellaneous taxes. The members have already set off on the 11th. (Central News Agency Dispatch, 11th)

The Central Museum Hires a Total of Thirteen Directors 29

(Nanjing) The first board meeting of the Central Museum will be held on the 15th. The directors of the association are hired by the Ministry of Education. The vacancy of the late Ding Wenjiang will be filled by Zhang Daofan. The directors are Cai Yuanpei, Zhu Jiayi, Li Ji, Fu Sinian, Weng Wenhao, Wang Shijie, Hu Shi, Gu Mengyu, Bing Zhi, Li Zhaohuan, Li Shuhua, Luo Jialun, and Zhang Daofan. The position of Chairman of the Board will be elected at the general meeting. The articles of association of the board have been drafted. (Special Dispatch, 11th)

Private Correspondence May Not Use Public Stationery 30

(Nanjing) The Military Affairs Commission ordered all its subordinate agencies and schools that, from now on, all private correspondence of officials must not use the public stationery and envelopes of their own agencies. Violators will be prosecuted for embezzlement of public property and impersonation. (Special Dispatch, 11th)

The New Building of the Central Daily News is Completed 31

(Nanjing) The new building of the Central Daily News was completed, and Shao Yuanchong, Weng Wenhao, and more than 500 other people were invited to visit it on the morning of the 11th. The newspaper office will move into the new building immediately. (Central News Agency Dispatch, 11th)

The Ministry of Finance Does Not Approve Hunan's Proposed Bank Business Tax 32

(Nanjing) The Hunan Department of Finance plans to levy a business tax on banks opened in Hunan, except for the Bank of China, the Central Bank, the Bank of Communications, and the Hunan Provincial Bank. The Department of Finance was asked for instructions by telegram, and the Ministry of Finance replied that the Ministry is planning to implement a tax on bank business income. The original telegram proposed that a business tax be levied on banks opened in Hunan, except for the Bank of China, the Central Bank, the Bank of Communications, and the Hunan Provincial Bank. This is not in line with the provisions of the Business Tax Law and the Bank Business Income Tax Law, and it is difficult to approve. However, recently, some money shops in Hunan Province have arbitrarily changed their names to banks in an attempt to evade taxes, which is also inappropriate. They should be ordered to promptly comply with the current banking laws and regulations and submit statutory documents to the Ministry for registration. If they delay in complying, they should be immediately banned in order to prevent trickery and emphasize tax revenue. (Special Dispatch, 11th)

Gu Shaochuan and Others Form the Gansu, Xinjiang, and Qinghai Petroleum Mining Company 33

(Nanjing) Gu Shaochuan and others have formed a petroleum company to explore and extract petroleum in Gansu, Xinjiang, and Qinghai provinces. They have submitted a request to the Ministry of Industry to issue a permit. The Ministry of Industry ordered the company on the 11th to report its construction plan and implementation methods immediately. (Special Dispatch, 11th)

The Ministry of Finance Approves the Shanghai Chamber of Commerce 34

(Nanjing) The Shanghai Chamber of Commerce previously submitted a request to the Ministry of Finance to cast additional two-and-a-half-cent copper auxiliary coins to facilitate the business of small vendors and maintain the market. The Ministry of Finance replied on the 11th that it will consider the needs of the market after the old copper auxiliary coins have been recovered to a manageable level. (Special Dispatch, 11th)

Judgment in the Appeal Case of Painters in Beijing 35

(Nanjing) In the case of the son of the painter Lu Changling in Beijing for bigamy, the Capital District Court sentenced Lu Changling to two months in prison and Lu Xiaochuan to ten months in prison. Lu Changling appealed to the Fifth Higher Court of Jiangsu in Zhenjiang. The court announced the judgment the day before yesterday that Lu Changling was sentenced to two months in prison, suspended for two years, and Lu Xiaochuan's original sentence was upheld and he was still sentenced to ten months in prison. The main text of the judgment was delivered to Beijing on the 11th (Special Dispatch, 11th)

The Tianjin Mint is Preparing to Start Work 36

The person in charge of the factory said that he would start work according to the order of the Hebei-Chahar Political Council, but the Ministry of Finance did not acknowledge this statement. The factory does not know. (Special Dispatch, 11th)

The Locarno Conference Decides to Continue Negotiations with Germany; Britain Undertakes to Inquire with Germany on Four Points; Assistance to France Against Increased Defense of the Rhine 39

(Geneva) The four signatory countries of the Locarno Treaty, Britain, France, Italy, and Belgium, held a meeting yesterday and have reached an agreement to study various opportunities for reconciliation, so that the situation caused by Germany's entry into the Rhine can be resolved satisfactorily. The meeting started at 3:00 p.m. and ended at 8:00 p.m. It reconvened at 9:15 p.m. and decided to hold another meeting during the meeting of the League of Nations Executive Council on May 11. The Italian representative reserved his opinion on this agreement. (Reuters Dispatch, 11th)

(Geneva) Today's meeting of the Locarno signatories decided to authorize British Foreign Secretary Eden to continue negotiations with German leader Hitler in order to resolve the Rhine issue. Although French Foreign Minister Flandin believed that negotiations with Germany could not be conducted, this opposition was not adopted by the meeting, so it can be said that British diplomacy has won another victory. The Locarno Conference then adjourned until the middle of next month, when the French general election should be revealed. (National News Agency Dispatch, 10th)

(Geneva) According to the news from the special correspondent of this agency, after the second decision-making meeting of the Locarno signatories, the opinions of Britain and France have become very close. Originally, France thought that the hope of reaching a compromise with Germany had failed, so it advocated implementing the various measures contained in the Locarno Treaty. Now, it has accepted the British opinion and allowed the country to continue its efforts to persuade Germany to accept the principle of collective security. Britain, on the other hand, accepted the French opinion that once Germany builds defensive fortifications in the Rhine region, it should come out to assist France and resist. In addition, the British also based on the memorandum submitted by the French government on April 8 and asked Germany to explain the four points contained in the German memorandum of March 31 in order to know the true intention. The so-called four points are: How can the non-aggression treaties proposed by Germany be integrated with the basic principles of the League of Nations Covenant, that is, the principle of collective security? What is the intention of separating the League of Nations Covenant from the Treaty of Versailles and making it an independent chapter? What is the content of the equal rights demanded by Germany regarding the colonial issue? Regarding the current situation in Austria, the Free City of Danzig, and the Memel Autonomous Region, are there any immediate demands? Is it necessary to immediately change the current borders of Europe? (Havas Dispatch, 11th)

Second Meeting of the Locarno Treaty Countries: France's Peace Plan Submitted to the League of Nations for Discussion 40

(Geneva) The second decision-making meeting of the Locarno Treaty countries (Britain, France, Belgium, and Italy) was held here at 3:30 p.m. British representatives included Foreign Secretary Eden and Lord Privy Seal Halifax; French representatives included Foreign Minister Flandin and Minister Without Portfolio Peng Gu; Belgian representatives included Prime Minister Jilange and Director of Political Affairs of the Ministry of Foreign Affairs Su Yilun; and Italian representatives included the Chief Secretary of the Prime Minister's Office Araya West and Director of Political Affairs of the Ministry of Foreign Affairs Rocco. Among them, only the Italian representative attended the meeting as an observer. After the meeting began, French Foreign Minister Flandin first read out the confidential memorandum he had submitted to British Foreign Secretary Eden a few days ago, and then began the discussion. There were two recesses in the middle, so that the representatives of each country could consult with their own experts. The meeting ended at 7:40 p.m. After that, the meeting continued at the office of the British delegation at 9:15 p.m. and adjourned at 11:25 p.m.

The following press release was issued: "The Locarno Treaty countries believe that in order to conclude a new treaty to replace the existing treaty, it is necessary to restore credibility first. Regarding this, if the German government can do its best, the countries concerned can immediately conduct general negotiations so that Article 7 of the draft Locarno Treaty can be implemented. (Article 7 states that the various proposals put forward in the German memorandum of March 7 should be participated in by Germany when negotiations begin in the future, but the proposals for non-aggression treaties with Eastern European countries and Germany's return to the League of Nations are not included in this negotiation. The four countries of Britain, France, Italy, and Belgium should conduct negotiations to conclude mutual assistance treaties to replace the Locarno Treaties, including the agreements to be concluded by the respective general staffs. The new construction of defensive fortifications in the Rhine region should be prohibited or restricted.) Unfortunately, Germany has failed to do so. However, all attempts to reach a compromise must be tried. For this reason, Germany should explain certain points contained in the German memorandum, which the French memorandum requested to be clarified. This should be contacted by the British government with the German government, allowing it to raise questions with Germany on the following two points, namely: What is the scope of the non-aggression treaties proposed by Germany? How can these treaties be compatible with the principles of collective security and mutual assistance stipulated in the League of Nations Covenant? The French representative stated during the meeting on Thursday that if a major change occurs in the current system of the Rhine River during the future negotiations, France reserves the right to take free action on all possible steps, whether collective or unilateral. The Locarno Treaty countries immediately decided that once such a change occurs, the countries should immediately meet to review it. In addition, the signatories decided to submit the French peace plan to the Executive Council of the League of Nations for discussion. As for whether the German plan can be submitted to the Executive Council together, the consent of the German government should be sought," and so on.

The Italian representative reserved the right to decide in the future whether to approve the above resolution. (Havas Dispatch, 10th)

On the German Question: Britain and France Reach a Compromise; Italy Seizes the Opportunity to Make Demands 41

(Geneva) According to this newspaper's diplomatic correspondent, the second Locarno Conference held its meeting today. The discussion was very earnest, and thanks to the mediation of Belgian Prime Minister Janson between British Foreign Secretary Eden and French Foreign Minister Flandin, they were able to reach a harmonious understanding. Four points of compromise were established:

Britain believes that the process of reaching a compromise with Germany is not yet complete. Regarding certain points in the German peace plan, Britain will request explanations from Germany on these points, namely: (A) equal rights, (B) the colonial question, and (C) the excision of the Covenant of the League of Nations from the Treaty of Versailles to become an independent chapter.

Talks between the general staffs of France, Belgium, and Britain will begin on the 15th of this month.

The signatory powers of the Locarno Treaty will hold a third meeting during the regular session of the Council of the League of Nations next month. However, if an unexpected event occurs, the meeting may be convened earlier.

France reiterates that if Germany builds defensive fortifications in the Rhineland region, France reserves the right to take any measures it deems appropriate.

In addition, this newspaper's correspondent has learned that Italian representative Aloisi raised questions to Britain, France, and Belgium on behalf of the Italian government during the afternoon meeting, stating that British Foreign Secretary Eden's repeated declarations never mentioned Italy. Therefore, he urgently wanted clarification as to whether Britain, France, and Belgium genuinely desired Italian participation in the talks. French Foreign Minister Flandin immediately replied that, personally, he hoped for full Italian cooperation and would welcome the Italian government's approval of the draft agreement decided at the Locarno Conference on March 19. Foreign Secretary Eden said that the crux of Aloisi's question did not lie with the British government but entirely with the Italian government. At that point, Aloisi did not leave the meeting, and the meeting continued. (Havas dispatch, 10th)

(Geneva) At yesterday's meeting of the second Locarno Conference, Italian representative Aloisi issued a statement on behalf of the Italian government. The full text of the statement has now been released by the Italian delegation, stating in brief: "Italy was an original signatory and guarantor of the Locarno Treaty. Having made a commitment, it should be respected. However, after Germany abolished this treaty and sent troops into the Rhineland region, the countries involved, one after another, found themselves in special circumstances in London and Paris, and had to adopt a reserved attitude. Unexpectedly, the British government completely ignored Italy. Therefore, the Italian government has instructed its representative to ask: Regarding the reconstruction of Europe, is Italy still needed for cooperation? If Italian cooperation is not necessary, then Italy need not risk danger and bear responsibility for this issue, and should know how to plan for the future." (Havas dispatch, 11th)

(Geneva) Italian representative Aloisi departed for home at 10:15 PM tonight to report the results of the discussions of the Committee of Thirteen and the Locarno Conference to Prime Minister Mussolini. British Foreign Secretary Eden is scheduled to return home tonight. French Foreign Minister Flandin and Cabinet member Peng Gu are scheduled to return home tomorrow. When the Committee of Thirteen meets next Thursday, the French government will be represented by Peng Gu. (Havas dispatch, 10th)

Turkey Requests Restoration of Straits Defenses; Sends Note to Signatories of the Treaty of Lausanne 42

(Paris) Turkish Chargé d'Affaires to France, Durasi, recently sent a note to Foreign Ministry Secretary-General Léger on behalf of the Turkish government, requesting a revision to Article 18 of the 1923 Treaty of Lausanne, namely the clause concerning the demilitarization of the Dardanelles Strait. The note stated that since Germany abolished the Locarno Treaty and sent troops into the Rhineland region, the international situation has changed, and the provisions of Article 18 of the Treaty of Lausanne can no longer be effectively implemented. The Turkish government also sent the same note to the other signatories of the Treaty of Lausanne, namely Britain, Italy, Japan, Bulgaria, Greece, Romania, and Yugoslavia. This move by the Turkish government was already foreshadowed in 1934. (Havas dispatch, 11th)

(Geneva) The Turkish government recently sent a note to the signatories of the Treaty of Lausanne, requesting a revision to Article 18 of the Treaty, namely the clause concerning the demilitarization of the Dardanelles Strait, and sent a copy to League of Nations Secretary-General Avenol. The note stated that the Turkish government is prepared to sign a new agreement in the near future to amend the current system in the Dardanelles Strait, to protect Turkish security and ensure freedom of navigation. (Havas dispatch, 11th)

(Geneva) The Turkish government has also sent a message to the League of Nations, requesting that this matter be included on the agenda of the League of Nations Council meeting beginning on May 11. (Reuters dispatch, 11th)

(London) Regarding the Turkish government's request to re-militarize the Dardanelles Strait, responsible figures recently stated that Britain's previous objections were due to fears that Germany would use it as an excuse. Now that the Turkish government has formally submitted a request to the relevant countries in accordance with legal procedures, it is commendable. Moreover, after Germany unilaterally abolished the Locarno Treaty, this request is fully justified. However, the British government must wait until the Rhineland issue is resolved before discussing this matter. (Havas dispatch, 11th)

(Geneva) Britain and France have significant differences of opinion regarding the Italian-Ethiopian War, causing great anxiety among the smaller nations. Many criticize the attitude of French Foreign Minister Flandin. At yesterday's meeting of the Committee of Thirteen, which considered methods for immediately starting peace negotiations between Italy and Ethiopia, Chairman Madariaga first reported on his discussions with Italian representative Aloisi, stating that the Italian side only said that Italy intended to send a special envoy to Geneva after Easter and requested that Madariaga and League of Nations Secretary-General Avenol visit Rome. British Foreign Secretary Eden then declared that negotiations should begin immediately and should not be delayed by a trip to Rome, and that the Italian government should be asked to send a representative to Geneva as soon as possible. The committee endorsed Eden's proposal. Chairman Madariaga then proposed that the committee should continue to meet in order to ascertain everything, which Eden strongly supported, saying that Geneva would inevitably involve serious issues. Flandin then rose to object, saying that the committee's staying in session might make the negotiations more difficult. After further discussion, the committee decided to adjourn until April 16, so that the chairman would have time to contact the Italian government and know whether there was hope for a successful negotiation. The committee also approved Eden's motion, resolving that the Committee of Eighteen should be prepared to convene at any time, possibly on Friday. (Reuters dispatch, 11th)

(Rome) Today, Italian Prime Minister Mussolini telegraphed General Badoglio, Commander-in-Chief of the Italian forces in East Africa, ordering him to take rapid action on all fronts in Ethiopia. It is believed here that the peace efforts of the League of Nations Committee of Thirteen will soon collapse, and that a critical period in the Italian-Ethiopian conflict is approaching again. Attacks on Britain by the Italian press have also resumed. At the same time, news from the East African front stated that 22 Italian bombers have cleared out the remaining enemy forces between Goran and Taesi, and that the Italian army's advance towards Taesi is now unimpeded. According to eyewitness accounts from pilots, Taesi may have been demilitarized, as many roofs are covered in white cloth. (National Telegram, 10th)

(Rome) According to a telegram from the Commander-in-Chief of the Italian forces in East Africa, 22 Italian aircraft bombed the Ethiopian army positions at Narda Gabo and Sasabana on the southern front yesterday. It is widely believed that this is the prelude to an Italian offensive on the southern front. The telegram also stated that after the Italian air raid, the Italian army occupied positions directly south of Sasabana. (Reuters dispatch, 11th)

Asmara - According to this newspaper's special correspondent, Baal, the Italian army on the northern front has advanced into the city of Gopo, which is located on the main road to Taesi and is of utmost strategic importance. The Ethiopian Emperor, who was previously supervising the troops on the northern front, has fled south since the defeat of his Imperial Guard at Lake Ashangi. It is known that he was stationed in the city of Adio Uda on April 3. At midnight that day, he went to the city of Guaran and arrived there the next morning. After resting there for two hours, he led over a hundred Imperial Guards on mules southward. (Havas dispatch, 11th)

(London) Official sources recently stated that foreign reports that the Ethiopian army has only 5,500 men left since the Battle of Lake Ashangi are completely unfounded. The report that the Ethiopian Emperor has again appealed to the British government for assistance, while alarming, is also without foundation. (Havas dispatch, 11th)

(Rome) The statement by British Admiral Keyes, "The Royal Navy is fully prepared to respond to any action by Mussolini," has aroused extreme dissatisfaction among political figures here, who consider it a most unfriendly expression. The Italian Foreign Ministry mouthpiece, *Il Giornale d'Italia*, published an editorial today targeting this statement, stating in brief: "Italy has never threatened any civilized nation in the world. At the same time, if other countries threaten or provoke us, Italy will use all its naval, land, and air forces to resist them without any hesitation. The Italian expedition to Ethiopia is solely to maintain the safety of its colonies and does not seek to infringe on the interests of other countries. This has been repeatedly stated solemnly by the authorities in recent days and should dispel the doubts of other countries." It is noted that the editor of *Il Giornale d'Italia* was summoned by the Prime Minister yesterday, so this comment can be considered a warning from the Italian government to the British naval authorities. Since the Italian forces in East Africa cleared the Lake Tana area, anti-Italian sentiment among the British has become particularly strong. The attitude of the British representative at the recent meeting of the Committee of Thirteen has also become more assertive, deeply angering Mussolini, who issued a firm statement at the cabinet meeting that "we must annihilate all Ethiopian forces." The Italian delegation was instructed not to participate in the Committee of Thirteen before departing for Geneva. British opinions are becoming increasingly extreme, and the efforts of the Committee of Thirteen will be even more futile. (National Telegram, 10th)

Latvian President Resigns 43

Riga, Latvia - President Kviesis' term expired today. His powers are temporarily exercised by Prime Minister Ulmanis. The successor to the presidency will be elected after the implementation of the constitutional reform plan (announced by the cabinet on May 18, 1934). The term of the President of the Republic of Latvia is three years. Former President Kviesis (leader of the Farmers' Union) was elected in 1930 and re-elected in 1933. (Havas dispatch, 11th)

Special Commercial Dispatch from Reuters, April 11 44

Gold and Silver: London, no market.

Mount Lyell Silver: Futures were quiet and stable this morning. There was slight demand from dealers, so the price rose slightly. The opening price for July was 45.12-45.40, higher than the closing price on Sunday by [unit of currency obscured].

Securities: New York - The securities market opened firm this morning due to speculative buying after yesterday's holiday. Silver and copper stocks were the most popular. Half an hour later, the market softened due to profit-taking. Oil stocks fell below Sunday's closing price. Steel stocks opened up one [unit of currency obscured], but fell 75 [unit of currency obscured] a few minutes later. At 11:00 AM, the market was quiet. Railway and oil stocks softened under selling pressure, while steel stocks became firmer again due to speculative buying. New York securities market prices are listed on the left.

Cotton and Wheat: The New York cotton market is still closed today.

Chicago Wheat: Futures opened firm today, expressing sympathy for the Canadian wheat market. The July price rose one and a half cents from Thursday's closing price to 86.875. Due to general buying pressure, buyers were even more numerous at 11:00 AM. The July price continued to rise 1.25 cents to 87 cents. The feed grain market was also stable. The July price rose 3.75 cents to 99.75.

Rubber: New York rubber also has no market today.

Amidst Reports of a Chinese Trade Surplus with the US; Sino-American Negotiations Continue; American Newspapers Focus on the Chinese Market; Chinese Tung Oil is Selling Well in the US 45

(Washington) The Department of Commerce announced today that, although China's trade situation in February was unfavorable with respect to the world, it had a trade surplus of US$6,627,000 with the United States. China's exports to the US were $9,03,000, while its imports from the US were $2,426,000. In January, China's exports to the US were $8,328,000, while imports were $2,875,000. Financiers here claim that if China can maintain a trade surplus with the US, the current exchange rate between the Chinese currency and the US dollar can be maintained. According to commercial experts, China's trade surplus with the US is largely due to the strong sales of tung oil in the US. As for US trade with Japan, Japan also achieved a trade surplus in February. The total value of US exports to Japan was US$13,215,000, while US imports from Japan were $14,531,000. In January, the total value of US exports to Japan was $18,753,000, while imports were $15,383,000. As for silver imports, their source has changed greatly. In February, imports came entirely from Mexico, Canada, Peru, Soviet Russia, and Chile. Although Britain was previously a major supplier, it now has almost no silver imports to the US. Chen Guangfu, representative of the Chinese banking community, consulted with experts from the Department of the Treasury again today, but did not meet with Treasury Secretary Morgenthau. Guo Bingwen studied tung oil sales with officials from the Department of Commerce. (National Telegram, 10th)

(New York) *The New York Commercial* published an editorial today stating that the US is very concerned about China's new currency system, not only because the US silver purchase policy has greatly affected China, but also because China is an important market for American goods. The Chinese government has also sold a large amount of silver to the US at prices exceeding the world market price, which is sufficient to consolidate the credit of the Chinese currency. Now that the Bank of China has established a branch in New York, it can freely purchase silver dollars here, causing a linked relationship between the Chinese currency and the US dollar. Chinese representatives Chen Guangfu and others are currently negotiating with Treasury Secretary Morgenthau. If this matter is successful, then China will be the first country in the dollar bloc. (National Society Telegram, 10th)

Japanese-Russian Conflict; Both Sides Issue Protests; Japan Transfers the Second Advance Unit to Northern Manchuria 46

(Moscow) On April 10, Soviet Deputy Foreign Minister Stomonyakov received Japanese Ambassador Ota and protested that armed forces from Manchuria had invaded Soviet territory in the Grodekovo area and opened fire on Soviet border guards 1,000 meters inside Soviet territory. This is according to a report from the Khabarovsk Telegraph Agency on April 9. Ota, representing the Japanese government, protested the same incident, saying that the conflict occurred in Manchurian territory and was caused by Soviet border guards firing on Japanese troops. According to Ota's report, three Japanese soldiers died. (TASS dispatch, 11th)

(Moscow) Khabarovsk reports that at 2:30 PM on April 9, five border guards from the Sosnovoye outpost discovered that someone had invaded 1,000 meters into Soviet territory north of Razsipnaye from Manchuria. The number of intruders is unknown. The border guards signaled them to stop, but the intruders opened fire. After a 20-minute exchange, the intruders retreated back into Manchurian territory. (TASS dispatch, 11th)

(Fukuoka) For the sake of guarding northern Manchuria, the Shimizu unit, which received a very enthusiastic send-off, departed for its first assignment yesterday. Now, the Second Advance Regiment, consisting of the Yakiyama, Iizuka, Hattori, and Tajiri units, are following in its wake and are scheduled to depart by ship on the 16th for their assigned posts. At a time when Soviet troops are recklessly committing acts with impunity on the Soviet-Manchurian border and conflicts are frequent, the departure after the First Advance Regiment is under a state of very high alert. Japan's peacetime army plans to increase to 25 divisions. This is the hope of the Ministry of the Army. 47

(Tokyo) Considering the international situation after the Manchurian Incident and the state of military preparations of various powers, there are many who hope to increase the peacetime strength of the Japanese army. Minister of the Army Terauchi is resolved to clearly state this policy at a special session of parliament, indicating the future goals for strengthening the army's armaments. After the European war, various countries around the world, based on their experiences in the war, have been focusing on strengthening their armaments and modern equipment, and are steadily implementing plans. Japan is the only country that is going against this trend, still maintaining the old-fashioned equipment from before the European war. Furthermore, in the first resolution for army reduction in Taisho 10 (1921), five divisions were reduced, and in the second resolution for reorganization in Taisho 14 (1925), three divisions were reduced. The army's peacetime strength plan planned after the European war, the hope for a standing army of 25 divisions, was suppressed and never implemented. It was with the Manchurian Incident as an opportunity that the situation in East Asia changed, and the empire, as a stabilizing force in East Asia, shouldered even greater responsibilities, so the army's arguments were gradually recognized. However, while European and American powers are strengthening their armaments, the equipment of the Japanese army, which is proceeding in the opposite direction, is far inferior to that of European and American countries. Therefore, the proposal to increase to 25 divisions is the unanimous wish of the Ministry of the Army and can be said to have become apparent. Minister of the Army Terauchi will explain in detail the aforementioned historical context in a future speech on strengthening armaments at a special session of parliament, frankly stating the true intentions of the military. The Hindenburg Airship Safely Flies Back to its Home Country; Closely Monitored While Passing Through France 48

Friedrichshafen - The German airship *Hindenburg* safely flew back to its base here after noon today, amidst cheers from 5,000 spectators singing the national anthem. As the airship descended here, Director Eckener leaned out of the window, his face pale and anxious. Those who saw him cheered even louder. Locals were initially concerned about the safety of the crew and 18 passengers after hearing news that one of the airship's engines had been damaged and that it was struggling against the wind off Gibraltar. They were greatly relieved to see it return safely. The French Aviation Ministry granted permission for the airship to pass through French territory on its return journey, but stipulated that the airship must not cross more than ten kilometers beyond the banks of the Rhone River. According to a Reuters correspondent on board the airship, the engine located on the front of the port side malfunctioned on Wednesday evening and was dismantled. As it flew off the French coast, a French airplane circled around the *Hindenburg*. Seeing that its propulsion system was not moving, it knew that its engine was indeed damaged. After the French aircraft returned to the coast, a seaplane also flew in to investigate. Soon after, another plane from Mimes also came to inspect. Captain Lehmann stated that the damaged engine had been repaired, but could only be used in an emergency. This was not the result of poor construction, as such damage is unavoidable when motors are actively tested and new oil is used. (Reuters dispatch, 10th)

(Berlin) The airship *Hindenburg* returned from Brazil, encountering wind and damaging its machinery on the way, forcing it to shorten its journey and pass through France. It safely arrived at Friedrichshafen at 6:40 PM. The round trip between Germany and Brazil took 11 days, covered 21,260 kilometers, the actual flight time was 216 hours, the average speed was 100 kilometers per hour, it passed through 10 countries on three continents, crossed the vast Atlantic Ocean, carrying 73 passengers, 53 crew members, 1,500 kilograms of cargo, 3,000 kilograms of food, and 60,000 kilograms of fuel. The airship itself weighed 112,000 kilograms. The journey from Germany to Brazil was smooth, but on the return journey, it suddenly encountered a storm off the coast of Africa, damaging one of the four engines it was equipped with. Although the ship's engineer immediately repaired it, it was never used. Captain Lehmann stated that this misfortune was not unusual, and that the advantages of the new diesel heavy oil engine were not diminished by it. All of the engines started and ran continuously for 330 hours, which shows their durability. As for the economy of fuel, it was also amazing. The two trips covered more than 21,000 kilometers, and the fuel consumed was less than 40,000 liters. On the return journey, some passengers requested to fly over the Alps, but I refused the request because the wind direction and weather conditions there at that time were unfavorable for flight. As for requesting permission from the French authorities to pass through their airspace, it was due to the engine damage and weather conditions. After we entered French territory, we followed the Rhone River, passing through the cities of Bourg-en-Bresse, Besançon, and Basel in Switzerland, before returning here. I am very satisfied with this trip, and I hope that all the passengers are also satisfied. (Havas dispatch, 10th)

Alps Tunnel to be Excavated, Committee to be Established by France, Italy, and Switzerland

(Paris) Mont Blanc in the Alps is the highest peak in Europe, located at the intersection of France, Italy, and Switzerland. Until now, there has been no tunnel, and travelers must detour, which is quite inconvenient. It has recently been learned that people from France, Italy, and Switzerland have jointly established a committee to plan the excavation of a tunnel, which will begin this summer. According to the "Industry Daily" magazine, the three-country committee sent geological experts to the vicinity of Mont Blanc to conduct on-site investigations and compile a report for review. It is understood that construction there is not difficult. There are no hot springs in the granite rock walls to hinder construction. The northern entrance of the tunnel is in Chamonix, France, at an altitude of 1,035 meters. The southern entrance is two kilometers away from Entreves, at an altitude of 1,305 meters. The total length of the tunnel is 12 kilometers and 600 meters, with a width of eight meters. After completion, cars can pass through. However, when cars are driving, they emit a lot of carbon gas. If there is no equipment for circulating air, this carbon gas will fill the tunnel and harm travelers. This problem can also be solved by excavating a small tunnel below the tunnel to transport fresh air and discharge turbid air. Carbon gas detectors will also be installed in the large tunnel. If the carbon gas content is too high and affects breathing, these detectors will automatically detect it. Then the alarm bell will ring, so that the management personnel can open the fresh air circulation mechanism to achieve a regulating effect. Also, an exit will be set every 200 meters, so that cars in the tunnel can drive to a passageway filled with fresh air. As for the problems of regulating light and setting up traffic signals, they will also be solved by scientific methods. Therefore, cars do not need to turn on lights when driving in the tunnel. The signals are all lit with lights to direct traffic. As for the funding, at the beginning of the construction, two-thirds of the basic funds will be borne by French banking groups. This amount can be repaid in installments over 50 years. It is estimated that after the tunnel is completed, a toll can be charged according to the weight of the car and the number of people carried, and it is expected that at least 120,000 cars will pass through each year. (11th Havas Dispatch)

Peiping, Incident of Two Newspapers Being Destroyed 67

Resolved After Mediation and Earnest Discussion, Muslims Will Celebrate with the Press

Peiping Correspondence, On the 5th and 6th of this month, the Peiping World Evening News and Citizen News successively reprinted a correspondence about Xinjiang customs titled "Hami Produces Beautiful Women". Local Muslims believed that it insulted the Islamic faith. On the 7th, they sent letters to the two newspapers, issuing a warning. The World Evening News immediately corrected the article on the 7th according to the publication law. However, the Citizen News did not receive the letter and was therefore unable to respond. As a result, on the morning of the 8th, at around 9:00 AM, members of the Muslim community gathered at the Qingzhen Mosque in Tianqiao. It was raining lightly, and the Muslims gathered in the rain to reach more than 300 people. They marched in formation to Xuanwu Gate and then to the Citizen News office at No. 7 Xianglai Street, where they carried out the destruction. All 24 rooms of the building were completely destroyed. The printing presses, lead type, and equipment in all departments were also completely ruined. At 12:30 PM, they went to the World Evening News on West Chang'an Street to carry out the destruction. At around 1:00 PM, because the goal had been achieved, they dispersed.

The losses suffered by the two newspapers were astonishing because there was no preparation in advance and no resistance. In addition to the fact that the Citizen News was temporarily unable to resume publication, the World Evening News was able to continue publishing because the printing factory was fortunately not affected. At the time, the attitude of the authorities of the two newspapers was very cautious and unwilling to make any statement. However, the local authorities were fair in their handling of the matter, but paid close attention to the issue of responsibility for the incident. When the Muslims departed from Tianqiao, the two newspapers telegraphed the Second District Police Department to send police to protect them. As a result, the director of the department, Zhu Dezhi, only sent three policemen to the scene, which made it impossible to prevent the unfortunate incident. The authorities also attached great importance to this point because it concerned public security and stated that they would thoroughly investigate it as a warning to those who neglected their duties. As of now, one patrol officer has been dismissed.

After the two newspapers were destroyed, the Muslims established a temporary joint association of various Muslim organizations at the West Temple in Niujie at around 2:00 PM that afternoon as an agency dedicated to dealing with this incident. On the morning of the 9th, they held an emergency meeting and passed six resolutions, including requesting the authorities to ban the recurrence of similar incidents in various newspapers and demanding compensation for reputational damage of 140,000 yuan (calculated at one yuan per person for the 140,000 Muslims in Peiping). At around 1:00 PM on the same afternoon, they gathered in front of Tiananmen Square, preparing to go to the Hebei-Chahar Political Committee and the Peiping Municipal Government to petition for protection. Fearing that the situation would escalate, the authorities immediately ordered Ma Yulin, the captain of the Detective Brigade, to rush to persuade them, promising to discuss the matter in the long term. The Muslims then dispersed and waited for a solution. That night at 8:00 PM, the Municipal Government sent Commissioner Wu Lengzhai, together with Qian Zongchao, the Chief Inspector of the Public Security Bureau, Ma Yulin, the Captain of the Detective Brigade, and Guan Yixian, the representative of the Journalists Association, to meet with Muslim representatives at the Northwest Middle School. After earnest discussions, a mediation plan was decided. The authorities instructed that the measures of the Five Races and One Family promulgated by the Central Government should be followed, and Muslims should not be discriminated against. A circular was issued to all newspapers stating that there should be no more insulting words about Islam.

Both sides agreed not to pursue each other's losses. The two newspapers published notices apologizing to the Muslims. The two newspapers punished those responsible. After the above plan was agreed upon, the mediator informed the two newspapers. The Citizen News, because it was still in suspension, decided to comply when it resumed publication. The World Evening News received a reply from its president, Cheng Shewo, in Shanghai after sending a telegram and published a notice in its evening newspaper on the 10th. The original text stated, "This newspaper published an article titled "Hami Produces Beautiful Women" on April 5th. It was done in haste and without careful review. After it was discovered by Muslims, they believed that it was inconsistent with the facts. Islam is the largest religion in the world, and its teachings are peaceful and its beliefs are pure. It attaches great importance to ethics and morality, and ethnic equality and freedom of religion are enshrined in the Provisional Constitution. In the 21st year of the Republic of China, the National Government reiterated the ban, strictly prohibiting discrimination against any religion. Due to a temporary oversight, this unfortunate incident occurred. This newspaper has always respected laws and regulations, and respects and admires Islam. In addition to punishing those responsible, it is necessary to correct the error and sincerely apologize to all Muslims. We hope for your understanding."

The Peiping Municipal Authorities instructed the Public Security Bureau on the same afternoon to assist and instruct all newspapers to earnestly respect religions, not to harbor any discrimination, and not to arbitrarily belittle them. The original order stated, "Ethnic equality and freedom of religion are enshrined in the law. The government has always respected, supported, and protected all ethnic groups and religions in the country, and the Executive Yuan has issued a circular to this effect. However, it has been found that various newspapers have recently reprinted articles related to Islam, which were either carelessly reviewed or were close to insulting, affecting local order. It is hereby ordered that the bureau be directed to instruct all newspapers to strictly abide by the circulars and resolutions of the Executive Yuan, not to discriminate against any religion, and not to arbitrarily belittle them. This order is of utmost importance."

Therefore, the incident between the Muslims and the two newspapers was completely resolved. The World Evening News is currently working hard to handle the aftermath. On the Muslim side, it is planned to host a gathering for the press in the city next week to remove past grievances and restore good relations. (April 10th)

Rice Prices in Guangdong and Guangxi Still Rising 68

Guangdong Expedites Construction of Warehouses Everywhere, Guangxi Levies Export Duties on Rice

Guangzhou Correspondence, Recently, in Guangdong and Guangxi provinces, due to the period between the exhaustion of old crops and the ripening of new crops, the demand for rice and grain exceeds the supply. Merchants in various places have been purchasing them one after another to hoard and speculate. Therefore, the two provinces have prohibited the export of rice and grain for the past month to maintain the people's food supply. In order to regulate the supply of rice and grain, Guangdong Province has implemented a reduction of one-fourth of the import tariff rate on foreign rice to compensate for the high price of foreign rice due to the rising foreign exchange rate. Also, the Provincial Food Regulation Association, considering the shortage of rice and grain in the interior and to prevent famine, has requested the authorities to order the counties and cities to expedite the storage of grain for famine relief and to submit a statement on building general warehouses everywhere for hoarding grain. After receiving the statement, the provincial government has forwarded the case to the relevant agencies for review. On the 1st of this month, the provincial government resolved to allocate 150,000 yuan from the provincial treasury to build three major grain storage warehouses in Xingning and Yangyang in the East River and Qujiang in the North River. Each warehouse will cost 50,000 yuan and will be constructed within a month. It is heard that eight grain storage sub-warehouses will be established in various counties. The locations for establishing the sub-warehouses have been selected as Wengyuan, Yingde, Nanhai, Zengcheng, Maoming, Qinzhou, Haifeng, Huiyang, and other eight counties. If the counties cannot raise the funds to build the sub-warehouses in time, the Food Association will provide subsidies as appropriate to ensure that they are fully established within three months.

Guangxi Province, which was originally a surplus rice area, has unexpectedly experienced a phenomenon of rising rice prices since the beginning of spring. It is heard that this is due to unscrupulous merchants purchasing and hoarding. Wuzhou Port implemented a ban on rice exports at seven yuan per unit last month. Recently, it has risen to ten yuan per hundred catties, and the livelihood of the poor people is becoming more and more difficult. At present, the Guilin Chamber of Commerce and the local defense army commander have discussed relief measures. It is heard that it is planned to release 150,000 stones of rice stored in the Guilin granary and hold a fair distribution to benefit the people's livelihood. At the same time, the Guilin County Government has strictly controlled the export of grain and rice. The Guangxi Provincial Government has recently received reports of high rice prices from various places and has implemented the collection of export duties on rice to prohibit exports through taxation. Yesterday, it ordered the Guangxi Taxation Bureau to comply. After receiving the order, the bureau issued a notice at the beginning of the month to start collecting taxes. The notice stated, "According to the telegram from the Provincial Government, it was reported that rice prices in Cangwu, Guilin, Wuxuan, He County, Xindu, and other counties were soaring and requesting a ban on rice exports. The Wuzhou Taxation Bureau was instructed to investigate and found that the export of white rice has accounted for one-third compared with last year, brown rice accounted for one-fourth, and rice accounted for one-sixth. White rice is mostly exported, which is because it is currently the peak month and there are more foreign sales. The export is not indicative of famine. In order to prohibit exports through taxation, it has been verified that the export of brown rice and rice will be subject to a tax of five cents for every hundred city catties, except for white rice, which will continue to be exempt from export duties to show restriction. You should immediately comply with the notification to the public and instruct your subordinates to comply with the report." (April 5th)

Yangzhou: Concerns Over the Melon Causeway Lead to a Petition from Dike Residents 74

Resolution: The meeting is scheduled to be held on May 15th. The second district of the county mostly borders the Yangtze River. During the great flood of the 20th year of the Republic, the dikes of Guazhou and Six Dikes nearby were destroyed, causing the collapse of many dike fields. Subsequently, in the 21st year of the Republic, officials and civilians cooperated to shorten the dike by more than 100 feet and build a new bank to protect the undamaged fields. Unexpectedly, recently, the new embankment in the Guadong area has once again approached the collapsed area. Moreover, the current year's river water is flowing with great force, and there is a risk of further collapse. The district head of the area, Zang Liuqi, learning from the past experience of the 20th year of the Republic, requested the county government to appoint Xu Kuan-yu, Liu Shi-zong, Chen Yu-shu, and others, the township heads of the collapsed sections, as the chief and deputy directors in charge of preparing for repairs and defenses. However, the project is difficult and requires huge sums of money, which cannot be completed in a short time by a small number of people. Therefore, the chief and deputy directors have been unable to come up with a solution. Local people such as Liu Changchun and Ma Yunqing have stated that the peach flood is approaching soon. If work is not started quickly before the busy farming season arrives, the tragedy of the past will be repeated this year. It is said that these people have repeatedly jointly petitioned the county government and plan to send representatives to the city to appeal, hoping to build a new bank as soon as possible to avoid an irreversible collapse. It is reported that the county government is also paying special attention to this matter and has ordered the Construction Bureau to send personnel to Guadong and the Ji Jia Port area to conduct on-site surveys.
