Artistic Musings

Thousands of Willows Outside the Red Railing Bridge (Part 2)

— Feng Zikai

Green symbolizes peace. Therefore, green flags are used at train stations to signal that trains are allowed to proceed, and green lights are used on roads to indicate that vehicles are allowed to move forward. Although these are man-made symbols, their selection is not without natural basis. Imagine if red and green were replaced with two other colors, such as yellow and purple, or blue and orange, they would be far less natural than red and green, and would be more difficult to remember. Drivers might cause accidents due to misidentification. Only the two colors, red and green, are natural and easy to remember. Drivers can intuitively feel the situation ahead from the colors of the lights, without having to memorize the meaning of these symbols. The human eyes and body's senses are cleverly interconnected. When the color red enters the eyes, the body's senses naturally become tense. When the color green enters the eyes, the body's senses naturally become relaxed. It is certainly possible to force oneself to appear calm when seeing red, or to force oneself to appear tense when seeing green; however, it is not human nature. Moving further from peace, green also symbolizes love. Therefore, postmen who deliver messages wear green uniforms. Esperanto scholars use the color green, which symbolizes peace and love, as their symbol. These are all very meaningful stipulations. Generally speaking, humanity's understanding of the symbolic power of green began with natural objects. Like today, on a sunny spring day, the grass and trees are thriving, the mountains and fields are covered in new greenery, and people's hearts are most joyful. Imagine in a few months, the green trees are dense, covering the sky and earth, the mountains and fields are filled with natural green lawns and curtains, and people's hearts are most comfortable. Therefore, all qualities such as joy, harmony, peace, love, nature, and comfort can be associated with the colors of nature. In short, green is a symbol of tranquility.

Red and green together create a sense of beauty, as can be deduced from the various examples and symbolic powers mentioned above. Red symbolizes vitality, and green symbolizes tranquility. Being both vibrant and tranquil is the most ideal life. Since ancient times, people in prosperous times have had these two emotions saturated and blended in their hearts. The colors of the current "Thousands of Willows Outside the Red Railing Bridge" are precisely a symbol of a prosperous time.

This can also be explained from the perspective of color theory: All colors in the world are created by variations of red, yellow, and blue. Therefore, red, yellow, and blue are called the "three primary colors." Each of the three primary colors has its own characteristics: red is passionate, yellow is solemn, and blue is serene. When two primary colors are combined, they become "three secondary colors," that is, red and yellow become orange, red and blue become purple, and yellow and blue become green. The three secondary colors also each have their own characteristics: orange is passionate plus solemn, that is, sacred; purple is passionate plus serene, that is, noble; green is solemn plus serene, that is, peaceful. By repeatedly combining them, countless colors with countless characteristics can be produced. Now, when red and green are combined, in other words, red is combined with yellow and blue. In contrast, all three primary colors are present, in other words, all colors in the world are included. Therefore, when it enters the eyes, the sensation is saturated and complete, without any deficiency. It can be seen that the reason why the contrast between red and green makes people feel satisfied is fundamentally due to the presence of all three primary colors. However, the contrast of all three primary colors is not limited to the combination of red and green alone. Yellow and purple (red and blue), blue and orange (red and yellow), are also combinations of all three primary colors. Why is the combination of red and green particularly satisfying? This is due to the different characteristics of the three primary colors. Colors are divided into two categories, yin and yang, with red being the leader of yang; colors are divided into two categories, light and dark, with red being the leader of light; colors are divided into two categories, warm and cold, with red being the leader of warm. Yang is stronger than yin, light is stronger than dark, and warm is stronger than cold. Therefore, red is the strongest of the three primary colors, stronger than yellow, and yellow is stronger than blue. Therefore, using the combined force of yellow and blue (green) to contrast red is the most evenly matched. Red and blue (purple) against yellow is not as balanced. Red and yellow (orange) against blue is even less balanced. From their symbolism, this principle can also be understood: passion, solemnity, and serenity, in terms of the needs of human emotion, also form a diminishing difference. Passion is first, solemnity is second, and serenity is last. Those who emphasize serenity lose their gentleness, and those who emphasize solemnity lose their strength. Only those who emphasize passion can achieve the correctness of yin and yang, strength and gentleness, and meet the needs of human vigor, suitable for the mood of a vibrant person. Therefore, simple primitive people like red and green; innocent children like red and green; people celebrating like red and green; and I, wandering along the West Lake, basking in the warm sun and gentle breeze, forgetting the worries of the times, also like the saturation of the colors of "Thousands of Willows Outside the Red Railing Bridge," and therefore temporarily experience the happy mood of the people in a prosperous age.

Unfortunately, these thousands of willows will soon wither and decline. I fear that in the future, when spring returns to summer, and the autumn air is bleak, the peaceful green will disappear, leaving only the insurance-like color of the red railing bridge dominating the natural world, and running rampant in the gray environment. However, at that time, no one will come to the West Lake to admire the scenery, and I will no longer wander here. March 18, Year 15 [of the Republic].

Page 10

Local News

Finance Minister Kong Discusses the Success of Monetary Policy: Stable Foreign Exchange, Increased Exports, and Active Industry and Commerce; Maintaining the Credit of Legal Tender and Paying Attention to National Production 79

Xin Xin News Agency reports: Kong Xiangxi, Vice President of the Executive Yuan and Minister of Finance, received a reporter from Xin Xin News Agency yesterday afternoon at 6:30 p.m. at the Central Bank and made the following important statements:

Effectiveness of Monetary Policy

It has been half a year since the implementation of the new monetary policy. Fortunately, with the support of the people, it has been very effective, which is gratifying. Recently, foreign exchange has stabilized, export trade has increased significantly, and domestic industry and commerce have gradually become active due to the easing of credit. In the future, the government should follow the established guidelines and implement them effectively, so that the country's finances and social economy will become more stable.

Establishing County and Township Banks

After the implementation of the legal tender policy, the Central Bank system is currently undergoing legislative procedures. The Central Reserve Bank will soon be established. The Ministry of Finance is currently drafting commercial and local banking laws and plans to establish county and township banks. In the future, the Ministry of Finance and the people will jointly organize these banks, so that the government and the people can work together to fully promote the great effect of promoting national economic development.

Organizing Financial Plans

As for organizing financial plans, preparations have also been completed. The most important thing is to seek a balance in the national budget. The total budget for the next fiscal year should still be based on the total expenditure for this fiscal year in order to achieve a balance between income and expenditure, maintain the credit of legal tender, pay attention to the development of national production, determine an economic policy of self-reliance and regeneration, and put the country on the path to prosperity. It is hoped that the people will all base themselves on patriotism and give the government sincere and close cooperation. The revival of the nation depends on this.

Farmers, workers, merchants, and young students all went astray. The survival of the Party and the country was at stake. Shanghai was a place where Chinese and foreigners lived together, making reconnaissance difficult. The Red bandits, who had lost their minds, often used this as a hiding place, creating elements of rebellion. During this period, I was responsible for punishing the wicked and maintaining law and order. I dared not but work hard to thoroughly purge them. However, my personal abilities are limited, and I still rely on the help of all sectors. I also hope that the press will express their great opinions from time to time and be generous in their teachings, so that I can achieve the goal of protecting the Party and the people.

Silk Manufacturers in Jiangsu and Zhejiang Provinces Discuss Borrowing Large Sums to Purchase Cocoons: An Amount of 20 Million Yuan, Guaranteed by the Purchased Cocoons; Bank Meeting Decides on Principles and Agrees 81

In order to purchase spring cocoons, silk factories in Jiangsu and Zhejiang provinces have jointly discussed borrowing large sums of money from banks such as the Bank of China and the Bank of Communications. Banks have expressed their agreement in principle. The silk factories have scheduled a joint meeting for 4 p.m. today at the Shanghai Silk Cocoon Association on North Shaanxi Road to discuss the number of cocoons each factory needs to purchase and the amount of money they need to borrow. Then, they will continue to contact the banks for further negotiations. The details are as follows:

No Extension Allowed

The Zhejiang Silk Control Committee's interim measures for the control and management of cocoon collection for the spring of the 25th year have been announced and implemented. The regulations are quite strict. All silk factory merchants inside and outside the province who purchase improved cocoons and local cocoons in the cocoon-producing areas of Zhejiang Province must apply to the committee for registration before April 15th. Otherwise, they will be refused to purchase in Zhejiang Province. The silk factory associations of Zhejiang, Shanghai, and Wuxi believe that the committee's restrictions are too strict and the deadline is too short, and the procedures for raising funds are not enough to handle. They jointly applied for an extension of the deadline, but yesterday the committee issued a decision not to allow it. It was decided that the registration deadline would be April 15th, and no further extension would be granted.

Joint Borrowing

Silk manufacturers in Jiangsu and Zhejiang provinces have generally borrowed money from banks to purchase cocoons in previous years, or the banks have automatically purchased them and resold them to the silk manufacturers. This spring, the silk factories have decided to jointly borrow from banks and have already started negotiations. According to Chu Hui-seng, a leader of the silk cocoon merchants, the silk manufacturers in Jiangsu and Zhejiang provinces have jointly borrowed a large sum of money from banks such as the Bank of China and the Bank of Communications. Representatives have been sent to contact Song Hanzhang, General Manager of the Bank of China, and Tang Shoumin, General Manager of the Bank of Communications, several times. The amount of the loan ranges from 15 million to 20 million yuan. According to past practice, the purchased cocoons are used as collateral. The Bank of China, the Bank of Communications, and other banks held a joint meeting on the 8th of this month. As a result of the discussion, they decided to accept the principle of the loan. The exact amount and all other methods are still to be decided. It is generally hoped that it will be successful.

Meeting Today

The silk factory trade associations of Shanghai, Zhejiang, and Wuxi have scheduled a joint meeting for 4 p.m. today at the Shanghai Silk Factory Trade Association on North Shaanxi Road. At that time, in addition to discussing important proposals such as the joint cocoon collection this spring, the method of allocating the large sums borrowed from the Shanghai banking community will also be discussed. The number of cocoons needed by each member silk factory of the three associations will be reported at today's meeting for reference.

Sino-French International Trade Has Greatly Developed Recently 82

Translated by the Foreign Press Agency from the French Chamber of Commerce Monthly in China: According to the French Commercial Counselor's Office, trade between China and France has greatly developed in recent years, and the future prospects are even better. Since the beginning of trade between China and France, China has always been in a surplus position, which is extremely beneficial to China. According to French statistics for 1935, Chinese goods imported into France amounted to 141 million francs per year, ranking 27th in the French import list. According to French statistics for 1935, French goods imported into China amounted to 88 million francs per year, ranking 22nd in the French export list. According to the French business authorities, there are four reasons why commercial measurement between China and France has failed to be developed: 1. Chinese and French goods are not essential goods in the eyes of both parties, so they cannot arouse the desire to purchase. 2. China and France are too far apart. 3. Chinese and French merchants lack in-depth research on the needs of each other's markets. 4. There are too many privately manufactured counterfeit goods in China and France, which cannot gain market credibility. According to the statistics of the Chinese Customs in 1935, trade between China and France in 1935 was indeed an increase compared to 1934, and China was still in a favorable position. The following table clarifies: (Gold Units)

From its total, the trade between China and France in 1935 was really an increase compared to 1934, and the most notable point is that the number of Chinese goods transported to France increased and the number of French goods transported to China decreased. From this, it can be seen that the purchasing power of the Chinese people has been greatly reduced. As for the trade between China and the French colonies, China is once again a country that has been surpassed, but this is true only in the case of Indochina, while the other French colonies are different. Wang Zhengting Discusses筹赎 Redemption of the Jiaoji Railway 83

Also Discusses Sino-Japanese Relations and the Soviet-Mongolian Agreement

Xinsheng News Agency reports that Wang Zhengting, Chairman of the Foreign Affairs Committee of the Central Government, recently went to Nanjing to negotiate the redemption of the Jiaoji Railway. After returning to Shanghai the day before yesterday, he received a reporter from the Xinsheng News Agency at his residence yesterday morning. He discussed the progress of the redemption of the Jiaoji Railway and his observations on the Sino-Japanese situation. The details are as follows:

Jiaoji Railway Expires Next Year

Wang said in response to a reporter's question that, regarding the redemption of the Jiaoji Railway, after the Washington Conference, the Shandong Case Committee decided to use public debt and roadbed as collateral to Japan. After five years to fifteen years, 40 million would be used to redeem it from Japan. This year is the fourteenth year, and next year is the expiration date. It should be redeemed, so I have come forward to prepare for it. I am currently discussing the redemption funds with the railway and finance departments. Japan originally bought this road from Germany. Since the Shandong Conference to date, in the past thirteen years, it has earned a surplus of more than 20 million. The operating situation can be said to be not bad.

Sino-Japanese War Imminent

The reporter then asked Wang about his observations on the Sino-Japanese pseudo "Man" Mongolian border dispute. Wang said that this area has become a point of contention between China and Japan, and it can even be said that it is where the Sino-Japanese War will break out. The pseudo-Mongolian border stretches for more than a thousand miles. Whoever occupies it will gain an advantage, naturally forming a must-contested area. At present, both sides have stationed heavy troops there, and the situation is very tense. A major war is very likely to break out.

Soviet-Mongolian Agreement to be Submitted to the League of Nations

Wang continued, "This decision by the Soviet Union and Outer Mongolia to sign a mutual assistance agreement ignores our country's sovereignty. Our foreign affairs authorities are continuing to protest to the Soviet Union. Some advocate that our country can appeal to the League of Nations. In principle, this is not impossible. However, we are still protesting at the moment. If it is deemed necessary in the future, we can submit it to the League of Nations. The League of Nations is originally a peacemaker for all countries. When there are disputes, as a last resort, we can only appeal to the League of Nations. But whether the League of Nations is powerful is another question."

Wang Denies He Will Be Sent to Soviet Russia

It was previously rumored that Ambassador Yan Huiqing to the Soviet Union will return to China in the future. Because of his old age, he is not suitable for living in cold regions for a long time, and he intends to retire. Wang Zhengting will succeed him. The reporter specifically asked Wang about this. He replied, "I have not heard of this. I only know that Ambassador Yan will return to China because Foreign Minister Zhang is newly appointed and needs to be consulted or reported to. Therefore, he will definitely return to China."

Regulations of the Antiquities Preservation Association: Procedures for Exporting Antiquities: Shippers Must Apply for an Export Permit, and the Ministry of Finance Will Order the Customs to Inspect and Release

The Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce previously received a letter from the Antique Industry Association stating that the Jianghai Customs Notice Department's order on restricting the export of antiquities did not have specific standards. It requested that the government authorities conduct a detailed review and formulate standards. After submitting the matter to the government, the Ministry of Finance issued an instruction stating: "The matter has been presented and referred to the Ministry of Interior for review and discussion, and then sent to the Ministry for compliance." Later, it was approved by the Ministry of Interior on March 23, Year 25, with the reply that when the Executive Yuan issued the aforementioned outline, it ordered the Central Antiquities Preservation Committee to formulate detailed rules and submit them to the Executive Yuan for approval and promulgation. At present, these detailed rules have not yet been drafted, and the committee has been ordered to conduct detailed research and formulate standards for reply, so that they can be transferred and complied with. It has also been ordered to comply with the previous order of the Executive Yuan to quickly draft the aforementioned outline details and submit them to the Ministry for review, approval, and implementation. According to the committee's report on March 13, Year 25, it was submitted to the 12th Regular Meeting of the committee for detailed discussion. It was unanimously agreed that there are many types of antiquities in the country, which are too numerous to list. China is a country with 5,000 years of cultural development. All things left by our ancestors, such as broken bricks and short slips of bamboo, contain historical, scientific, or artistic value and are worth preserving. Therefore, it is necessary to examine the value of antiquities, regardless of whether they are works of art or modern products, and only after confirming that they meet the principles suitable for preservation should they be restricted from leaving the country to avoid loss. Moreover, China has a unique abundance of buried antiquities, which are often discovered. The art of imitation has gradually improved over the years. If antiquities leaving the country are not clearly identified one by one, there is a great concern that misrepresentation will increase and restrictions will become mere formalities. The outline of the scope and types of antiquities that the committee previously submitted for approval and promulgation was originally intended to be general in order to avoid omissions and prevent abuses. If specific standards are formulated only within the current scope of research, it will still be difficult to be comprehensive and applicable. As a result of the deliberation, it is proposed to waive the drafting. However, for the convenience of merchants, in the future, those who wish to transport antiquities from all over the country out of the country should first submit them to the committee for appraisal by experts or academic institutions before shipment and issue a certificate of permission to leave the country. At the same time, the committee will inform the Ministry of Finance to order the customs to inspect and release them so that both customs and merchants can slightly reduce difficulties in procedures. This will not lose the purpose of preservation while considering the business situation. As for the details of antiquities, the committee is inviting experts to study and draft them. In addition to waiting for the details and the rules for the implementation of the certificate of permission to leave the country, they will be submitted for review and promulgation separately. Before receiving the order, the reasons are presented in writing, and it is hoped that they will be reviewed and instructed, etc." Accordingly, the notification is hereby given for reference and compliance. This approval.

法租界公董局 撤銷烟號增捐 85

According to New News Agency, more than ten Qing Tiao Pi Si tobacco shops in the French Concession's New Kai He area, including Xinfutai, Yongshengrui, Xiehesheng, Yilinfeng, Sutai Xiang, Lindasen, Linsanhe, Gonghexiang, Sudekang, and Tongxingtai, were suddenly subjected to an additional "Categorized Business Hygiene Fee" of ten yuan per month by the French Concession Public Works Bureau's Donation Office, on top of the tobacco tax. This was deemed an unbearable burden. Therefore, they jointly sent a letter to the Taxpayers' Association to negotiate for its cancellation. After the association lodged a protest, a satisfactory resolution was reached. Details are as follows:

Increased Tax Repercussions

The Qing Tiao Pi Si tobacco shops specialize in selling Lanzhou Qing Tiao and Fujian Pi Si tobacco. In the past, their business was quite good, with annual transactions exceeding one million. However, with the popularity of cigarettes, the industry has suffered a major blow, and sales have been declining daily. In addition to paying the tobacco tax to the French Public Works Bureau, there are no other taxes. Unexpectedly, last month, the French Public Works Bureau's Donation Office suddenly sent personnel to collect a "Categorized Business Hygiene Fee" of ten yuan per month, with penalties for violations. The businesses in the industry believed that with the current sluggish business, it would be impossible to bear the additional burden. They jointly sent a letter to the Chinese Taxpayers' Association of the French Concession to negotiate with the Public Works Bureau to cancel this exorbitant tax, to alleviate the burden and benefit commerce.

Negotiation Process

After receiving the letter, the association immediately sent personnel to investigate and confirmed the situation. They immediately sent a letter to the Public Works Bureau to express their opposition. Furthermore, the association's secretary, Zhang Shishi, met with Mr. Blandin, the acting director of the Public Works Bureau, and explained that these businesses only sell tobacco and do not sell other goods. The additional "Categorized Business Hygiene Fee" seemed unreasonable and unwarranted, and should be quickly cancelled to reduce the burden on merchants and residents and promote the restoration of prosperity within the concession. Mr. Blandin agreed to investigate and respond later.

Satisfactory Resolution

Mr. Blandin, the acting director of the French Public Works Bureau, replied to the Taxpayers' Association in a letter yesterday, stating, "Having read your letter of March 23, we understand the matter. On the 7th of this month, your association's secretary came to the bureau for discussion. It has been verified that ten Qing Tiao and water pipe tobacco shops, including Xinfutai, are still only required to pay the tobacco tax each month and do not need to pay for a categorized business license, as these shops only sell Qing Tiao and Pi Si tobacco used for water pipes. As for tobacco shops that retail tobacco used for cigarettes, they are not included in this exemption and are still required to pay ten yuan per month." After receiving the letter, the association immediately forwarded it to the respective shops for their information.

Tan Dingfen Returns to China After Completing Studies, Invents a Lightweight Wireless Electrical Machine 86

Mr. Tan Dingfen, who recently returned to China after completing his studies in Europe, went to the United States several years ago to study at the Department of Electrical Engineering at the University of Chicago, where he devoted himself to studying wireless electricity and gained considerable insights. Two years ago, he transferred to England and interned at the Marconi Wireless Telegraph Company. He recently returned to China due to personal matters and originally planned to go to France and Belgium for further studies. However, the government is recruiting talent for the telecommunications administration and has already appointed him, so his intention to go abroad has been cancelled. Mr. Tan suffered from a minor illness on his way back to China due to exhaustion. After arriving in Shanghai, he was admitted to the hospital for rest. After two weeks, he was discharged from the hospital and immediately went to Beijing. Before taking office, he also plans to visit various parts of the country to investigate the telecommunications administration. According to Mr. Tan, speaking to a Central News Agency reporter yesterday, he had invented a lightweight wireless electrical machine in England, based on his experience, that can simultaneously send and receive telegrams and broadcasts, making it ideal for use on ships and vehicles. He has already assembled one machine and will take it to Beijing for field testing. Mr. Tan has also written two books, "Experiments in Wireless Electricity" and "Internal Combustion Engines," which will be published soon and contain rich content.

Nine Shipping Companies Seek to Salvage Far East-Europe Maritime Transport, British Ships Account for the Largest Share of the Pooling Ratio, American Ships the Least 88

(Special Report by This Newspaper) The economic recession in recent years has shaken the entire world, especially in China, where the "September 18th" and "January 28th" incidents have led to commercial decline, rural bankruptcy, increased unemployment, and reduced industrial and commercial production, all reflecting the exhaustion of social finance and revealing the bottom layer of economic depression. This is truly the reality of China today amidst the global recession.

Shanghai is the leading commercial port in the Far East, the hub of China's land and water transportation, and the only large market for countries around the world to sell their goods. Counting ships from the East and West, at least four to five hundred ships arrive at Wusong and enter the Huangpu River each month, not including those sailing on inland waterways. The volume of foreign goods imported each year is imaginable. However, the value of imports has also decreased sharply in the past three years, especially last year and this year, when foreign imports plummeted. This year, China has surprisingly broken the record for trade surplus, something that has not been seen in over sixty years. Is this a good phenomenon? No, it reflects the lack of purchasing power in our country. The decrease in imports is truly due to the sluggish market.

The fact that China's exports can exceed imports is theoretically a good phenomenon, but a detailed examination of the customs report shows that the amount is still less than the amount during the months with an import surplus in previous years. The overall decline in imports has directly affected major shipping companies. In recent years, shipping companies operating on ocean and foreign routes, whether European or American, have been losing money in 99% of cases. If they can maintain expenses, it is already considered rare. Therefore, the Blue Star Line ships in the Far East were the first to suspend operations, and the E-Tai-Gelden Line, which had been operating for decades and had deep roots, was also merged into the Blue Funnel Line.

The overall decline in shipping has caused great alarm among European shipping merchants in the Far East. At first, they used competitive methods, such as secretly offering rebates, as conditions for carrying more goods. However, these actions were always irregular and disruptive, and China's exports were decreasing day by day. As a result, shipping merchants from England, France, Japan, the United States, Italy, Germany, the Netherlands, Norway, and Denmark in Shanghai held discussions for a long time and finally agreed on a safe method to rescue Far East-Europe shipping: abolish the competitive practice of offering rebates and discounts, implement a "public dispatch" of goods based on a grand alliance, and have a public notary hired by all shipping merchants to handle the matter.

The volume of export goods from Shanghai to Europe has now decreased by two-thirds compared to before (mainly because soybeans and miscellaneous grains from the Northeast are no longer being shipped). According to current investigations, the total annual exports are at most between 110,000 and 160,000 tons. There are five British shipping companies, one French shipping company, two German shipping companies, one American shipping company, one Japanese shipping company, and one each from Norway, Denmark, the Netherlands, and Italy competing for the shipping. The principle of pooling has shifted from "not worrying about scarcity but worrying about inequality" to "no equality and no scarcity."

Pooling has long been established for foreign railways. All parallel lines have a pooling system. The six companies of the Yangtze River in our country also have a pooling system, but the method seems similar to and different from this European shipping pool. In the European pool, "Thomson & Company", the agency in charge, first investigates and clarifies the total number of export goods from Shanghai (i.e., all of China) each month, and then statistically analyzes the ships and tonnage of the fourteen shipping companies. The amount of cargo loaded is then allocated using a percentage ratio. Once allocated, no more competition is allowed. Even for passenger loading, Thomson must be contacted first to obtain a pooling cargo certificate before reporting for shipment.

After detailed investigation by the reporter group, the pooling ratio of the fourteen shipping companies is listed below: British India Steam Navigation Company accounts for fourteen shares; Blue Funnel Line accounts for thirteen shares and four tenths; Nippon Yusen Kaisha accounts for twelve shares and twenty-five hundredths; American Mostyn Yanghang accounts for ten shares; Hempel Line accounts for nine shares and five tenths; French Post Office Steamship Company accounts for five shares and one tenth; Italian Post Office Company accounts for four shares and twenty-five hundredths; Netherlands Java Company (European class) accounts for five shares; Shunheng Yanghang accounts for five shares; Shilong Yanghang accounts for three shares and fifty hundredths; E-Tai (now E-He) accounts for four shares; Jardine Matheson (European class) accounts for two shares; Huichang Yanghang accounts for three shares; and Dalai Yanghang accounts for one share.

Pooling has now been implemented, and although there is less cargo, it is allocated evenly. From now on, the freight rate per ton can be maintained at a minimum of seventy-five shillings. Rebates are limited to 10%, but can only be settled after one or two months. Whether this method is convenient for loading is another question, but amidst this shipping recession, the European shipping industry has finally found a deep and solid solution. From now on, there will be no more favoring of some over others.

Zhejiang and Shanghai Purchase Foreign Rice, Jiangsu Chamber of Commerce Jointly Cables to Stop It 89

According to Shanghai Times News Agency, the Jiangsu Provincial Chamber of Commerce United Council telegraphed the Executive Yuan's Ministry of Finance yesterday, stating, "According to a letter from the Wuxian Chamber of Commerce, a member of this council, the Ningbo Chamber of Commerce is colluding with Shanghai merchants to request the Executive Yuan to issue free passports to purchase foreign rice, harming the country and its people, which is outrageous. Eastern Zhejiang had a great harvest last year, but the province's officials and merchants falsely claimed a poor harvest and, under the pretext of stabilizing rice prices, petitioned the government to issue tax-free passports for foreign rice to handle hundreds of thousands of bags of rice for sale in Shanghai. This year, farmers in both provinces are seeing a slight increase in rice prices, which can alleviate their hardship slightly. Unexpectedly, the province's officials and gentry have relapsed into their old ways and are again requesting tax-free passports, and Shanghai merchants are also being swayed, showing signs of following suit. If they are deceived and the request is approved, the reduction in national tax revenue is a minor matter, but the rural areas, which are already on the verge of bankruptcy, cannot withstand further destruction and pain. The matter is of great importance. We should telegraphically request the government to stop the transportation of foreign rice to relieve the people's livelihood," etc. Upon receiving the letter, the council investigated and found that the original purpose of transporting foreign rice to relieve famine was a necessary measure for Qin disasters and Jin rice sales. However, rural areas in Jiangsu still have 50-60% of rice in storage, and rice prices are currently rising slightly. If foreign rice is allowed to be dumped and deprives us of rice sales, rice prices will inevitably plummet to an irreparable level. This matter concerns the rural economy and cannot be ignored. We should truthfully submit this document and telegraphically request your review and approval to stop the transportation of foreign rice to relieve the people's livelihood," etc.

Rotary International District 81 Annual Conference Opens in Shanghai Tomorrow 92

The conference will last for three days to discuss four key points of service. The head office has sent the former president to Shanghai to participate.

According to the East China News Agency, the first annual conference of Rotary International District 81, including China, Hong Kong, and the Philippines, will open at the International Club on Jing'an Temple Road in this city at 7 pm tomorrow. The conference will last for three days and will close on the 15th. The US headquarters has specially sent former President Dr. Mark Lauer to Shanghai to participate. Dr. Mark went to Hangzhou the day before yesterday for sightseeing and is scheduled to return to Shanghai tonight. The District Governor, Wang Zhengting, is currently preparing various proposals and agendas and is very busy.

Head Office History

Rotary Club was founded in 1905, and the headquarters is in Chicago, USA. All members are all over the world, and only people with proper occupations are admitted. Its purpose is: 1. Automatically serve the society, 2. Service of this profession, 3. Social service (relief for widows, widowers, orphans, and the lonely), 4. Promote international peace. Since its establishment 31 years ago, there are a total of 3,915 locations and 166,032 members.

District Status

The Shanghai Rotary Club was founded in 1919. Its members are all over North China, Central China, South China, and other places, and 15 branches have been organized in various places. In the past year, Ningbo, Wuhu, Kaifeng, Shantou, Wucheng, and Wuchang have been established. Five more branches were established. Last year, Hong Kong and the Philippines were contacted and combined to form District 81. Over the years, in disaster areas around the world, members of the club have generously donated money. In recent years, our country has suffered from floods and droughts, and the amount of money donated by the club is very large.

District Conference

The club established the District 81 General Assembly last year. This year is the General Assembly. Rotary Clubs from all over the district, one representative is recommended for every 25 people or less, and two representatives for more than 25 people (one representative is recommended for every additional 25 people) come to Shanghai to attend. A total of 21 representatives from all over China, one from Hong Kong, and three from the Philippines, totaling more than 300 people, and over 100 representatives have arrived in Shanghai. The remaining people have already left for Shanghai one after another and will report tomorrow.

Opening Tomorrow

The meeting is scheduled to open at the International Club at 7 pm tomorrow. District Governor Dr. Wang Rutang, Shanghai Rotary Club President Zhu Puquan, Secretary Hague, and others are busy preparing for the meeting these days. The center of the meeting is to review past work and discuss the service center. The preparatory committee has assigned duties before the meeting: Chairman of the Committee Wang Zhengting; Member of the Certificate Committee (ie the certificate of representatives from all places) Yong Fuzhuo; Chairman of the Motion Committee Harris; separate finance, reception, accommodation, and transportation groups to serve the representatives and there are general auditors to maintain order. Also, the presidents of each branch serve as deputy directors, organizing and promoting the attendance committee, and the director is Meg, the secretary of the Shanghai Club.

Motion Schedule

Tomorrow, a dinner will be held at the International Club at 7 pm. The meeting will open at 10 am on the 14th. The District Governor will give a welcome speech and report on the purpose of the meeting. The Nanjing Branch will host lunch, and group discussions will be held in the afternoon. The Shanghai Branch will host dinner in the evening. The motions will be passed at 9 am on the 15th, and the club affairs report will be given. The governors will be elected. At noon, honorary member Wu Tiecheng, the mayor of this city, will host a reception in the city center. In the afternoon, the governor and district officials will meet. In the evening, a banquet will be held at Paramount (club members' wives and friends are welcome to participate). Dr. Mark Lauer, the former president specially sent by the head office to attend and give training, arrived in Shanghai and went to Hangzhou a few days ago, returned to Shanghai today, and can attend the meeting tomorrow.

The Silk and Satin Industry Association Asks the Municipal Chamber of Commerce to Arbitrate the Debt of Dashengfu 93

Xinsheng News Agency reports that Tianfu and Dashengfu, two silk and satin stores associated with the Quan Tuan [權團 - a business guild], have debtors who have not fully complied with the agreed-upon terms. Therefore, F康 [Fu Kang], 大豐 [Da Feng], 同章 [Tong Zhang], 雲章 [Yun Zhang], 協與 [Xie Yu], 麥成 [Mai Cheng], 麗華協 [Li Hua Xie], 鼎康 [Ding Kang], and sixty other silk stores have jointly sent a letter to the Silk and Satin Industry Association, requesting them to forward it to the Municipal Chamber of Commerce for arbitration. The letter reads: "Respectfully, after the bankruptcy of Tianfu Silk and Satin Store, the owed money to the staff and for goods amounts to more than 80,000 yuan. We should pursue Dashengfu, the associated store, for payment. However, the debtor, Wu Zhihao, who bears the same responsibility, has disappeared without a trace. The manager of the associated store initially completely denied any responsibility, attributing everything to Tianfu and refusing to deal with the matter. Subsequently, our members pursued legal action and the court ordered the inspection of the books. Wu Zhihao, realizing his position was untenable, then appointed Liang Shigui as his full representative to negotiate. After several rounds of discussions, he finally agreed to pay 35% of the total loan amount first, with the remaining balance to be paid after Dashengfu's autumn inventory, after repaying the loans with collateral, the remaining amount will be distributed among the members. A lawyer certified this agreement, and each party kept a copy for record. Later, the representative Liang sent Dashengfu's autumn inventory statement, which our members, after reviewing, found to be suspicious. We immediately sent representatives to inspect the store's books and found that there was a large amount of inventory that did not match the reported statement. We then appointed an accountant to re-examine the books, but the accountant found that the inventory listed in the books was mostly stamped with the words 'to be returned.' After the accountant studied the handwriting of the stamp, it seemed newly engraved and obviously not factual. When questioned, the person in charge of the store replied that the inventory had been returned to Tianfu. Upon investigation, Tianfu's goods were always collected by Dashengfu on its behalf. If suitable, Tianfu would issue a receipt. According to the person in charge of the store, if this were considered factual, then Dashengfu's goods would still rely on Tianfu. If unsuitable, they would be returned to Tianfu. Although separate in appearance, they are one in substance, indicating that they had a fraudulent intention from the start. Our members, unaware of their deceit, fell into a trap. We were in the process of legally pursuing them based on the agreement and the false accounts when Dashengfu suddenly announced liquidation, which halted our planned response. Now, the store is openly auctioning off its remaining goods, with large advertisements in major newspapers claiming to have over 500,000 yuan worth of inventory and a shocking promotion of selling two chi [尺 - a unit of measurement] of real silk spinning fabric for one fen [分 - a unit of currency]. We ask, is this inventory the remaining 65% owed to our members? And is selling two chi of silk fabric for one fen spending other people's money generously? This is obvious even to the unwise. However, one person opened two associated stores. When one store went bankrupt, the other store continued to operate calmly, without bearing the debt responsibility, and even selling off inventory at low prices, treating the creditors' capital like dirt. No one but a fool would willingly accept this. Therefore, at 7:00 PM on March 31st, we held a meeting of creditor representatives and invited Wu Zhihao to attend and report on how to resolve this case, in order to avoid accusations from all the creditors. Wu replied with a letter, still denying responsibility. Unexpectedly, the next day, the original site of the Dashengfu inventory auction officially opened as the 'Fuxing Guohuo Company' [復興國貨公司 - Revival National Products Company]. Interpreting the meaning of the word 'revival,' it is clearly Dashengfu's disguised resumption of business. Such rampant fraud is about to destroy commercial ethics completely. If not strictly suppressed, not only will the public anger of our members be difficult to quell, but also others who open associated stores may follow suit. The future of commerce is unimaginable. We have previously sent a letter to your association, requesting that it be forwarded to the Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce for arbitration. Now, our members have suffered significant losses and are unwilling to accept this. Moreover, your association is promoting commercial ethics and strictly punishing industry outcasts. We dare to jointly write this letter again, hoping that your association will forward it to the Municipal Chamber of Commerce, asking them to consider our commercial difficulties and promptly convene both parties for a fair arbitration based on reason. At the same time, we also request that you forward it to the Shanghai Municipal Social Affairs Bureau, asking them to order a thorough investigation and strict suppression of such pests who destroy commercial ethics, in order to deter fraud and prevent others from following suit. We are deeply grateful." The association, after receiving the letter, has already forwarded it separately.

In the Gu Zhuxuan Bribery Case, Zhang Tinggui and Zhao Guangfu Were Interrogated Yesterday 94

Zhang Testified About the Handover of the Bribe

Zhao Claimed His Mind Was Unclear

In the case of Gu Zhuxuan instigating the assassination of Tang Jiapeng, he was detained by the Special Second Court and sentenced to 15 years in prison. Later, during Gu's appeal period, the case of him bribing prison guards Zhao Guangfu and Zhang Tinggui (also known as Xiao Sizi) and others to give false testimony to overturn the verdict was revealed. After a clear investigation by the prosecutor, Gu Zhuxuan, his brother Gu Songmao, prison warden Wu Lu, guard Ma Xianxiang, and fugitive prison guards Ma Xianxian, Ma Xiancai, and Wang Yushou were prosecuted by the Criminal Court of the same court for the crime of instigating perjury. After Judge Li Changnian once interrogated them, all the defendants vehemently denied the charges. The trial was suspended by order, pending further questioning and verification. This has been reported in previous newspapers. Now, the presiding judge, Li Changnian, deemed it necessary to interrogate the complainants in this case, Zhang Tinggui and Zhao Guangfu. Therefore, yesterday afternoon at 3:00 PM, he and Prosecutor Wang Ren sat in the Second Criminal Court and first brought up Zhang Tinggui for questioning. Zhang testified that the warden Wang Yushou first said to him, "It's no use for you to accuse Boss Gu. If you want money, we can discuss it." Zhang replied, "We are in prison, what's the use of money?" Later, the guard Ma Xianxiang told him to retract his testimony, saying, "Everything has been taken care of elsewhere. It's useless for you to accuse him. You might as well take some money to use." Zhang asked how much money there was. Ma said 3,000 yuan, from which he would deduct 500 yuan as commission, leaving 2,500 yuan for Zhang. However, the money could not be given to Zhang temporarily and had to be deposited in a bank. Ma also said that Zhang's name could not be used and Ma would use a name on his behalf, Wang Chunhua. The official asked who deposited the money in the bank. Zhang replied that according to Ma Xianxiang, it was Gu San (Gu Songmao), Ma Xianxiang, and Zheng Jian three people who went to the Daya Bank to deposit the money. When Ma showed Zhang the bankbook, Zhang noticed that the account name on the book was Zhang Senyu. Zhang felt strange and asked why the account name changed from Wang Chunhua to Zhang Senyu. Ma said he had taken the wrong one, that the bankbook belonged to Zhao Guangfu, and then took out a bankbook with the account name Wang Chunhua from his pocket. At this point, Zhang managed to snatch the bankbook. Ma Xianxiang wanted to get the bankbook back, saying he would deposit it elsewhere. Zhang refused, and as a result, he asked fellow prisoner Cao Shida to keep it for him. Cao issued a receipt to Zhang (the receipt had already been submitted). At that time, Ma Xianxiang said to Zhang, "Just say in the appellate court that Zhao Guangfu asked me to testify." The official asked how Zhang testified in the appellate court. Zhang replied, "I said that Wang Jinkui, who is on the run, told me that the fourth boss asked him to do it, but I did not say Gu Si Laoban [顧四老闆 - Fourth Boss Gu]. I also said that Zhao Guangfu asked me to come out to testify." Zhang thought he would temporarily change his testimony in order to get the remaining money the next day. Unexpectedly, Ma and others abandoned their posts and fled with the money. The official asked what Zhang's initial testimony about Gu Zhuxuan was. Zhang replied that he had always testified that Gu Si Laoban instigated the crime. Only after obtaining the bankbook did he retract his testimony. He also asked if Warden Wu and Ma Xianxiang had spoken to him. Zhang replied no. At this point, Zhao Guangfu was brought to the court. The official asked if he had initially accused Gu Zhuxuan. Zhao replied yes. He also asked if his testimony had changed. Zhao replied that he could not remember clearly what he said during each interrogation. When asked if Gu Zhuxuan had instigated the killing of Tang Jiapeng, Zhao replied that he had never seen Gu Si Laoban. When asked if the guard Ma Xianxiang had given him a bankbook and asked him to retract his testimony, Zhao replied that there was no bankbook and he did not know Ma Xianxiang, only a guard named (Xiao Ma). When asked if Ma Xiancai and Wang Yushou had spoken to him, Zhao replied that he did not know these two people either. When asked if Gu Zhuxuan had sent anyone to persuade him to retract his testimony, Zhao replied that no one had spoken to him. He really wanted to borrow money from Gu Zhuxuan, but because Gu refused, he had this idea. Unexpectedly, he made a false thing true and was sentenced to 15 years. Later, he had a change of heart, so he explained in the appellate court that it was not him. The official asked why Zhao admitted that Ma Xianxiang asked him to retract his testimony during the prosecutor's investigation, but denied it today. Zhao replied that his mind was really unclear. The rest of his testimony remained evasive and cunning. Judge Li ordered that both prisoners be returned to prison to serve their sentences.

Female Thief Zhou Wangshi Confesses to Robbery and Murder Cases 96

The Case Is Very Complex

Nine Robbers and Another Woman

Thieves Zhou Yitong and others, gathered a gang of Jiangbei robbers, specializing in robbery and murder. The firearms they used for robbery were carried by Zhou's concubine Zhou Wangshi, in order to conceal them from the attention of detectives. Unexpectedly, in January of this year, she went out to engage in robbery again. She was still carrying two pistols and 30 bullets when she passed through the Gonghexin Road area. A police officer noticed her, suspicious of her behavior, and searched her, finding the above-mentioned pistols and bullets. After investigation by the detective team, she confessed that she was from Yancheng, living on Hengfeng Road, Zhabei. On January 1st of this year, Zheng Xiaoshouzi took away two pistols and went with Li Yizhi, Wang Shaoqing, Xia San, etc. to Nanshi Dapu Bridge to shoot and kill Wu Fugui. On the 6th of the same month, Zheng Xiaoshouzi colluded with Yang Defu and others to rob a certain cigarette paper shop on Xinqiao Road. They also colluded with Xiao Mao, Xu Xueqing, etc. to rob Liu Fengqi's jewelry store on Haichang Road. On the 8th of the same month, Zheng Xiaoshouzi also colluded with her husband Zhou Yitong, Sun Jiaoyou, Zhang Bao, Wang Liangyu, Zhang Yihong, Xiao Kuzi, Xu Defu, Ni Xiaoyouhan, Xu Yaowu, Tian Guisai, etc. to rob Chen Shunxing Bamboo Shop on Fangxie Road of legal currency, clothing, etc. On the 11th of the same month, Zheng Xiaoshouzi went out to rob again, resulting in the woman being arrested. The detectives then arrested Zhou Yitong, Xu Heshun, Xia San, Sun Jiaoyou, Wang Xiaoqing, Zhang Bao, Li Yizhi, Wang Liangyu, Zhang Yihong, etc. one after another, and together with the woman, they were handed over to the local court. After verification by Prosecutor Xiao, one pistol with serial number 169 matched the gun used in the Wu Fugui case. Therefore, a public prosecution was initiated for robbery and murder. Yesterday, Judge Chen interrogated them for a long time. Due to the complexity of the case, he ordered them to be interrogated again later. The defendants were returned to prison.

Where Did the Head Come From in the Fields of Zhoujiaqiao, Huxi? 97

The Bloodstains Were Obvious, Indicating It Had Been Separated from the Body Not Long Ago

The Reason Was Traced and Sent for Examination to Determine the Time of Death

A strange head was found in the fields of Zhoujiaqiao, Huxi, yesterday. The local bailiff reported it to the Shanghai Local Court, which appointed Prosecutor Kong Xianglin and Medical Examiner Xuan Zhiming to conduct an on-site examination. The head was found to be in the form of a skull, making it impossible to distinguish gender or age. However, the skull's blood color had not faded, and there were still bloodstains at the neck. It was determined that the head had been separated from the body for a maximum of three or four days, and that the murderer had used artificial methods to scrape off the skin, flesh, eyes, ears, nose, mouth, etc. from the head, making it into a skull shape in order to conceal the official investigation. This shows careful planning. It is evident that a tragic case occurred. Because there were no clues at the time, it was learned from the investigation that when the head was discovered, a passerby saw it being thrown out from inside a wall and reported it to the police, who took the reporter to the police station for questioning. Therefore, the prosecutor, exercising his authority, began to question the reporter while sending the head to the Zhenru Forensic Examination Institute to determine the sex and the time of death in order to thoroughly investigate the matter.

It was also learned that a farmer in the area claimed that at 5:00 PM on the 9th of this month, while picking vegetables in the field, he suddenly saw a paper package thrown out from inside the wall of a house. He immediately went forward to open it and saw a human head without skin or flesh. He was shocked and had to report it to the police station in charge. The detective then went to investigate the house, but everyone in the house said they did not know anything.

Jiang Xingjie's Youngest Son Asks for the Partition of a Million Yuan Estate 98

The Account Books Were First Submitted for Inspection

The Hearing Was Postponed for Two Weeks

Jiang Xingjie, a wealthy merchant from Nanjing who lived in Shanghai, passed away on January 22nd of the 23rd year of the Republic [1934], leaving behind a large estate. Jiang had four sons and six daughters, but all the assets were not divided, but was managed by Yang, Jiang's concubine. Now, his youngest son, Jiang Guopei, claims that his father's estate is estimated at 3 million yuan, and since he is now of age, he should be entitled to a portion according to the law. He therefore hired lawyer He Shimei to file a lawsuit in the First Special District Court against his mother Jiang Yang, and his brothers Jiang Guoyou and Jiang Guozhang, requesting a partition of the estate. He demanded that the 3 million yuan estate be divided into three parts, with himself receiving one-third, amounting to 1 million yuan. Yesterday morning, Judge Peng Shi opened the Fourth Civil Court for the hearing. The defendants also hired lawyers Jiang Yiping and Wang Fuchang to defend them. They claimed that they had just been appointed and were not prepared. Moreover, the assets of Jiang Xingjie were not as much as the plaintiff claimed. Furthermore, Jiang Xingjie had made a will before his death, which clearly stated the assets. His six daughters were each given 10,000 yuan, relinquishing their right to inheritance. The plaintiff was not a son born in wedlock, but was recognized as a son in the will, so he has the right to receive a portion and should be given according to the will. However, the plaintiff's lawyer, He, claimed that the plaintiff had never seen the will and that the estimation of the assets must be based on the defendant's general accounting books. These books were kept at the residence at No. 1 Qinyuan Village, Xinzha Road. To avoid any changes, he requested that the defendant be ordered to submit the books to the court for sealing. The defendant's lawyers insisted that there was no concealment or alteration and that such a measure was unnecessary. The plaintiff's lawyer insisted on this request, leading to a long debate. Finally, it was decided that the defendant would submit the books to lawyer Wang's office on Monday, and lawyer He would jointly review and seal them. Judge Peng Shi then announced that the case would be postponed for two weeks for another hearing.

Fang Tianjiexuan Confessed in Sichuan

The Police Searched the House but Found Nothing

The Shanghai Bank of China received a telegram from the Hongxian branch in Sichuan the night before, stating that they had detained a female counterfeiter who used Bank of China counterfeit currency. Therefore, the bank's deputy manager, accompanied by a representative lawyer, went to the French police to report the situation. Yesterday, Wang Lei Shi was sent to the First Criminal Court of the Second Special Court. The bank's representative lawyer then requested a postponement because the bank was currently closed for the holidays and did not understand the details. When questioned, Wang Lei Shi confessed that her husband, Wang Jizhi, had passed away eight years ago. She came to Shanghai last winter to collect debts and visit relatives. She had stayed at the Wuling Apartment and met a fellow Sichuan woman, Fang Tian, introduced by a fellow villager, Ou Huiyu. She had never sold counterfeit currency and requested a thorough investigation. The plaintiff's lawyer also requested a postponement in order to telegraph Sichuan to clarify the details before proceeding with the investigation. Xue Jinzhai and Xue Chunrong Were Found Not Guilty and Released on Bail

Jiang Changlin and Others Jumped Out of the Window and Were Injured

Firefighters Bravely Rescued a Young Girl

The Shanghai News Resolves to Actively Rectify the City Appearance at the New Life Movement Conference 102

Calling for Charity Organizations to Discuss Relief for Beggars and Attention to Hygiene Facilities in Public Places

The Shanghai New Life Movement Promotion Association held its eleventh executive meeting at the Fenglin Bridge Municipal Party Headquarters conference room yesterday at 9:30 AM. Instructor Wu Tiecheng, executives Yu Hongjun, Cai Jinjun, Jiang Wen, Yang Hu, Zhang Shouyong, and Sui Jingshi were present. Hu Tianseng, Chen Cong, Wu Kecheng, Zhu Jiarang, and others were in attendance. Wu Tiecheng chaired and Hu Tianseng recorded. Chairman Wu Tiecheng first reported on the association's affairs, followed by resolutions on cases such as rectifying the city appearance and improving public health, which are recorded below:

Banning Welcoming Gods and Temple Fairs

The Municipal Party Headquarters sent a letter stating that temple fairs and welcoming gods should be strictly prohibited. Resolution: (Merged into the third case for discussion.) Regarding our association holding Cleanliness Movement Week, a method has been drafted, and it is requested to be approved. Resolution: Passed. Executive Jiang Hao proposed three items regarding the method for banning welcoming gods and temple fairs. Resolution: A letter will be sent to the Municipal Party Headquarters, requesting them to convene relevant parties to discuss the banning method in detail.

Actively Rectifying the City Appearance

Executive Cai Jinjun proposed: (1) Beggars are spread throughout the city, not only hindering the city appearance but also being a serious social problem. It is proposed to request the Municipal Government to provide relief to benefit the New Life Movement. Resolution: A letter will be sent to the Public Security Bureau requesting them to convene local charity organizations to find ways to provide relief. (2) Most lower and middle-class residences in the city do not have balconies or backyards, so residents often dry clothes in the street, which is most detrimental to the city appearance. However, it is difficult to prohibit this in the short term. It is proposed that from a fundamental perspective, the Public Works Bureau should not approve new building plans without balconies. From a symptomatic perspective, if it is not due to limited space and there is a possibility of installing balconies, the Public Works Bureau should investigate and encourage installation. Resolution: A letter will be sent to the Public Works Bureau for handling.

Attention to Public Health

(3) The sewers in the streets of the South City are often in disrepair, and some densely populated areas still lack sewer facilities, resulting in sewage filling the streets. This not only hinders the city appearance but also violates hygiene standards. It is requested that the Public Works Bureau actively investigate and repair this. Resolution: (A letter will be sent to the Public Works Bureau for handling.) (4) Since the city started using garbage cans, residents have generally found it convenient. However, the existing cans are mostly damaged, and many residents have not replaced them, often dumping garbage on the streets, which is very unsightly. It is proposed to request the Health Bureau to actively investigate and reorganize this. Resolution: (A letter will be sent to the Health Bureau and the Public Security Bureau for handling.) (5) Public toilets and urinals in the city are insufficient, and their facilities are mostly simple and crude. This not only hinders the city appearance but also harms public morals. It is proposed that the Health Bureau actively investigate and reorganize this. Protective walls must be installed on both sides of urinals in the street to emphasize public morals. Resolution: (A letter will be sent to the Health Bureau and the Public Security Bureau for handling.) (6) Disorderly posting of advertisements and slogans is most detrimental to the city appearance. However, except for the Pudong Branch's jurisdiction, most other areas in the city do not have enough advertisement posting locations. It seems necessary to investigate the needs and urgently add more to improve the city appearance. Resolution: (A letter will be sent to the Public Security Bureau.)

Improving Bathhouses and Teahouses

(7) Bathhouses in the city charge high fees, and the general poor cannot widely enjoy them. It is proposed to request the Municipal Government to establish public bathhouses or instruct bathhouses to reduce bathing fees to achieve universality and emphasize public hygiene. Resolution: (A letter will be sent to the Health Bureau and the Public Security Bureau, jointly convening bathhouse owners in the city to discuss reducing bathing fees and jointly establishing public bathhouses.) (8) Most teahouses, taverns, and bathhouse attendants in the city do not receive wages and rely on tips for income. They spare no effort to beg from customers, and some even extort money. This not only insults their personality but also fosters a bad and despicable social atmosphere. Three reform measures are proposed for resolution (attached measures): Request the Municipal Government to order the Public Security Bureau to instruct shop owners to determine the wages of attendants, and the walls of each room must have a solid slogan saying "No Tipping" signed "By the Owner." Stipulate penalties. Resolution: (A letter will be sent to the Social Affairs Bureau.)

Specifying the Work of Scavengers

(9) Scavengers in the city work too late, often not finishing until after 9:00 AM. Residents' chamber pots are lined up in front of their doors, which not only hinders the view but also violates hygiene standards. In addition to the Public Security Bureau urging residents not to place chamber pots outside their doors before the scavengers come and to bring them indoors after they are emptied, it is proposed that the Health Bureau specify the working hours of scavengers according to the seasons. Resolution: (A letter will be sent to the Health Bureau and the Public Security Bureau for handling.) (10) Please decide on the liaison method for the city's military police and New Life Movement to facilitate the work. Resolution: (A letter will be sent to the Garrison Headquarters to convene a meeting.) (11) The promotion of the New Life Movement in the city is complicated by the environment, and there are many things that need to be organized, which cannot be completed simultaneously. It is proposed to detail a plan for phased implementation to facilitate the work. Resolution: (Transferred to the association's design department for planning.) (12) Executive Zhang Shouyong proposed to investigate and do our best to eliminate accumulated habits in prisons and strive for cleanliness. Resolution: (Convene prison officials for discussion and invite the Public Security Bureau to participate.) The rest is omitted.

The Commercial Bank and Ningbo Money Shops Resolve the Issue of Using Secretly Marked Coupons 103

Each Shop Also Sends a Letter to the Siming Bank Requesting Fulfillment of the Contract

The Shanghai Times News Agency reports that twenty-eight money shops, including Ningbo Baoda and Dakang, previously had a dispute with the Commercial Bank over the issue of obtaining secretly marked coupons. Now, Yu Zuoting, Wang Wenhan, and others have resolved the issue through consultations with Du Yuesheng, the chairman of the bank's board of directors. Yesterday, the twenty-eight money shops also sent a letter to the Siming Bank, requesting them to consider the contract and continue to pay interest as before. Details of each situation are noted below:

Commercial Solution

Twenty-eight money shops, including Ningbo Dakang, jointly sent a letter to the Shanghai headquarters of the Commercial Bank, stating that the Ningbo branch of the Commercial Bank canceled the agreement to receive secretly marked coupons without the consent of both parties. They requested the maintenance of the contract's credibility. They also sent a letter to the Ningbo Chamber of Commerce, relayed to the Shanghai Ningbo Fellow Association, Yu Zuoting of the Shanghai Chamber of Commerce, Yu Qiaqing, and others, asking for their assistance. At the same time, they requested Wang Wenhan, the chairman of the Ningbo Chamber of Commerce, to come to Shanghai to negotiate with the Commercial Bank headquarters. Now, Chairman Du Yuesheng of the bank and Wang Wenhan have reached a consensus. The Ningbo branch of the Commercial Bank will subsidize interest, from December 21, 1935, until the expiration of the contract, totaling 20,320.69 yuan. Both parties expressed their agreement and announced a solution.

Siming Negotiation

Also, the money shops in the area have not resolved the issue of obtaining secretly marked coupons from the Ningbo branch of the Siming Bank. Therefore, they jointly sent a letter to the Shanghai headquarters, requesting the maintenance of contractual obligations and the continuation of interest payments. The original letter stated: Respectfully, in the case of the coupon contract established between your bank and our shop, all clauses have been clearly determined and both parties have complied. Our shop has also worked hard to promote sales, even if it means subsidizing premiums. However, it concerns our vital interests, ensuring smooth circulation without assuming responsibility. We believe that this difficult situation will be clearly understood. Even though the Ministry of Finance has ordered centralized issuance, we have not heard any orders to stop the circulation of paper money. The matter is clear, so how can we take this opportunity to cancel the contract? Now that the Commercial Bank's coupon issue has been resolved, we believe that your bank will remember past efforts and continue to honor the original contract, including continuing to pay interest to relieve business difficulties and emphasize credibility. Correspondingly, we request that you investigate and reply.

The Masts of the Jiang'an and Jiangxin Steamships Were Damaged by Lightning 104

Both Will Be Repaired After Arriving in Shanghai

The state-owned China Merchants Steam Navigation Company's Yangtze River transport ships, Jiang'an and Jiangxin, arrived in Shanghai yesterday. The masts of both ships were struck by lightning in Hankou at the same time. This matter is quite interesting. Our reporter went to the Jiang'an ship to meet Captain Chen and inquire about the truth. According to him, at 7:00 PM on the 8th, the ship was docked at the company's pier in Hankou. The crew members were having dinner in the cabin. There was a strong wind and heavy rain that day. Suddenly, there was a clap of thunder, and a flash of lightning struck the Jiang'an's rear mast. The ship shook as if it were about to capsize. The magnitude of the impact was immense. The metal on the pier clanged loudly, and pedestrians scattered. Fortunately, no one was on deck, and there were no accidents. Afterwards, an inspection revealed that the upper half of the mast had been struck in the center, as if split by a knife. After arriving in Shanghai, efforts will be made to repair it. Fortunately, there was a large iron ring on the mast, and the lightning stopped there, otherwise the deck would have been damaged as well. After striking the Jiang'an's mast, the lightning flew diagonally to the Jiangxin steamship (at that time, the Jiangxin and Jiang'an were docked at the same pier, bow to stern). Where the lightning struck, the outer layer of the Jiangxin's rear mast was also etched away, leaving only a wooden core. The etching of Jiangxin, which left only a wooden core, was the opposite of the Jiang'an's, which had its core removed. Truly a strange tale. No one on the Jiangxin was injured either. After arriving in Shanghai, the mast will also need to be repaired, he said.

Four People Died from Puffer Fish Poisoning 106

Fan A'quan...Fan A'da...Pan Lansheng...Zhao Lao'er

Around 11:00 AM the day before yesterday, an unknown man and Fan A'quan (30 years old) and Fan A'da (40 years old) each rode three rickshaws to the Shanghai Sanatorium. The unknown man claimed to the hospital that the two Fans had been poisoned by eating puffer fish and requested treatment. He also said that he did not bring any money and would return home to fetch it. However, he never came back. The Hongkou Police Station was notified and ordered Detective Shi Guichun to investigate. The two bodies were then taken to the Filon Road morgue for examination.

Also, Pan Lansheng, 49 years old, from Nanhui, Jiangsu, opened a butcher shop at No. 742 West Zha, Yinxiang Port. On the 9th of this month, Pan bought several puffer fish and brought them home. After cooking them, he and four members of his family used them as dishes for lunch. The family members only ate the fish meat and were fine afterwards. However, Pan ate all the fish organs, causing severe abdominal pain shortly afterwards. He was taken to the Sacred Heart Hospital for treatment, but it was ineffective, and he soon died. The Yangshupu Police Station was notified and ordered detectives to investigate. Pan's body was also taken to the morgue. Yesterday morning, Prosecutor Song Genshan from the First Special District Court, accompanied by forensic doctor Zhang Yan and clerk Wang Zuji, arrived at the morgue. All three bodies were examined and determined to have died from puffer fish poisoning. After the two police stations reported the previous situation, Mr. Song instructed that the bodies of the two Fans be buried by the Pushan Villa, and Pan's body was given to his wife, Pan Zhang, who signed a statement to take it back for burial.

Yesterday in the Gaolangqiao East Wangjiazhai thatched shed, Zhao Lao'er, 41 years old, from Tongzhou, picked up puffer fish eggs the day before yesterday afternoon and cooked them at home. He died of poisoning from the meal. Local guarantor Wang Dachang reported this to the local court, which dispatched Prosecutor Kong and others to examine the scene.
