Special Publication of the Shenbao Chinese Architecture Exhibition

Foreword 166

— Ye Gongchuo

Of the four greatest issues concerning people's livelihood, housing has become increasingly important in our country in recent years, and its impact has grown. In particular, production has been sluggish recently, and all industries have declined, but the need for housing has not decreased significantly. Moreover, due to the progress of new construction, the number of buildings in major cities is increasing day by day. The national cost each year is at least tens of millions of yuan, and the percentage of foreign materials is almost 70% or more. Therefore, it has become an extremely serious problem, similar to the influx of rice, wheat, yarn, and cloth. How to seek a remedy quickly is the responsibility of all citizens. However, it is ultimately better for specialists and entrepreneurs to understand and be closely involved. Furthermore, our country's architecture has a history of thousands of years, and it goes without saying that it represents the Far East. But in this era of rapid academic development, and with the environment constantly changing, how can we bring out inherent advantages and absorb foreign ideas to create an epoch-making style? Both of these issues urgently need answers.

However, in recent years, specialists and entrepreneurs have been burying themselves in their business, and no longer have the leisure to do more fundamental research. Therefore, the above-mentioned situation is gradually evolving day by day, and no one has been able to raise awareness and seek to remedy it. This danger is probably no less than clothing and food. Moreover, clothing and food are relatively simple, unlike the complexity and cost of housing. Therefore, the issue of housing can be said to be particularly important and serious in our country today. Colleagues, aware of this, have launched the Architecture Exhibition, with the intention of gathering specialists, scholars, and architectural peers from all over the country to jointly seek improvement measures, to learn from each other in academic theory and practice, to acquire new knowledge and methods to suit the times. At the same time, we want to give the public a full understanding of the inherent advantages of our country, and gradually digest and absorb them for application in modern things, in order to become a national style and establish new standards in the East. Therefore, we are soliciting submissions in five major categories: models, drawings, materials, tools, and books and periodicals, to meet the needs of this association and provide viewers with research material. Experts are invited to lecture on important issues in architecture on different days, in order to exchange knowledge. I believe that this exhibition will give the audience a deeper impression and become a new driving force to promote various skills and undertakings related to architecture. It is not merely to admire beauty and communicate ideas.

It seems strange that various sectors of the country have not paid deep attention to architecture, a matter so closely related to life. But it is not too late to plan for it now. Moreover, the country spends tens of millions of gold yuan on construction each year, and it is estimated that more than thousands of architects and supervisors are needed for construction, but the country can only train less than a hundred such talents each year. No more than a few universities across the country have architecture departments, and the facilities are far from complete. I don't know whether the education authorities think this is enough, as it has been temporarily forgotten. But there is no doubt that this phenomenon needs improvement. It is hoped that the authorities concerned will give it special attention.

As for the industries related to architecture, such as steelmaking, ironmaking, copper production, afforestation, timber production, paint production, pigments, enamel, ceramics, cement, bricks, tiles, stone, and various decorations, they are directly and indirectly related to the national livelihood and are related to the rise and fall of interests. Observing the general psychology, it is not that people do not know the fear of leaks, but domestic products are not enough to meet the demand. Sometimes, although domestic products are available, due to poor management and poor marketing, they cannot be obtained. And engineers and the construction industry are afraid of difficulties and take convenience, which turns into a habit, thus blocking the way for the development of domestic production. Cause and effect multiply, and things are getting worse. We cannot but hope that those concerned will quickly realize it, and that the authorities will do their best to promote it.

Moreover, our country's architecture is not backward. There have been famous experts in every generation. Since the opening of the sea, we have not been able to stick to the old rules, and inevitably picked up the leftovers of others. In the past 20 years, the domestic expenditure on large buildings has been huge, and the remuneration has been abundant, but there are very few who can come up with unique ideas and express their unique intentions. This is also a shame for our academic and business circles. Looking at how developed architecture and industry are in various countries, books on the study of our country's architecture are still emerging endlessly. Comparing the two, can we not feel ashamed? At present, world architectural patterns are tending to focus on the Eastern style. For the sake of the future of the entire architecture and for the sake of promoting the inherent characteristics of our country, we should have a plan to extract the essence and provide it to the world, and its responsibility is irreplaceable. Furthermore, how can our country's architecture in the future produce a new style, a Chinese style in the world, a Chinese style of the present era, while taking into account both inherent habits and economic conditions, so that it does not run counter to the real life of the people, and contains the significance of maintaining and developing the national livelihood? These are all the things that our architectural circles should painstakingly worry about and seek to answer: because this kind of responsibility, apart from our architectural circles, no one can shoulder. Therefore, the responsibility of our colleagues in the architectural world today is definitely not to be satisfied with obtaining their own fame and fortune, and to think that they are worthy of this era and national society. It is hoped that colleagues will pay great attention to this point during this gathering. Now, at the beginning of the opening, I dare to directly present my thoughts as above, and I hope that the public will teach me.

Preface to the Journal of the Chinese Architecture Exhibition 167

Our country's architectural studies were established the earliest. The "Kao Gong Ji" (Record of Trades) in the "Zhou Li" (Rites of Zhou) states, "Examine the curved surfaces and shapes to embellish the five materials and manage the people's utensils. This is called the hundreds of crafts." This is the beginning of architects in China. "The craftsmen are in charge of building the state, with the ancestral temple to the left and the altar of land to the right, facing the court and behind the market. The main roads are nine chariot tracks wide, the circular roads are seven tracks wide, and the field roads are five tracks wide." This shows that the construction of palaces had reached perfection, and had further developed into the construction of roads. The Afang Palace of Qin, the Weiyang Palace of the Han dynasty, the Dew Terrace, the Changhe Gate, the Taiji Hall of Emperor Wei Ming, the Zongzhang Temple, and the Lingyun Terrace, were all more than ten feet high, with phoenixes built on top of them, jade wells with brocade railings, toads holding and receiving, and divine dragons spitting out various structures. They followed the old ways, increasing their splendor and becoming extremely magnificent. Although they had already initiated the licentiousness and excess of Chen Houzhu's Linchun, Jieqi, and Wangxian Palaces, and Emperor Sui Yang's Maze Tower, from the perspective of architecture itself, we can still measure its rapid progress. Occasionally, I have examined the prosperity of architecture in our country, and there are two reasons for this. The Chinese people are ingenious and good at thinking, and they do not want their residences to be simple and crude. Therefore, after clothing and food, they must embellish their houses to gather their families and enjoy their etiquette. The "Kao Gong Ji" in the "Zhou Li" records that all people above the commoners have sleeping temples and schools, and the rooms where they usually live are called palaces. This is the proof. The Chinese people have a deep love for the past, and attach great importance to ancient buildings. The buildings of the Han and Tang dynasties, such as the Great and Small Wild Goose Pagodas, the Hall Without Beams, and the Single-Pillar Hall, still exist today. They have been destroyed and rebuilt many times, and repaired and renovated repeatedly. If it were not for the Chinese people's deep attachment to ancient objects, they would not be able to stand tall. With these two reasons, it is appropriate that Chinese architecture stands out in the East. Mr. Ye Yuhu and others are erudite and fond of antiquity, and especially like Chinese architecture. Therefore, they have organized the Chinese Architecture Exhibition, and they probably know this intention deeply. It is expected that it will promote Chinese culture and arouse the interest of the Chinese architectural community in using the past to create the new. The expansion and development of Chinese architecture will be determined by this meeting. As the conference journal is about to be published, Mr. Yuhu asked me for a preface. I am not talented, and I especially do not know about Chinese architecture. I will respectfully recite the anecdotes of ancient Chinese architecture and use it as a title for a few hundred words to correct it.

April, the twenty-fifth year of the Republic of China, respectfully prefaced by Zeng Yangfu of Pingyuan.

The Current Urgent Tasks of Chinese Architects 168

— Shanghai Architectural Society

Regardless of their type or nature, buildings have three major purposes: namely, economy, applicability, and aesthetics. In European and American countries, due to material development and cultural progress, architecture before the war rarely considered the above three principles. However, after the war, they received extraordinary lessons, and the architectural style changed dramatically. For example, the clumsy podium lines of the past, the rigid window frames or door frames, and the head lines around the outer doors have all been abandoned, and replaced with simple and clean planes and corners, striving for economical, beautiful, practical, and durable structures; unlike the cumbersomeness of the past, which was not practical, costly, and annoying.

Honorary President Wu Tiecheng Honorary Vice President Zeng Yangfu Honorary Vice President Shen Junyi President Ye Gongchuo Vice President Zhang Xiaoliang Vice President Li Jinpei 169

Several years ago, there was a fierce war of words in various architectural engineering publications and newspapers in Japan. The progressive faction advocated the modernization of Japanese architecture, while the conservative faction advocated conservatism. The final conclusion was that the faction advocating the conservation of Japanese architectural styles was gradually eliminated. Last year, due to the pro-fascist movement, there was another proposal for Japanese-style architecture, hoping to revive it. But in a short time, the　　　lun was extinguished again. Buildings are the symbols of human cultural progress; the evolution of styles has various complex reasons such as social economy, and its latent power is very great, and it can never be conservative and stagnant. Therefore, the faction in the Japanese architectural world that advocated conserving Japanese architecture was repeatedly defeated because it did not meet the needs of the times, and could not exist. Its failure was inevitable.

Since the establishment of the Republic of China, various constructions have been actively carried out. Since the revolution was completed and the capital was established in Nanjing, all administrative facilities have gradually been put on the right track, and the government authorities have made more efforts to build, with full scale. Looking at the various courts, ministries, and associations in Nanjing, all of them have been built one after another. In addition, there are many more public offices to be built. It is possible to take this opportunity to create a new architectural style that meets the above three principles of economy, applicability, and aesthetics. Because the current general architectural style is deeply felt to be rich in imitation and has lost its unique creative ability. Although we cannot forget our ancestors, it also loses the spirit of the new era to move and perform feudal products such as styles. The spirit of the new China must be expressed with epoch-making architecture. If the palace style is still used as the standard for architecture, not to mention its economic beauty, durability and applicability, but the suspicion of sticking to the old ways and not seeking progress is difficult to deny. I still remember that when Mr. Tan Zhen traveled to Germany to study the judiciary, he met a famous professor of law who asked Mr. Tan, saying that since the completion of the Chinese Revolution, the promulgation of laws has been based on the spirit of the Three People's Principles. Professor of architecture is asking about the current style and trend of Chinese architecture, I am afraid that it will be difficult for famous Chinese architects to have a real answer at a time, or they will say directly that modern Chinese architecture has a dual imitation: one is to imitate Western styles, and the other is Chinese ancient architecture. As for the new architectural style of the new China, it has not yet been conceived, and it is even more difficult to speculate when it will be conceived.

However, the creation of fine art in an era depends entirely on the efforts of artists and the supervision of society in that era. If the sages of the current architectural world can devote all their efforts to the research of new Chinese architectural styles, if there is any gain, they can describe it in writing, openly discuss it, and collect the opinions of the people. The conclusions obtained will definitely provide many inspirations and contributions to the new Chinese architectural styles. Or, with this power, a certain style can be produced, so that the Chinese architectural world will show a new dawn.

Buildings with rich imitation are often felt to have only a clumsy appearance and no spiritual sustenance. This may be because they are too imitative, focusing on copying, and looking at them is boring, making people feel intestinal gas. In front of us, we only feel a pile of solid objects, lacking a new spirit of creation. The general public may not understand the truth, and only feel that it is magnificent and beautiful; but those involved should know that China is in a precarious situation, and material resources are difficult. Only by seeking hard work and perseverance can we survive in the end. If we repeatedly move and perform this kind of architecture that is rich in feudal thoughts and wastes manpower and financial resources, the architects will be too ignorant of the current serious national crisis!

General Situation of the Society for Research in Chinese Architecture 170

1. Main purpose of work

The work of the Society for Research in Chinese Architecture focuses on studying the inherent architectural techniques of China and helping to create new architecture in the future. However, Chinese architecture, in terms of time, includes more than 4,000 years up and down; in terms of space, it extends from Japan in the east to the Pamirs in the west, from Jiaozhi in the south to the vast desert in the north. Architecture within this time and space is completely under one system. The highest and final goal of this association is to complete the history of this architectural system.

However, this architectural system with a long history and vast territory has been dismissed by scholars and officials in its birthplace for thousands of years. Although there are many relics, there are many documents that cannot be examined; sorting them out is often difficult. Therefore, to thoroughly study its history and technology, it is necessary to seek documentation and match it with physical objects. Therefore, this association temporarily established two groups: documentation and methodology, to divide the work and cooperate. For the convenience of work, we will start by studying the architectural style of the Qing Dynasty palaces. After we have a good understanding of the Qing style, we will trace back to the Ming and Yuan dynasties, and then seek the Song and Tang dynasties, in order to solve the problem easily. In order to achieve the above-mentioned objectives, the work mainly focuses on field investigation. The remaining work of sorting out old books and compiling books is focused on practical aspects. The research results will be used to plan the repair of ancient buildings by domestic groups, and to provide reference materials for teaching or design.

Page 18

. In recent years, the work of the association has gradually been recognized by the general public, and the association has gradually gained the opportunity to contribute and serve, which is a pleasure for colleagues.

2. History and General Situation of Work

In the seventh year of the Republic of China, Mr. Zhu Guixin passed through Nanjing and browsed the books in the Jiangsu Provincial Library. He discovered the manuscript of the "Yingzao Fashi" (Building Standards) of the Song Dynasty by Li Mingzhong. He then negotiated with the authorities and agreed to publish it in lithographic edition. Later, he and Mr. Tao Lanquan collected various editions of the "Siku Quanshu," including the Wen Yuan and Wen Jin editions. After careful proofreading, in the fourteenth year of the Republic of China, the Song-style edition of "Yingzao Fashi" was re-published. Scholars at home and abroad gradually learned that there was also the study of construction in ancient China. Later, Mr. Zhu devoted himself to the collation of the Qing Dynasty's "Engineering Practice Rules and Regulations." By the eighteenth year of the Republic of China, Mr. Zhu felt that the scope of research was expanding and that it was not easy to work independently. Therefore, he negotiated with the Board of Directors of the China Foundation for the Promotion of Education and Culture to subsidize 15,000 yuan for research expenses each year for a period of three years. Thus, the Society for Research in Chinese Architecture was organized, and private research became an academic organization. Later, subsidies were continued, and it has been seven years now (the twenty-fifth year of the Republic of China).

In March of the nineteenth year of the Republic of China, the Society for Research in Chinese Architecture was formally established at No. 7 Baozhuzi Hutong, Beiping. At that time, the scope of research focused on the collation of ancient books and the translation of foreign works. In addition to the collation of the Qing Dynasty's "Ministry of Engineering Practice Rules and Regulations," which began in the sixteenth year of the Republic of China and still needs to be continued, the "Yuan Zhi" was also collated, and the materials of "Zhejiang Lu" and "Yingzao Da Shi Nian Biao" were collected. Also, in this year, the first volume of the "Hui Kan" was published in two issues, the main items of which include the founding of the Society for Research in Chinese Architecture and the opening speech, the commemoration of the 820th anniversary of Li Mingzhong, the proofreading of the re-published Song-style "Yingzao Fashi," the "Yuan Dadu Palace Garden Tu Kao," and several translations. At that time, there were fewer than ten staff members.

In March of the twentieth year of the Republic of China, an exhibition of cultural relics from the Yuanmingyuan was held in Zhongshan Park, Beiping, which attracted the attention of society. In the second year, in addition to continuing to collect documentary materials, the "Hui Kan" in the second volume increased to three issues, the main items of which include the "Ji of Imitating the Sutra Pavilion of the Putuozongcheng Temple in Rehe," "Yingzao Suan Li," and the collation and printing of the "Gong Duan Yingzao Lu" and other articles.

In July of the twentieth year, the Society was reorganized into two groups: documentation and methodology. The work of the documentation group focused on the collection of historical materials, and Mr. Zhu himself served as the director. The methodology group focused on physical measurement and the collation of methods and regulations, and Mr. Liang Sicheng was hired as the director. The staff increased to more than ten people. The important works include the compilation of "Zhejiang Lu" and the collection of historical materials of the Ming Dynasty's Beijing Palace Garden, and the measurement of the Liaojian Guanyin Pavilion, Shanmen, and the Three Bodhisattva Hall of the Liaoguangji Temple in Binzhi County, Hebei Province. Since then, members have been dispatched in groups to investigate in the spring and autumn seasons every year, which has become the main work of this association. And the "Hui Kan" has been set as a quarterly from this year, publishing four issues a year, and the contributions are limited to the research papers of the members.

In July of the twenty-first year, because the address of the society in Binzhuzi Hutong was not enough, the Zhongshan Park Board of Directors agreed. It was moved to the West Chaofang inside Tiananmen, as the address of the association. Mr. Liu Dunzhen was hired as the director of the Documentation Group. The staff increased to more than 20 people. The main works of this year include the investigation of ancient buildings in Zhengding and the compilation of the "New Interpretation of Yingzao Fashi," the collection of historical materials on construction in the Ming Dynasty's "Shilu," and participation in the repair plan of the Wen Yuange and other places in the Forbidden City in Beiping, and the supply of reference specimens and models to many domestic and foreign groups and schools.

In September of the twenty-second year, ancient buildings in Yingxian and Datong in Shanxi, and Zhengding and Yuanshi in Zhao County, Hebei, were investigated, and historical materials on construction in the Qing Dynasty were collected. The "Qing Style Yingzao Rules and Regulations" written by Mr. Liang Sicheng was also published in this year.

In the summer of the twenty-third year, the Board of Directors of the Sino-British Boxer Indemnity Fund decided to subsidize the association with 20,000 yuan for the compilation of books and records, which was paid in two years. In the autumn of this year, the relics of Taiyuan, Wenshui, Fenyang, Xiaoyi, Jiexiu, Lingshi, Huoxian, and Zhaocheng in Shanxi Province, and Hangzhou, Jinhua, Xuanping in Zhejiang Province, and Dingxing, Laishui, Yi Zhuo in Hebei Province were investigated. Construction Hall, planned the repair plan of Liuhe Pagoda in Hangzhou. The following spring, the Cultural Relics Consolidation Committee of the former capital hired the association as a technical consultant to repair ancient buildings in Beiping. Also, at the invitation of the Ministry of Internal Affairs and Education, the plan for the reconstruction of the Confucius Temple in Qufu was planned. In May, antiquities in Anping, Quyang, Dingxian, and Anyang in Henan, and other places in Hebei were investigated, and the Qing Palace-style bridge seat was sorted out.

In the autumn of the twenty-fourth year, the Wenyuan Pavilion, Wenhua Hall, and the Inner Cabinet Warehouse of the Forbidden City were measured, as well as ancient buildings in Suzhou and the ruins of Lama Pagodas in Beiping. Edited the "Reference Atlas of Chinese Architectural Design," "Investigation Report of Ancient Buildings," "Panoramic View of the Collection of Books in Wenyuan Pavilion," and "Chronicle of Events in the Ming Dynasty."

A Brief History of the Shanghai Architectural Society 171

— Jian

The Shanghai Architectural Society has a history of seven years since its establishment. The comrades in the architectural world originally had a gathering in Yingchunfang, Zhejiang Road. Later, due to differences in opinions, it was divided into two, and finally merged into one, and Rongyangli in Pingwang Street was rented as the meeting place. In a few years, due to changes in personnel and changes in the environment, the once-prosperous club affairs returned to a state of sluggishness. Although there were a few enthusiasts who came to the meeting every day, unfortunately, at this time, a member was kidnapped by bandits at the entrance of the lane, so the other members were afraid and dared not come, and regarded the meeting place as a dangerous place, so they had to temporarily end this gathering.

Because of our professional relationship, we often have the opportunity to get together. Since the club affairs were suspended and scattered for a long time, we felt that the organization of the group has great potential for promoting friendship, exchanging business, and cultivating the spirit. We also felt that the previous gatherings without purpose and organization had the function of uniting, but no central goal. Therefore, after a long period of brewing and many discussions, the Shanghai Architectural Society was initiated in the spring of the nineteenth year of the Republic of China. The author was publicly elected to draft the constitution, and a preparatory office was set up on the third floor of No. 19 Jiujiang Road. In addition to the old members from the Rongyangli era, many newcomers were also recruited and jointly listed as initiators. At this time, the initiators had divided opinions on the progress of the club affairs. One was radical, soliciting 1,000 members at a time, each paying a membership fee of 200 yuan, for a total of 200,000 yuan. In this way, land could be purchased to build a club, and the daily expenses could be taken from the income of the remaining houses of the club, so that the future of the club affairs could be based on a stable and long-term basis. The person who advocated this proposal was Mr. Chen Shouzhi, and those who agreed were Zhu Quantong, Lu Songhua, and Wang Fafao. The other side was opposed to this faction, believing that the club was still in the preparatory stage, and there was little work to be done, and not many people understood the purpose of the club. It was better to publicize widely and solicit members on a large scale. After the club was formally established and gained the belief of the general public, the aforementioned proposal would be implemented. The person who presided over this view was Mr. Tao Guilin, and those who agreed were Jiang Changgeng and Tang Jingxian. The author's proposition is between the urgent and the slow, only seeking that the club affairs can move forward, both are good strategies. All my views are moderate and progressive.

Drawing of the New Building of the China Aviation Association (China Architecture Exhibition held here) 172
