Constructed by Jiutai Jinji Construction Factory

After a considerable period of preparation, with approval and encouragement from all sides, the spirit of active progress was further stimulated. Now that the association's affairs had taken shape, the only task was to complete the procedures for registration with the Party and government authorities. The Shanghai Special City Party Department's Civil Training Committee sent personnel to inspect several times, deemed it qualified, and issued a certificate of permission to establish. Following the regulations, a request for registration was submitted to the Shanghai Municipal Education Bureau, which sent personnel to inspect several times before granting approval. In the summer of the nineteenth year, during the preparatory period, a bulletin was compiled and published weekly, dedicated to preparation news, along with specialized translations, and distributed to various architectural engineering groups, organizations, and individuals, to publicize the association's affairs and to make the general public aware of our objectives. The current Architectural Monthly has its roots in this nascent bulletin. In the autumn of the same year, in view of the shortage of intermediate architectural engineering talents, the Enemy Reserve Committee established a vocational supplementary night school, publicly recommending Mr. Tang Jingxian as the principal. Classes were held from 7:00 PM to 9:00 PM daily, with a curriculum divided into elementary and advanced levels, each lasting three years, for a total of six years of study. At the beginning, three classes of the elementary level were recruited first, with students mostly being apprentices from construction factories, and draftsmen and trainees from architectural engineering firms, each having their own full-time jobs during the day.

During the preparatory period, the early compilation and printing of the bulletin and the establishment of the night school were practical and garnered external sympathy. At this time, the preparation of the association's affairs proceeded smoothly, and there was enthusiastic demand from all sides to join as members. With the registration procedures successfully completed, there was an urgent need to conclude the preparatory work and formally establish the association on a fixed date. The preparatory committee decided to hold the inaugural meeting on February 28th of the twentieth year at the Ningbo Fellow-Provincials Association on Xizang Road. Prior to this, a request was submitted to the Municipal Party Department and the Municipal Education Bureau to send personnel to attend for guidance and supervision of the election.

At 2:00 PM on February 28th of the twentieth year, pedestrians streamed along Xizang Road, and carriages followed one another, all heading towards the Ningbo Fellow-Provincials Association, clearly to attend the inaugural meeting of the Shanghai Architectural Association. On that day, attendees included representatives from Party and government organizations, namely Li Jiran from the Municipal Party Department and Li Dachao from the Municipal Education Bureau, guests including Shen Junyi, Director of the Municipal Public Works Bureau, Dong Dayou, Wu Mai, and all members, totaling over three hundred people. Wang Gaosun, Xie Bingheng, Chen Shouchi, Tao Guilin, and Du Yange were publicly elected as the presidium. The meeting opened with a speech by Wang Gaosun, followed by Du Yange reporting on the association's preparatory process. Representatives from the Municipal Party Department and the Municipal Education Bureau then delivered speeches in succession, followed by speeches from guests. Finally, the association's charter was discussed and approved, and officers were elected in accordance with the charter, including nine executive committee members, three alternate executive committee members, three supervisory committee members, and two alternate supervisory committee members. The elected executive committee members were Tao Guilin, Wang Gaosun, Jiang Changgeng, Lu Songhua, Tang Jingxian, Du Yange, Chen Shifan, Chen Shouchi, and Xie Bingheng. The elected alternate executive committee members were Sun Deshui, Gui Lansun, and Xu Huchen. The elected supervisory committee members were Zhu Quantong, Chen Songling, and Wang Faho. The alternate supervisory committee members were Fang Xianghe and Zhang Yutian. The elected executive and supervisory committee members were sworn in, and a photograph was taken before the meeting adjourned. On the same day, the Shishi Xinbao (The China Times) published a special broadsheet on the inaugural meeting of the Shanghai Architectural Association. (We originally planned to publish a thick special issue on that day, but due to insufficient time for compilation and printing, it was postponed for one month.) On the same evening, a grand banquet was held in the entire hall of the Dadong Restaurant, attended by over five hundred Chinese and foreign guests and members. During the banquet, speeches were given by Mr. Jiang Changchuan, the son of Mr. Jiang Yusheng, a pioneer in Shanghai's architectural field, and lawyer Wu Mai, followed by entertainment, and the gathering concluded late into the night.

On March 2nd, the first joint meeting of the first executive and supervisory committees was held, and Wang Gaosun, Jiang Changgeng, and Tang Jingxian were elected as standing committee members, and Wang Gaosun was elected as chairman among the standing committee members. The work was divided into nine sections, each with specific responsibilities, namely: (General Affairs) Jiang Changgeng, (Accounting) Chen Shouchi, (Investigation) Lu Songhua, (Education) Tang Jingxian, (Academic and Publicity) Du Yange, (Materials) Tao Guilin, (Equipment) Xie Bingheng, Wang Gaosun, (Introduction) Chen Shifan, etc. In July of the same year, due to the progress of the association's affairs, the original premises were no longer sufficient, so the association moved to No. 316-318 Pushi Road in the French Concession. In the autumn of that year, the entire China suffered a rare historical flood. Provinces were inundated, almost becoming swamps. Lamentations of refugees were everywhere, a tragic sight to behold. At this time, most of the association's energy was spent on fundraising for disaster relief, which was the responsibility of individuals and organizations and the most urgent action at the time. Unexpectedly, before disaster relief was completed and appeals were still ongoing, the border province sounded the alarm on September 18th, and the work of national salvation had to be taken care of as well. In this environment of internal troubles and external threats, mutually tormenting each other, it was truly difficult to seek the progress of the association's affairs, and maintaining the status quo was already a great blessing.

On January 28th of the twenty-first year, an unfortunate conflict occurred in this port city again. Due to this turmoil, Shanghai, known as the national commercial and financial center, fell into a state of depression and stagnation in all industries. Profit-making production organizations found it difficult to maintain themselves, and consumer groups and enterprises felt that there was no way to proceed. The affiliated night school was also temporarily suspended due to the declaration of martial law at night due to the war, which made it inconvenient for teachers and students to travel. It was decided to wait for the situation to stabilize before resuming classes. At this time, the association entered a state of invisible stagnation, and in the process of progress, it tasted cruel flavors.

The responsible colleagues, bearing the entrustment of all members, were still planning the association's activities day and night despite the extremely difficult environment. At the same time, as the term of office had expired, it was imperative to re-elect in accordance with the charter. Furthermore, as the association's location on Pushi Road in the French Concession was inconvenient, it was moved to No. 620, 6th Floor, Continental Emporium, Nanjing Road, the current location, in the summer of the twenty-first year, and Rooms 616 to 618 were opened as a reception hall for members to relax and receive guests. At the same time, the affiliated night school was also moved to No. 18 Guling Road, Changsha Road, and students were recruited starting in the autumn, and classes resumed as usual.

After the association moved to the Continental Emporium on Nanjing Road in the summer of the twenty-first year, the association's affairs progressed and showed signs of resurgence. In September of the same year, an order was received from the Shanghai Municipal Education Bureau, which was then forwarded by the Shanghai Municipal Government to the Ministry of Education of the National Government, approving the registration. Thus, the registration procedures with the competent authorities were completed, and the Shanghai Architectural Association was listed as one of the legal organizations in the country. The executive and supervisory committees considered that the term of office had expired and that the second general membership meeting should be convened in accordance with the charter to report on the status of the association's affairs, discuss progress matters, and re-elect officers, etc., and it was decided to hold the meeting on October 9th in the association's reception hall. In addition to all members, the attendees included Mao Xiaxuan, representative of the Municipal Party Department, and Nie Haifan, representative of the Municipal Education Bureau, who came to guide and supervise the election. The elected members of this term included Tang Jingxian, Tao Guilin, Jiang Changgeng, Xie Bingheng, Sun Deshui, Du Yange, Lu Songhua, Wang Yuefeng, and Chen Shouchi, as executive committee members. The alternate executive committee members were Yin Jizhi, He Jingdi, and Tao Guisong. The supervisory committee members were Zhu Quantong, Chen Songling, and Chen Shifan. The alternate supervisory committee members were Sun Weiming and Wang Faho. At the first meeting of the executive and supervisory committees, Tao Guilin, Xie Bingheng, and Du Yange were elected as standing committee members, and Tao Guilin was elected as chairman among the standing committee members. Since taking office, the officers of this term have held regular meetings and weekly meal meetings to discuss association affairs and provide more opportunities for gathering, with the twelve executive and supervisory committee members taking turns on duty. In November of the same year, the inaugural issue of Architectural Monthly was published. Subsequently, the service department, library, and other facilities were established one after another, adding a lot of work to the association's affairs.

On October 20th of the twenty-third year, the third general membership meeting was held in the West Hall on the 9th floor of the Eight Immortals Bridge YMCA in accordance with the charter to report on the status of the association's affairs, discuss progress matters, and re-elect officers, etc. In addition to the members, the attendees included Mao Xiaxuan, representative of the Municipal Party Department, and Nie Haifan, representative of the Municipal Education Bureau, who came to guide and supervise the election. The chairman was Tang Jingxian. After the rituals were completed, the report on the association's affairs and the revision of the charter were completed in succession. Finally, the results of the re-election of officers were as follows: the executive committee members were Zhu Quantong, Yao Chang'an, Chen Songling, Ying Xinghua, Chen Shouchi, He Jingdi, Yin Xinzhi, Sun Deshui, and Sun Weiming. The alternate executive committee members were Wang Minzhang, Chen Shifan, and Wang Faho. The supervisory committee members were Jiang Changgeng, Tao Guilin, and Lu Songhua. The alternate supervisory committee members were Tang Jingxian and Du Yange. On the same evening, a dinner party was held, attended by guests Pan Gongzhan, Director of the Shanghai Municipal Education Bureau, Jiang Kanghu, Xie Fusheng, Xu Xiaotian, and all members. During the banquet, speeches were given by Mr. Pan and Mr. Jiang, followed by entertainment such as architectural films and performances by the Datong Music Association. The first joint meeting of the third executive and supervisory committees produced three standing committee members: Yin Xinzhi, Lu Xinghua, and He Jingdi; and Mr. Yin was elected as chairman among the standing committee members. Later, as Mr. Yin often went on business trips to other cities and could not reside in Shanghai permanently, he resigned from the position of standing committee member and chairman, and Chen Songling was elected as standing committee member and chairman in his place. In order to increase the efficiency of the association's work, the Editorial Committee of Architectural Monthly and the School Affairs Committee of the Affiliated Night School were established. Chen Songling, Jiang Changgeng, and Zhu Quantong were elected as editorial committee members. Ying Xinghua, He Jingdi, and Yao Chang'an were elected as school affairs committee members. Since taking office, the officers of this term have shown a more enthusiastic service spirit than before, and all facilities have been put on the right track. However, because the entire society is trapped in the gloom of recession, the economy is declining, people's lives are withering, and all kinds of enterprises feel the depression of a slump. The association's income can only provide a part of the expenses of the association headquarters, and there is still a need to raise huge amounts of funds to maintain various affiliated enterprises such as the monthly magazine and night school. Therefore, in addition to being responsible for handling the association's affairs, the officers of this term have also put a lot of effort into raising funds.

Up to now, the Zhengyi Architectural Industrial Supplementary School affiliated to the association (named specifically by order of the Municipal Education Bureau) has held one graduation ceremony, with seven graduates: Liu Jiasheng, Wang Cheng, Huang Rongfang, Zhang Shanxiang, Wu Haozhen, Zhu Yunjun, and Zhang Yaozhong. The graduation certificates have also been verified and returned by the Shanghai Municipal Education Bureau. Each student has their own full-time job, and their skills are being applied, which is not in vain for the association's painstaking cultivation with huge sums of money for several years. The second graduation will be held in the summer of this year, and the semester has not yet ended, and the results have not been reviewed, so the number of graduates cannot be determined at this time. Architectural Monthly has been published to Volume 4, Issue 2. In terms of architectural books, the Architectural Dictionary can be published by the end of June this year, and the Continuous Beam Calculation Formula has been printed and is now on sale. The works of Mr. Lin Tongyan, an internationally renowned engineering expert, such as the Cross Continuous Frame Calculation Method, which have been published successively in Architectural Monthly, only need to be sorted out and can be printed immediately. Other works such as Engineering Valuation, Construction Science, and Architectural History, etc., will also be printed separately and listed as part of the series after they are published in the monthly magazine, in order to fulfill a slight responsibility in architectural culture.

The association has been established for seven years now. Outsiders will have their own evaluations of the achievements, and it is not convenient to elaborate. However, the author believes that the future harvest still needs to be cultivated with current efforts. As for whether the harvest is rich or not, let's not ask yet!

Characteristics That Architects Should Possess 173

— Yuan Zongyao

Design Ability

Design is crucial for architects. They spend a long time researching various architectural styles and methods to acquire specialized knowledge that others do not possess, which is also appropriate. Architects make the spatial distribution of any building convenient, so that each space is perfect in form and size. Architects should also know how to distribute the construction of each part so that it occupies the most advantageous position, and so that the entire plan can be achieved. Furthermore, the houses built by their drawings have convenient entrances and exits, which benefits the homeowners. Architects who lack intelligence are not like this: they often cause one part of a building to occupy too much space, or another part to occupy too little, or one part's position to be inconsistent with the plan, or they cause the passageway to occupy too much or too little space. All of these cause inconvenience or unsuitability to the users. Technically excellent architects pay attention to all aspects, so the above-mentioned shortcomings can be avoided.

From the economically important standpoint, in a limited position, architects can solve all the difficulties for the occupant and precisely plan the required volume, without neglecting even one cubic foot of area, and without failing to make it reach the most useful path. Because increasing one cubic foot of space costs money, and abandoning it without applying it to proper use is equivalent to wasting money. Now, architects can use space without abandoning it, which is of great benefit to us.

Knowledge of Observation Materials and Construction Methods

Using superior materials and equipment in construction, and building with good methods, these two should always be expressed by architects as their characteristics and originality. The importance of this characteristic and originality to architects is self-evident; the key is to study this characteristic and originality during their training and when they start drawing in the drawing room. For example, they observe various construction materials, examine their appearance, consider their durability, and then think about how an experienced person would select and specify various construction materials to realize their original plan. When construction begins, they should supervise and observe how materials are placed, such as whether they are appropriate; later, they should review whether the methods used and the materials taken are consistent with what was previously used.

Material suppliers often provide various materials and samples, so construction architects can often contact them or other representatives. In their spare time, they can also visit factories to understand the manufacturing methods of bricks, tiles, wood, marble, and oil cloth. In addition, from newspapers, architectural publications, and contemporary conversations about architecture, they can also obtain the essence of all professional undertakings, such as the comparative experiments transmitted by the U.S. Bureau of Standards (U.S.B. of Standard) and other famous industrial school laboratories, they can also take their essence as a reference. In short, they must be like merchants who buy the best materials, and when we hire them, they are our merchants, so that we can get excellent materials and save money.

Architects must inform material suppliers of what kind of materials are needed to achieve the intended effect during construction, adding color to those that are excellent and suitable. They supervise the project according to their policy, and sometimes ask reliable assistants to do it for them. When the construction is completed, we must be satisfied with the building's firmness and durability, and if it needs to be named or repaired in the future, the cost will be minimal. Because the foundation is solid, the ceiling is dry, the roof is firm, the walls do not transmit cold, heat, or moisture, the floor is always dry and does not crack, the ceiling lasts long and does not fade, and the stairs are easy to go up and down without noise. In short, a building that pays attention to everything and achieves such an effect is nothing more than for our enjoyment and peace, and to save us money, without the need for constant repairs.

Aesthetic Concepts Should Be Possessed

The third key point about architecture is aesthetics. Architects should use good plans to make the building suitable, and how to rely on their knowledge of building materials to ensure that it is strong and durable after completion has been detailed above. What I want to discuss now is the architect's drawings. Any completed building must have beauty: and this beauty is also unique to architects, so that they stand out from other businesses engaged in construction. Good engineers and architects know how to build well, and can even develop their ability to reach economical and elective plans; however, it is rare to see architects who have a full sense of beauty. I dare not say that every architect can possess this kind of aesthetic concept, and can reach the highest level; but I dare to silently say that every architect must have a considerable degree of aesthetic concept at least. Therefore, those who aspire to be architects must have drawing and aesthetic concepts. Their usual thoughts are mostly various concepts such as ratio, average, quasi-harmony, timbre, color, light, and experience: all day long, they are also immersed in ancient architecture, painting, sculpture, music, literature, and drama. All of these things have the word "beauty" in the middle, and after a long time, it is not surprising that architects possess aesthetic concepts. Architects can distinguish between good and bad beauty, and can apply this principle to construction, so the buildings formed by their drawings should be able to stand out from the buildings of ordinary untrained and unintelligent workers.

Regarding the concept of beauty, we can at least understand a little. If there are two things here, and we are allowed to choose, we must choose the better one, without a doubt. If we choose clothes, furniture, or cars, even if the various points of each type of object are the same, the result is that we choose the more beautiful one. If choosing objects is like this, then why not houses; because we want gorgeous houses and beautiful rafters. If architects add beautiful decorations to the building, the value of the house will increase, and the houses of the neighbors will also prosper, and the rent of this house will also increase as a result. Therefore, a house built with a good drawing and a house built with a worse drawing, even if they are in the same location and the same place, will definitely be more expensive when sold, it can be said. Bankers often make mortgage loans for houses with beautiful appearance, because they know that the value of houses handled by good architects must be considerable, and they must be easy to sell when sold one day. Real estate operators often say that in houses in the same convenient location, those that are beautifully built are easier to rent out than those that are inferior. From the above, the quality of beauty has commercial value, and can exceed the quality of firmness and convenience. Who can provide this quality other than architects?

Knowledge of Building Codes Should Be Possessed

There are several laws and regulations in various states in the United States that are related to construction. Therefore, architects must understand these laws and regulations so that the owners do not suffer any losses.

The current laws on architectural registration and licensing established in various states are to prevent a group of people who pretend to be architects from impersonating them, causing harm to the public. This law specifies that architects must receive considerable training, and prohibits general people without sufficient qualifications from being called architects. Therefore, general architects must be registered to be considered legal. In the registration law, the building codes of various cities and towns are often listed, such as the construction cost and planning cost, which must not exceed a certain number; if there is an excess, the architect must report it. Many of the states that do not have this law now also adopt it.

The so-called building codes refer to the old rules of various places, and the rules of various places are also different from each other. Therefore, if you want to build a house in Location A, you must comply with the building codes of Location A; if you want to build a house in Location B, you must also comply with the building codes of Location B at the same time. In addition, there are zoning or land section laws, which are also related to building houses. Furthermore, the state laws, insurance laws, contract laws, and public safety laws of various states and regions must be fully understood for construction. In addition, the federal patent law should also be studied; because if a certain style is adopted, and this style was invented by someone and has a patent right, a patent fee must be paid first before it can be adopted. For example, if you want to build a low-style counter for a bank building, the architect should know that this is a patented style, and it cannot be adopted without paying a patent fee. If you want to build several car garages, and you don't use elevators up and down, and you have to follow the law, if you don't know that this style is also patented, that is, even if the patentee has no direct relationship with this building, and the owner doesn't have to follow a certain patent. Paying the patent fee is the owner's responsibility; but it is the architect's responsibility to let the owner know about this current position. Therefore, architects must also understand building codes such as various patent systems.

Knowledge of Contractors Should Be Possessed

If architects have knowledge of contractors, they can decide who is qualified and who is not qualified when we invite workers to bid. If we listen to their advice, we can avoid everything related to bad projects, poor materials, and disputes. With their knowledge and experience, architects can introduce honest contractors to us. These people are responsible for their work and do not want to ruin their reputation. Architects choose a reliable and lower price among the prices asked by these people and let them build it, so that the owner can get satisfactory results without any worries about the architect; and on the other hand, they can save money, and even the amount saved exceeds the architect's remuneration. From this point of view, the benefit of architects to us is not also great! (Translated from the American Pencil Point magazine)

The Duties of an Architect 174

— Zong

In general, the success of a building project depends on very detailed procedures. Here, from the architect's consultation and planning of the building's progress to its completion, I will briefly describe the steps involved.

When we intend to construct a certain type of building, we should first go to an architect and inform them of the architectural style, location, and interior layout, as well as determine the size of the project, the preferred style, and the budget. In short, all information about the construction should be clearly communicated. The overall design should be discussed, and even minor details should be debated. The architect's duty is to ensure that the owner is satisfied with the work. How can they fulfill their responsibilities if they don't know everything, big and small? During the consultation and planning phase, we should share our needs and preferences. If the architect feels something is unimportant or unsuitable, they should use their knowledge and experience to explain the situation in detail, outlining the advantages and disadvantages. At the same time, the owner should listen to the architect's advice, just as they would listen to a doctor or lawyer. This would show wisdom.

When the architect is planning and proceeding, they will propose many things that are beyond our expectations. These suggestions are what we need and represent the most complete and innovative architectural solutions. Therefore, we should gladly accept them. The architect should thoroughly discuss the building's location, current and future land rental values, transportation, as well as drainage, gas, water, heating, and electricity. If deemed necessary, the architect can visit the site with the owner to gain firsthand knowledge. In short, before the architect begins to draw up plans, there must be multiple contacts and discussions with the owner before putting pen to paper. Initially, only a rough plan and an exterior design are created. This exterior design complements the original plan, and its beautiful form and harmonious colors should please viewers. At this point, the owner can observe and assess the architect's knowledge.

If you want to estimate the final cost of the completed building, it is difficult to predict the exact amount during this initial planning stage. Even if the architect can calculate the cost per cubic foot and then multiply by the total cubic footage to get an estimate, it is rare for the final cost to match the initial estimate after the building is completed. General contractors, with detailed drawings and specifications, still find it impossible for their bids to be within ten or twenty percent of each other. How much more so without detailed drawings and specifications? These initial plans and exterior designs are only for our reference, to see if we approve of the original plan or want to make changes.

When we view the initial plans and colored sketches, we can get an impression of the entire building and point out the advantages and disadvantages of various architectural styles for discussion. This continues until the sketches are revised and perfected to the owner's satisfaction. In this way, both parties agree, and the architect can determine the direction of progress. During the discussion period, within reasonable limits, we can make changes to the building as we wish, without any hindrance, no matter how many times. If all the initial consultations are carried out effectively, much trouble can be avoided in the realization of a complete plan. In short, we should be careful in advance and not act rashly, because what people care about is to be given working drawings and specifications.

Items not included in the working drawings are called "extra conditions". Architects and contractors dislike the existence of such conditions, as they can lead to disputes in the future. Therefore, during the negotiation, it is best to consider everything carefully, leaving nothing unmentioned in the conditions, to avoid future troubles.

Once we approve the plan and the cost of the building is within our intended range, the architect will begin the final working drawings and specifications. These two are extremely important because the contractors base their bids on them.

The working drawings and specifications contain information to give to the contractors. These documents are quite important and must be clearly expressed, otherwise, the contractors cannot calculate accurately and will inevitably ask for a higher price, fearing disputes and losses in the future. In this case, the owner's money is wasted. Therefore, all working documents must be carefully reviewed by an engineer to avoid excessive demands.

Our responsibility for the building is not limited to informing the architect about the location and reasonable requirements. We must also carefully review the initial sketches, working drawings, specifications, various suggestions, contracts with contractors, and other documents related to the architect and the owner. In short, the architect should not bother the owner with irrelevant matters. What they want to discuss is what they are entrusted to do for us. Their working drawings and specifications are the architect's words to the contractor, and they represent the architect's own ideas.

Working drawings are not academic exercises, sketches, or pictures, but drawings for work. Good working drawings give the contractor the same instructions as needed, without any deviation. These drawings must be clean, clear, accurate, and without vague conditions. The contract between the employer and the contractor is based on this, including the smallest and most visible details, such as foundations, floors, walls, heights, and descriptions of all parts of the building. From these specifications, the contractor can estimate the value of various materials and make an accurate list of material costs and all work costs, so they can ask for the lowest price. This price usually includes a profit of ten percent in addition to materials and labor costs. If the working drawings are poor and the conditions are unclear, the price will be high to prevent future losses and uncertain material costs. Improving the working drawings and specifications prepared by the architect can save us a lot of money.

Specifications are a written statement of all the guiding principles; this written expression fills in what is missing in the working drawings. These specifications must be clear and unambiguous, and all terms must be consistent with the terms in the working drawings. The quality of materials and the level of workmanship must be clearly stated. When drafting these specifications, refer to various material tests, material samples, and meet with material suppliers to compare market prices and determine which materials are most suitable for the building. In short, they are our purchasing manager for materials.

The complexity of working drawings and specifications is always proportional to the architectural style. For example, the cost of a hospital, residence, church, warehouse, or train station may be the same, but the drawings for the former are more complex and the latter are simpler. Therefore, the cost of the architect is often based on the form of the building. For buildings of the same cost, if the form is complex, the fee will be higher, and vice versa. Therefore, determining the fee based on the complexity of the drawings is the fairest method.

When we have approved the working drawings, we proceed to solicit bids from contractors. Under normal circumstances, the architect, as our representative, invites five or more contractors to prepare bids. Usually, they recommend several reliable contractors. If we have a familiar contractor, we can also include them. The working drawings and specifications are printed in blueprint form and distributed to each bidder. Each bidder estimates based on this the total cost of the building (including the contractor's capital and profit) and submits the sealed bid in a bid box before a specific date. To ensure fairness, the architect invites the owner to open and inspect the bids together. After opening, we often see that even with detailed working drawings and specifications, the bids vary greatly. The reason for this is the economic method of work, the method of construction, and the ability to purchase materials. Furthermore, the bids of general contractors include all the prices of subcontractors. The contractor undertakes the entire project and subcontracts each part of the building to subcontractors, such as plumbing, electrical, and hot water systems. Therefore, their bids are very different. General contractors usually undertake plumbing, excavation, and foundation work, while other work is undertaken by subcontractors. These subcontractors also enter into contracts and share responsibility for the work.

The matter of bidding has been described in detail. However, there is one thing that must be said: if bidders are unwilling to use inferior materials in the building, we can hire them regardless of how low their bid is. However, if we think their bid is too low and the bidder seems to be acting in bad faith, we have the right to reject their bid. After the bid is decided, the architect draws up a legal construction contract between us and the bidder, so that there is no doubt between the two parties and all work conditions are clearly understood, so that no disputes arise in the future. Sometimes the architect also requires the contractor to fulfill special conditions, otherwise, a fine will be imposed. This can affect the value of the work and make it slightly more expensive, but it can avoid the contractor's irresponsibility. In short, if the contractor is subject to these special conditions, we can rest assured about all aspects of the building!

Once these matters are completed, the drawings are submitted to the local government's construction department for review, and a building permit is requested. Then the contractor hires workers, gathers materials, and begins work, while the architect must also prepare detailed drawings.

Working drawings generally include all the conditions for the building. However, to ensure that contractors, subcontractors, and workers clearly understand the various conditions required for the building, the architect still needs to supplement detailed drawings to be distributed to the parties involved in the building, so that they make no mistakes or delays in the supply and formation of materials. The number and scope of these drawings depend on the complexity and size of the building. For example, when building a small-scale house, the number of detailed supplementary drawings will be less; if building a public library, the number of these drawings will be more. When detailed classification drawings are being built, the architect must plan how to eliminate the problems of wood shrinkage and expansion, moving parts in the building, and other unfavorable conditions. In this drawing, if the architect can accurately draw the carved ornaments, it will increase the beauty of the building. Sometimes the architect prepares a wooden model of the ornaments in advance, and then asks the craftsmen to imitate the model to achieve accuracy and beauty.

Architectural drawings can clearly answer all architectural questions and doubts. These drawings can not only reduce manufacturing costs but also increase the convenience and comfort of the building. For example, if the form and position of stairs, closets, bookshelves, and other utensils are clearly shown, they will be convenient and comfortable after they are made. Although the installation of various utensils is clearly shown in the drawings, due to the small size of the drawings, the workers still need to calculate carefully when implementing the installation. However, if all installations are calculated in detail by the architect, no errors will occur; and everything can be calculated by proportion, which is even more convenient. As for window decorations, eaves, chimneys, etc., they must be able to withstand wind and rain without peeling off. When the construction project is in progress, everything is prepared in the detailed drawings to avoid temporary haste, so that neither money nor time is wasted.

Even if the builder has specifications and detailed drawings, as well as explanations of all the minor problems of the building, it is impossible to guarantee that no problems will occur during the progress of the work. Therefore, the architect or their representative must often supervise the work in progress. If a large project is in progress, the architect must hire a supervisor to supervise regularly. If such a project is contracted by several contractors and there is no general contractor, then the supervisor cannot be omitted. Although it costs the employer more money, the efficiency of the work is greatly increased, which is convenient for the employer. In small projects, the supervisory representative of the contractor is responsible for checking whether the progress of each event in the work is consistent with the building register. The architect or their representative comes to check the materials used and the work in progress from time to time. When coming to inspect, sometimes some corrections are made: these corrections are difficult for others to know except for architects who have received several years of training. Also, if the architect does not propose these corrections, the workers will also ignore them.

The architect's observation of whether the materials and work meet the original work regulations is the most valuable and effective service for us. All contractors are honest and unwilling to commit fraud and neglect work, but it is human nature to be selfish. In short, they use inferior materials during the period to seek profit, just like sellers and buyers. The architect is not like that: their position is aligned with ours. They earnestly hope that the building will be successful and can do everything perfectly, which is the same as our original intention. Because this building can affect their reputation, they do not want many problems to occur and have unsatisfactory results. Therefore, they urge the contractor to do their best to complete the project. Inspection does not guarantee the elimination of bad work, so supervision is necessary. Inexperienced employers often give construction projects to those with the lowest bids, and claim that the contractor can give them excellent work, thereby not listening to the architect's advice.

We know very well that the architect can only be responsible for inspection due to other duties, but cannot be responsible for supervision. According to common practice, the scale of the project is small and only requires inspection, so the architect can act according to custom. However, when supervision is necessary, a supervisor must be hired. Although the salary is paid by the employer, the architect must also inspect

Page 20

the project.

For all construction projects, except for extremely small buildings, a supervisor is indispensable. The architect must advise the employer to hire this person. The architect does so only to benefit the employer. When the employer and the contractor initially sign the contract, the method of paying the bid price must be specified. If a part of the work is completed and the contractor asks for payment, the architect shall issue a certificate proving that the part of the work has achieved satisfactory results, and the employer shall then issue payment. When the contractor requests payment, the architect shall inspect whether the work is satisfactory and whether it is carried out in accordance with the specified conditions before issuing the certificate. At the beginning, the contractor calculates the price of materials and labor, and divides them into several phases for the employer to pay, so they can also pay other small contractors. This calculation sheet is submitted to the architect, and the architect now issues a certificate for the employer to pay, which is also based on this sheet. When they present this sheet to the architect, the architect shall be cautious and ensure that the initial and mid-term payments are not too much to prevent accidents; they do so to benefit the employer! (Translated from American Pencil Point magazine)

Discussions on Improving Chinese Architecture 175

— Du Yangen

The most distinctive feature of Chinese architecture is the roof. The magnificent glazed tiles, the unique beast-shaped ornaments, the standing and lying animal and human figures on the ridge, and the curved corners of the roof and the brackets under the eaves all demonstrate a full Chinese style. Therefore, in this time of declining national spirit, the inherent Chinese culture should be specially brought out. This contains the meaning of enlightening the masses and has the same significance as the reprint of ancient books by major bookstores and ethnic tomb sweeping. However, blindly imitating foreign things and blindly imitating ancient things are both criticized by the world. Therefore, in today's world, it is the right way to maintain the inherent spirit of our culture on the one hand, and to follow the world trend on the other hand. Taking the Chinese roof as an example, the wooden frame is originally used under the roof, and even the brackets at the eaves are made of wood. Now, because the wood is not durable and easily catches fire, reinforced concrete is used instead. However, the style of the brackets is still exactly the same as that of wood. The outside is painted and gilded. Moreover, because cement is prone to moisture and contains alkalinity, before painting, waterproof glue paint is applied, resulting in cumbersome and foot-binding work. This is only in terms of the reinforced concrete surface. As for the reinforced concrete used as roof trusses and roof panels, because the Chinese roof has a small slope, it is not beautiful, so it must be steep to show a dignified appearance. For example, the roof of a Chinese temple does not look very high from a distance, but when you step into the temple gate and want to see the head of the Buddha sitting in the center, you have to arch your neck. From this, you can imagine how high the roof is. Now, because the roof truss and roof are changed to reinforced concrete, and because of the load-bearing relationship of the reinforced concrete itself, and the wide span of Chinese houses, the structure of the roof truss is like a bridge, and the construction of the roof is difficult and costly. However, this is just one type of reinforced concrete roof truss and roof. As for glazed tiles, roof ridges, beast-shaped ornaments, and walking beasts, it is another cumbersome and material-consuming work, which violates the three principles of architecture: economy, aesthetics, and practicality. The uneconomical nature of the Chinese roof has been described above. The Chinese roof, from the eaves to the ridge, has a large area because of the steep slope. However, this large area cannot be used for proper purposes, which is an impractical drawback. Some people will definitely disagree with the unaesthetic nature of the Chinese roof and will criticize the author, so listen to the explanation. Aesthetics must have a sense of the times. In retrospect, let's discuss what is considered beautiful or not beautiful in this era. Simply put, in the past, Chinese women had to bind their feet, and the smaller the feet and the more unable to walk, the more beautiful they were considered. Now, what kind of feeling do you have when you see small feet? Furthermore, consider women's head ornaments, body suits, pleated skirts, and embroidered belts tied around the skirts, with bells hanging at the end of the embroidered belts. What kind of feeling do you have when you see women in this kind of dress now? These are all things that happened decades ago, so let's not mention them. Now, let's talk about the headdresses of our Mongolian compatriots, with all kinds of heavy and dazzling things. Although we can't directly say they are not beautiful, we definitely have doubts about their beauty. So, summing up the above, it is certain that beauty advances and retreats with the times. Then, can the so-called beauty of the Chinese roof stand firm in the ever-changing world for thousands of years? The critic must say no. Therefore, knowing that we cannot stay together and will eventually change, then we should not be bound by traditional ideas and not move forward, but should catch up quickly. All large buildings should be changed to reinforced concrete flat roofs, because flat roofs are really economical and practical. Moreover, all the required materials can be made in China. For example, cement is abundant in China, and steel bars are already made in China. Although the output is not much, the output will definitely increase once it is jointly promoted. Yellow sand and stones are almost everywhere in China, so there is no need to buy them from abroad. For the wood used for the shell, as long as the architect specifies in the specifications to use Jian pine or other Chinese wood as the shell, and use barrel wood for the props, then although foreign wood is cheaper than Chinese wood, Chinese materials will definitely be used in accordance with the specifications. Architects should be able to fulfill this responsibility. In this way, the construction of flat roofs does not require foreign materials. Only the felt and asphalt to be laid on the flat roof must be foreign goods. In fact, all of these can be avoided. As long as you pay attention to mixing evenly and pouring tightly when pouring cement, and there is no gap in the middle, and then use cement fine sand to smooth the surface after pouring, then this flat roof can be used without felt and without the worry of leakage. If the cement flat roof transmits heat easily, the problem is easier to solve. Just lay a layer of yellow sand on the smooth roof, build a layer of hollow bricks, pour coal ash cement on the brick surface, and then add cement fine sand to smooth the surface. In this way, the heat is blocked by the hollow bricks and cannot be directly transmitted to the room below, and the room will naturally be cool. After the above explanation, the economy and practicality of flat roofs should be clear. Only aesthetics and Chinese style need to be explained separately. Regarding aesthetics, it has already been said above that it should advance and retreat with the times. The trend of modern times is to focus on light makeup and plain colors, and those strong and gorgeous decorations are no longer suitable. Therefore, to seek aesthetics, you can add a little decoration to the eaves and use Chinese patterns, so that aesthetics and Chinese style can be solved easily. Furthermore, adding a Chinese roof on a three-dimensional building is an unnatural performance like pretentious behavior. I hope that architectural colleagues will have a revolutionary spirit and no longer be confined to one corner.

Architectural Industry 176

— Shanghai Architectural Society

It goes without saying that the architectural industry is more essential and grand than any other industry. However, ordinary people often fail to recognize this, leading to backward production and the purchase of large quantities of building materials from abroad, resulting in alarming financial losses over the years. Taking just the example of imported pine, the amount transported and sold in Shanghai, and then transshipped from Shanghai to inland areas, reaches 300 million feet annually, with a value of over 19 million national currency. Other materials needed for construction, such as steel, glass, water pipes, radiators, stoves, and electrical materials, are too numerous to list. Construction is the culmination of various industries and holds not only authority in industry and commerce, but also is closely related to the health, prosperity, history, and culture of a nation. Here are a few examples to illustrate the rest.

Architecture and National Health: Few Chinese people can enjoy the beauty of their homes. Most ordinary people live in cramped and dilapidated rooms, barely able to turn around. As for the extremely poor, some even live in nests or caves. This is, of course, due to their weak economic capabilities. These dilapidated houses lack drainage ditches for sewage and bright windows; as for dry floors, rainproof roofs, and walls that block wind and snow, these are even more out of the question. The poor living in such poor environments experience a life almost unbearable for humans, which undoubtedly affects their intelligence and health. Moreover, in the severe winter season, rain and snow are mixed; and when summer arrives, mosquitoes breed; plagues arise, and deaths follow. Although these disasters primarily affect the poor on the surface, the vitality of the nation is also severely lost. The people are the foundation of the country, as the ancient saying goes: rich and poor, noble and humble, all belong to humanity. There is no time to not have compassion for these extremely poor and helpless people, how can they be neglected? Therefore, authorities in Europe and America pay special attention to housing for the poor. For example, England's slum clearance movement builds new houses to accommodate them. America's construction of smoke-free zones, with over four thousand households in each village, uses electric heating for cooking. These are all ways for the government to improve the lives of the poor. In recent years, our country's authorities have also gradually paid attention to this, such as the construction of civilian villages, which is a clear sign of benefiting the common people.

As for those with some assets, they all strive for large size when building houses. Houses with nine bays and deeper depth are not uncommon. As a result, there are few people in large houses, and cleanliness and order inside the house cannot be maintained. Cobwebs form, snakes and rats hide, and the atmosphere is gloomy, which greatly harms the hygiene of the house. The reason for building such large houses is nothing more than to facilitate weddings and funerals, to flaunt wealth and power, and to show off. As for seeking comfort, that is not the primary consideration. As for major cities, due to the higher land prices, there are so-called Western-style houses. However, the interior is neither Chinese nor Western, creating a kind of deformed architecture. Sometimes, in order to prevent thieves, the iron bars are strict, like a prison; living in it, one gains security but loses freedom. Therefore, most Chinese people live in dwellings that are either simple and unbearable or clumsily abnormal. It is rare to find a simple, elegant, and practical house. The health of the nation depends on the comfort of the home, and the Chinese people should pay more attention to this.

Architecture and Industry and Commerce: As mentioned earlier, architecture is the culmination of various industries. Consider the smelting of the steel industry, steel beams, steel bars, reinforced concrete, steel mesh, and other steel materials. Although this industry is extremely large, it is, in general, only a part of the architectural industry. Other examples include mining and quarrying, extracting limestone, burning lime, and cement; as well as the extraction of granite and marble. These industries cannot be said to be small, but most of them have no possibility of development except for supplying the construction industry. In addition, industries such as forestry, sawmills, water and land transportation are all interdependent with the architectural industry, and their interests are closely related. The inseparable relationship between industry, commerce, and architecture can be seen in this. If the architectural industry is stagnant, these industries and commerce will be the first to suffer.

Architecture and History: Architecture is most closely related to history. When we examine historical sites, architecture is the most reliable source. The architecture of previous generations can serve as the historical record for today's people, and the architecture of today's people can be left to future generations as a reference. The solidity and grandeur of the Great Wall show the defense facilities of the Qin Dynasty. Nowadays, archaeologists live among broken walls and shattered monuments, all in order to obtain reliable historical materials from them.

Architecture and Culture: The culture of a country is expressed through books and paintings, and through drama and music; although they can each fully express the function of culture, the method of expression is most prominent and easily attracts attention through buildings. Other examples include sculpture and painting, all of which display the crystallization of architectural culture.

In summary, architecture is a comprehensive art with multifaceted relationships. Taking the example of a theater, it encompasses electricity, heating and cooling, sound, art, civil engineering, drainage pipes, water channels, lighting, hygiene, and safety equipment. This shows the complexity of its composition and the greatness of its construction. Those engaged in the architectural industry should all be glad to be a member of a great enterprise, and at the same time, should understand their own responsibilities and not fail the mission entrusted to them.

The Relationship Between Wire Mesh Fences and Architecture 177

— Ji

The development of the architectural industry in recent years has been rapid, and the magnificence of the external appearance and the splendor of the interior decoration of various buildings have been designed meticulously, and are constantly changing and improving. However, the outer perimeter of the building, which is related to the appearance, has not been improved. Looking at the major public buildings and private residences in Shanghai, and the exquisitely beautiful buildings and lush gardens, those who need to use the outer perimeter of the building all follow the old methods. The better ones are built with cement brick walls, and the worse ones are still surrounded by bamboo fences. The former is not very economical, and the latter is neither beautiful nor durable. Therefore, if you want to find a substitute that does not have these two disadvantages, there is nothing better than wire mesh fences.

Wire mesh fences have been used in various countries in Europe and America for a long time in public buildings, private residences, sports fields, stations, machines, factories, warehouses, doors and windows, etc. Because of their durable material, beautiful appearance, and ability to be installed in various shapes, they can also prevent accidents. There is nothing better than this to meet the needs of the outer perimeter and protection of buildings. It is a pity that few domestic architects have paid attention to this. The reason for this is nothing more than ordering from foreign countries, and there are many obstacles. The size of the fence eyes, the thickness of the wire, the height of the scale, the change of the installation style, and the configuration of the fence post materials all require accurate calculations in advance. If there is a small error, it will not meet the needs, or the foreign company will not be willing to order if the amount is too small. And the cost is unexpectedly expensive.

The Gongqin Iron Factory on Linqing Road, Yangshupu, Shanghai, already has this product. If you need this kind of mesh fence, you can directly inquire with the factory.

The Characteristics of Huaxin Cement Floor Tiles 178

The composition of a room must have a bright ceiling, soft walls, and a beautiful floor. The ideal floor should have the following five characteristics: 1. The floor should be attractive. When a person enters a room, they must first come into contact with the floor, and the contact is more than any other part. Therefore, the material used for the floor should be harmonious with the color of the walls and ceiling and have artistic significance, so that people feel refreshed and not tired when they enter the room. 2. The material used for the floor must have the ability to resist external friction. It must be used for a longer time, and the floor will be firmer. After thousands of years, it will be no different from the new paving. 3. The floor material should have the advantage of never fading. All inferior materials will change color once they are paved. Although the four walls are beautifully decorated, the beauty of the entire room has been greatly reduced. 4. The floor should use materials that are easy to clean. If there is dirt, it can be washed at any time to maintain hygiene. 5. The floor should be paved with durable materials, so that the value paid once will never increase, in short, no more floor repair costs will be required in the future.

The above five characteristics are necessary for an ideal floor, and Huaxin Bricks and Tiles Company's cement floor tiles (commonly known as patterned tiles) can meet this demand.

The cement floor tiles produced by Huaxin Company are different from the patterned tiles sold in the market in terms of quality and color. Huaxin floor tiles use high-quality raw materials, the required machinery has the highest pressure, and the patterns and colors are poured in very thickly. The longer they are used, the brighter the brick surface will be. Even after decades, they will still not change their beauty and vividness. Using Huaxin floor tiles, the cost is lower than any other paving material except cement floors, and its durability may even exceed it.

Although the manufacture of cement floor tiles in China has not been long, they have been popular in Europe and America for decades. In places such as Cuba and Havana, there are those that were paved a hundred years ago, and they are still as new as ever, without any damage. In recent years, cement floor tiles are used more often than other materials in large buildings in Europe and America. It can be seen that the use of cement floor tiles is no less than any other paving material. As for rough and shoddy patterned tiles, they should be discussed separately.

In Shanghai, it has been twenty years since there were cement floor tiles. The market is depressed, and sales are sluggish. This is indeed affected by rough and shoddy manufacturing. Now Huaxin floor tiles have risen and issued in a downturn, and have been promoted by the architectural community. The speed of sales is surprising. If it does not have its own standing, how can it be like this?

Huaxin floor tiles are manufactured using non-fading pigments and the best white cement, using new steam pressure machines, the smoothest models, and extremely beautiful patterns. Each square requires a pressure of more than two tons. With such a novel method, floor tiles with accurate dimensions, smooth brick surfaces, solid texture, bright colors, and clear patterns are made. The cost is saved and the floor tiles are durable, and then immersed in water for a considerable time, and then placed in a suitable temperature to dry, and then become the ideal floor tiles.

Huaxin floor tiles do not need to be burned or baked. Most of the manufacturing workers are skilled, and experts are hired to supervise from time to time. Therefore, the quality of the products is the best in the industry. Huaxin floor tiles with eight-inch squares are the most common, and four-inch squares, six-inch squares, and four-inch and eight-inch squares are also quite popular. Among them, there are two types: patterned and plain. They are most suitable for public places, banks, hotels, theaters, apartments, school hospitals, classrooms, and living rooms, corridors, platforms, and bathrooms in city houses.

Huaxin floor tiles are sold widely and spread to various ports. The quality of their products can be imagined. In addition to the major buildings in Beijing, Shanghai, Hangzhou, and Jiangxi last year, the International Friendship Club and the new houses of the Supervisory Committee of the Central Party Headquarters in Nanjing, which are currently under construction, also use the company's products, it is said.

A Visit to the Dazhong Brick and Tile Factory 179

This reporter believes that Shanghai's architecture is changing with each passing day, and that the high-rise buildings are new and stylish, almost comparable to Europe and America, and that the inner methods of the past know that the bricks and tiles that occupy an important part of the building materials must be gradually improved to adapt to the needs of the times. Therefore, there is a desire to visit one with a larger scale and better equipment. Fortunately, my friend Mr. Zhang has a good relationship with Mr. Zhu Hongxin, the manager of Dazhong Machine-made Brick and Tile Company, and specially entrusted him to introduce him and express his welcome. So in the bright spring light, he accompanied three people to Dongjiadu Dupu in Nanshi, took the car of Shangnan Transportation Company to Zhoupu in Nanhui County, and then took a connecting ferry south for an hour to reach the destination of Xiasha Tiexiang. Soon after landing, looking eastward, he saw towering chimneys, winding blue smoke, and workshops and factories arranged like scales and compared. Colleagues pointed remotely and said that this is probably the Dazhong Brick and Tile Factory, which is famous in Shanghai. Walking east, turning west and heading south, crossing the bridge to the factory, the stockpiles of goods were piled up, and the types were diverse. After another mile or so, he arrived at the office and sent a business card to pay a visit and state his intention. He was greeted by the factory director Mr. Shen Binru, who politely invited him to lead the visit. After more than two hours, he traveled all over the factory. The factory is located in the southeast of Xiasha Town, surrounded by rivers on three sides, with convenient transportation. It is more than two miles long from north to south and one mile wide from east to west, covering an area of more than 1,100 acres, and the breadth of the area can be said to be unique. The factory is densely covered with railways, from raw materials to manufacturing, cooling, drying, firing, and stacking, and all transportation is carried out by this to achieve the purpose of lightness and speed. The raw material is the local sticky soil, which is transported, dried, poured into the mud grinder, ground into powder, transferred to the mud mixer to mix with water, and then pressed into the mud press to squeeze and solidify, and then put into the blank making machine to make various bricks and tiles. The power is a 150-horsepower diesel engine, a 70-horsepower steam engine, and five motors of different sizes from 50 horsepower to 20 horsepower. In addition to the mud grinder, mud mixer, and mud press, there are two German-style brick making machines and six tile making machines, which can produce 200,000 blanks every day. After the blanks are completed, they are transported to the cooling room for a week of shade, and then transported to the drying field for drying. The drying and drying equipment is fired in the kiln. There are several types of kilns. One is a German-style ring kiln, with a total of two seats and 64 doors, which are specially used for firing red goods. The architecture is grand, and the Chonglou is built on top of it, which is also used for cooling blanks. The remaining various types are various pottery trials and large water kilns for firing green goods, with a total of twelve seats. The fire is lit day and night all year round, so although the sales are wide, the cargo yard along the river, two miles from north to south and east to west, is still piled up with nearly 10 million. The river is the cargo yard on both sides, and in the middle of the two kilns facing each other is the river. The blank making room is to the east, and the raw material yard is to the east. The office is to the south. The north and south sides of the blank making room, the raw material yard, and the office are all cool rooms and drying yards. There are more than 340 cool rooms, and the buildings on the kiln are not included. The drying yard is more than 250 acres wide, stretching endlessly from north to south. Looking at its products, hollow bricks, Western-style tiles, imitation ancient decorations, etc. suitable for modern architecture are all complete. The eastern border of the factory is a pool with more than a dozen banks planted with peach and willow trees. The pond stores fresh shrimp and green waves, and the swimming fish float and sink. It is a scenic spot for workers to relax. The Zhougui of the equipment and the Hongtan of the building are amazing.

The Outer Perimeter of the Building is Solemn and Beautiful with the Wire Mesh Fence Produced by Gongdong Iron Factory 180

Meihua Xincun (Holly Heath) at the corner of Hongqiao Road and Zhongshan Road in this port is very popular with those who come to build houses. The picture above shows the most beautiful new three-story building in the village. The entire building is built with steel and reinforced concrete and occupies an area of seven acres. The flower garden and the ball field are all beautiful. It is said that the design and supervision of the Shanghai Museum Road No. 128 Xingye Architects Office was done by Mr. Yang Runjun, Xu Jingzhi, and Li Huibo. Those who like to study the architectural industry should visit it.

A Visit to the China Stone Company 181

— Jingying

A few days ago, due to something happening in Shanghai, I was introduced by a friend to visit a China Stone Company that is purely domestic. The products are novel, the types of stones are various, and the colors are brilliant like woven brocade. I also heard that the internal and external stone materials of the International Hotel on Jing'an Temple Road, the Sihang Savings Association, and the Dashin Company Building on Nanjing Road are all supplied by the China Stone Company. The black feldspar used in the bottom layer is particularly superior to imported products in terms of material strength and luster. The Shanghai business office of the stone company is located at No. 310 Jing'an Temple Road. The founder is Mr. Yao Huasun. Mr. Yao has always had patriotic enthusiasm. In view of the fact that our country has abundant deposits, the Chinese people have abandoned them without development, but instead let the rough stone materials from across the ocean flow into the domestic market, which is a pain in his heart. Therefore, based on his patriotic enthusiasm, he made a groundbreaking move to develop the reality, and has worked hard to operate it. Over the years, he has made great achievements, which is enough to put a ray of light on the industrial and commercial industry of our country. Mr. is more spare no effort to study carefully, and the excellence of its products is especially rare. It is hoped that the Chinese people will advocate its application, so that the industrial and commercial industry operated by the Chinese people will not be affected by the downturn, open up new ways to resist foreign goods, and be a great fortune for the real industrial and commercial industry. It is also a way to block the outflow of wealth.

A Record of the Zhenye Asbestos Factory 182

— Zhongchi

Founding

Zhenye Asbestos Manufacturing Factory was founded in 1934. The factory is located in Dachangyu Hutong, Special Second District, Tianjin. The factory covers an area of 1.5 acres with capital of 200,000 yuan, and is a joint-stock company with Zhou Jinting as manager and Li Xingfu and Wang Xingjiu as deputy managers. The factory employs more than 120 workers and has 40 machines of various sizes. It is the largest asbestos manufacturing factory in China. In the spring of 1935, it took over Tianjin Asbestos Company, China Asbestos Company, and Kuiyelong Asbestos Factory, and its strength became more abundant. Mr. Zhou and Mr. Li believe that domestic asbestos products were mostly shoddy in the past, and imported goods have been increasingly dumped in recent years. The annual loss is extremely considerable, so they have carefully studied, added machinery, and improved various products. The various products produced are not inferior to foreign goods, and have been praised by various factories, railways and the construction industry throughout the country.

Mining Area

The mining area is located in Laiyuan County, Hebei Province, and the output is quite abundant. Except for a small part of Sichuan that has not been mined, the national asbestos raw materials are completely supplied by the Zhenye Asbestos Mine. It has a mining license, and mining is carried out independently. There are often 300 people, in addition to supplying the needs of the whole country, the export volume is also very large, and only this mine in the country is being mined.

Factory

The factory site is large, and the entire factory is divided into paper-making section, weaving section, rope-making section, brick and pipe section, spinning section, mining section, elastic rolling section, engineering section, etc., and the writing room is divided into accounting section, general affairs section, purchasing section, wholesale section, export section, and health section. Each section has one material chief and several clerks, 80 engineers and 40 apprentices, divided into day and night shifts. All workers and staff in the factory wear Zhongshan uniforms, and all the equipment is quite large-scale, which is enough to show the spirit of the factory.

Products

There are a wide variety of asbestos products, which can be summarized into dozens of types, including: asbestos coarse and fine cloth, asbestos copper wire cloth, asbestos square rope, asbestos yuan rope, asbestos loose rope, asbestos coarse and fine thread, asbestos lead wire square yuan rope, asbestos various cloth belts, asbestos paper, asbestos magnesium powder brick, asbestos magnesium powder tube, various asbestos mud, asbestos ring pads, asbestos fire-resistant clothing, cotton gloves, boot covers, asbestos stove opening, wick, pillow down, fiber, etc. The above-mentioned rope types range from 3/10 of a circle diameter to three inches, and the thread and paper types range from 2.5/100 of an inch to 4/10 of an inch. The humidity, tensile strength, pressure, and firepower of each product are not much different from foreign goods, because the raw materials from the mine are very cheap.

Business

Business Except for North China, which is directly wholesale by the head factory, the first general distribution location in Shanghai for South China is No. 7, Lane 573, Dongxi Huade Road. The telephone number is 53547. The second distribution address is in Hannichi at No. 390, Funan First Road. The distribution in Nanjing, Guangdong, Qingdao, and Peiping, which are still in preparation, mainly deal in building materials such as asbestos magnesium powder tubes, asbestos magnesium powder bricks, asbestos mud (paint), and asbestos paperboard, etc., which are well received by the architectural community for procurement. This proves that the factory's products are exquisite.
