Industrial and Commercial Practice

Tactics of Advertising 184

— Fu Xueqin

Everyone in the industrial and commercial world knows that advertising plays a vital role in business competition. For every commodity manufacturer, every company, foreign firm, and store, advertising expenses account for the largest portion of their expenditure. We have heard many experienced merchants say that if you want to do 20,000 yuan of business, you should spend 10,000 yuan on advertising. This is indeed experience speaking. Because nowadays, there are many similar types of any given product, if you have a good product but don't advertise it widely, the general public won't know about it, and naturally, they won't buy your product.

However, advertising must also be done effectively to achieve the greatest results with the least amount of advertising expenditure. At the same time, whether a business can prosper often depends on whether its advertising is effective. Sometimes, even the quality of the product is secondary; modern industrial and commercial competition mainly revolves around the quality of goods and the effectiveness of advertising. Therefore, industrial and commercial enterprises put their heart and soul into advertising methods, paying particular attention to them. Most larger industrial and commercial enterprises have a dedicated advertising department and spare no expense in hiring specialized technical personnel to specifically study advertising methods.

There are many types of advertising, and the methods are even more varied. We cannot discuss them in detail here, but we can briefly mention a few important points.

First of all, the primary purpose of advertising is of course to make the public aware of the products you want to sell. In addition to spending a lot of money on advertising, advertising in various places, and promoting it through various methods, the main thing is to use concise and powerful language to express the characteristics of the product, so that the general public unknowingly develops a deep and lasting impression of the product. According to people's general nature, they are generally not happy to read long texts, especially advertisements that have little to do with the country or society. Too long and fewer people will read it; therefore, unless absolutely necessary, advertising text should not be too long; it is best to choose a few words of slogan to express the characteristics of the product, so that the general public can easily remember it. For example, "Bailing Machine has unexpected effects," "Mingxing Flower Dew Perfume gets more fragrant with age,"... are good examples.

Secondly, in advertising, pictures are as important as words. A good advertisement must vividly present the product with an eye-catching picture, and then explain it with concise and appropriate text. But there are many types of advertising pictures? Generally, we can see two types: flat and three-dimensional. These two naturally have their own advantages, but generally speaking, we can say that three-dimensional images are more likely to make people have a concrete impression than flat images. A certain German tobacco company produced a type of cigarette. They initially created a flat advertising image for this cigarette, which opened the cigarette box and revealed half of the cigarettes inside, presenting it flatly to the people's eyes; later, they created a three-dimensional image, specially taking out two cigarettes from a box and presenting them in a three-dimensional way in the image. As a result, according to research, the latter gave people a deeper impression. We can also feel this situation if we pay attention to the advertising images in newspapers and on the roadside.

Of course, advertising images not only have the expression of pictures, but also have text descriptions. Therefore, in advertisements with both text and pictures, the order of arrangement becomes a question. Should the text be placed above? Or should the picture be placed above? This, of course, cannot be rigidly stipulated, but depends on the situation. However, generally speaking, because pictures are better at embodying objects and attracting attention, it is better to put the picture above and the text below in general. If, in addition to the main text expression, you also want to use a few simple sentences to supplement the explanation to increase the effectiveness of the advertisement, then these supplementary explanations should be placed next to the picture, and the font should of course be smaller, while the main expression should undoubtedly use a larger font and be placed below the advertisement or in other places that can achieve the greatest effect.

Whether it is text-based or text-and-picture advertising, special attention should be paid to the target audience of the goods. Here I can cite an interesting fact: a certain hotel transported a type of wine from the inland. Some people initially advocated naming the wine Guifei (Imperial Concubine) wine, meaning that Yang Guifei could attract the masses; but some people opposed this name and advocated naming it Taibai wine, on the grounds that Yang Guifei was not as good as Taibai at drinking. "Taibai drinks a dou of wine and writes a hundred poems" is something that generally pleases those who love wine; the result was that the latter was adopted, and a statue of Taibai with a strong sense of drunkenness was made as the advertisement. This is paying attention to the target audience of the advertisement. In addition, there should also be distinctions in advertising for the elderly, young people, children, and people from various social strata, and cannot be generalized. Taking the cigarettes that people generally love to smoke as an example, the lower and even middle classes not

Page 22

only can only afford to smoke cigarettes that cost a dozen copper coins a box, but also want to get a little profit from it, so recently many cigarettes of this type have small prizes (such as matches, soap, etc.), which is very correct; some cigarettes of this type do not adopt this method and state in the advertisement that they are unwilling to make such a waste, in my opinion, this is not recognizing the target audience. Conversely, high-end cigarettes smoked by noble people naturally do not need to take the method of giving prizes for smoking, because noble people do not seek those small profits, they mainly want the goods to be beautiful and noble.

In addition, in the competition of advertising, we must pay close attention to the situation of the business world; we must know the advantages and weaknesses of our competitors; we must be steady and not be afraid of sacrifice, just like gambling;... In this way, entering and exiting the business world, coupled with ingenious advertising techniques, the possibility of victory is very high.

Amateur Study

How to Study Music? 185

— Lu Ping

According to the general public's view, music is a kind of entertainment, so those who like to play the piano, harp, flute, and flute are mostly considered to be people who like to play. However, everyone knows that sad music can make people sad and want to cry. Joyful songs can make people feel happy and crazy, and passionate tunes can also make people excited and nervous: these facts fully prove that music, like other arts, has the function of organizing human emotions and thoughts, and plays a positive role in our lives. For example, religion uses music to preach, the military uses music to encourage soldiers, and the state uses music to educate the people; more concretely, such as the great role played by the Marseillaise in the French Revolution, the Soviet Union's use of music in all aspects to improve the cultural level of its people, and Christians' use of singing to gather crowds to promote the doctrine of "Jesus loves me, I love Jesus," are all practical evidence. Therefore, if we want to study music, we should not treat it as a kind of entertainment to play with, but should study it as an art that serves our lives.

Furthermore, it is generally believed that studying music is nothing more than learning musical skills, such as how to play the piano, how to play the violin, etc. However, even if the piano and violin are played very well, if you do not understand the theory of music, you can only be regarded as a highly skilled technician, and cannot be called a musician. A true musician not only has certain musical skills, but also understands the theory of music, or can write songs and musical scores. Therefore, our study of music is not biased towards technology, but mainly studies its theory. The question of how to study music cannot be scrutinized in a piecemeal way; learning musical skills requires long-term practice based on many mechanical laws.

If we want to study music theoretically, we must first understand what music is and understand its relationship with human life. As mentioned above, music is an art; its characteristic is to organize human thoughts and emotions with harmonious sounds. If sound is a phenomenon of matter in nature and society, then thoughts and emotions are the product of human life, and not illusory and magical things. According to the investigation of historians and artists, in primitive times, music did not have an independent form, but was only a simple song or a harmonious cry of organizing labor that occurred in the process of human labor, which fundamentally could not be separated from labor itself. When human life had moved away from the primitive state to a considerable extent and became more complex, music could be formed accordingly; and its flowering period was in the Greek era when society had already had group divisions. From this fact, we can know that the origin of music is inseparable from human labor life, and it develops with the development of human life. Therefore, our central standpoint in studying music is to study it from the perspective of human life and the perspective of society; only in this way can we understand all musical phenomena. For example, the music of the medieval feudal aristocracy is combined with gods and religion, and its form is characterized by solemnity; and the content and formal characteristics of the music of classicism, romanticism, and naturalism since the Renaissance are the same as those of these literary genres; but these phenomena cannot be understood unless they are studied from the lives of the medieval feudal aristocracy and the developing citizens after the Renaissance.

Here we can also cite a more practical modern example to talk about the problem. That is, according to common sense, music emphasizes harmony and rhythm; the so-called noise has always been despised by general musicians. But in the new era of the twentieth century, with the emergence of futurism in literature, futurism in music also appeared. The former destroyed general grammar in creation, and the latter completely ignored harmony and rhythm in music, and strived to explore noise. They declared: "The art of music, in order to entertain our hearing with gentle harmony, has explored transparency, purity, and sweetness. But the current art of music is exploring the most chaotic, strangest, and sharpest mixture of sounds." Why? Because they feel: "In all our discoveries in life, noise is accompanied by it, and noise has a force that guides us to life. On the contrary, the ordinary musical sounds that have nothing to do with life, a kind of mutually separated sounds - become a more familiar image to the eyes, and too familiar to the ears. Unmusical and irregular noise hides infinite surprises for us. We are convinced that sharing noise (everything) and letting them respond to each other will enrich life from invisible joy." Such a strange phenomenon may surprise you. But, if we can socially examine the era and land in which futurist music was produced, then this strange phenomenon is not difficult to understand. In fact, such futurist music appeared in Italy, a young capitalist country in the new era of the twentieth century, as an artistic genre. Because at this time, Italy was a young capitalist country, where there were mechanical noises, the noise of streetcars and automobiles, and the noise of urban crowds, so futurist musicians had the object of "irregular noise"; also, because the living conditions of the intellectuals in young capitalist Italy were unexpectedly bad, and the citizens also held aggressive ambitions, so the futurist musicians, as a group of intellectuals, followed the citizens of Italy, were dominated by moneybags, and stood on the position of the citizens to vigorously praise machinery and express its aggressive ambitions. In this way, even such futurist music is not understood by us?

Secondly, we should study the musical theory itself. Because although music is a product of society, it has not lost its characteristics and independence as a result; on the contrary, to have its characteristics and independence is to have its meaning of existence, so that it can be understood socially, otherwise there is no way to grasp it. Therefore, after we know how to study music socially, we still need to study music theory, music form, harmony, etc. according to the characteristics of music. Naturally, the study of music theory, etc., should also be studied socially, because even the characteristics of music exist in its social nature; however, in order not to cause confusion, and in order to clarify the characteristics of the problem, it is still necessary to specifically propose the study of music theory itself.

The so-called music theory is the knowledge on the music score, such as symbols, rhythms, musical terms, intervals, scales, etc. The so-called musical form is the various forms of musical songs, such as sacrificial songs, symphonies, sonatas, etc. As for harmony, it is the study of the organization of sounds and the usage of strings. In addition, there are also the structures of various musical instruments, the history of the development of the instruments themselves, etc., which must be studied separately. Although these studies are somewhat close to technical theory, to be a musician, if you do not understand the rhythm, form, sound structure of music, as well as the names and structures of many musical instruments, it is impossible.

At the same time, because music is a field of art, the artistic trends of an era have an inseparable relationship with the music of that time. For example, the characteristics and tendencies of futurist literature and futurist music mentioned above are completely the same, which is a clear example; therefore, we study music not only to study its characteristics and social nature, to study its history of development, to understand its position in art, and to understand the roots of the musical trends that occur in each era. Otherwise, many musical phenomena cannot be understood in the general artistic trends, and the result is that the study of music becomes isolated, becomes unrelated to the study of art, and therefore the knowledge obtained in the study is bound to be imperfect.

However, what has been said above is only the points that should be paid attention to in the general study of music. Below this, there are many more special and specialized studies, which require more special knowledge and laws. For example, when studying the violin, in addition to having the general musical knowledge mentioned above, we should also study the origin and structure of the violin and its position in music, study why putting four silk threads on a pair of wooden boxes becomes such an instrument, and why the sound of the violin is so mellow and soft, etc. The same applies to learning the piano, etc.

In this way, is it not very difficult to study music and want to become a musician? Indeed, this is more difficult than the study of general art; in fact, how many Beethovens have there been from ancient times to the present? From this, we can see the difficulty of the birth of a great musician. However, we do not necessarily hope to become Beethoven when we study music, but mainly to learn a little musical knowledge and skills to serve society and to promote music education. Moreover, if we want a new Beethoven to be born, we must popularize music education and improve the general level of musical knowledge. As in the current Soviet Union, because general music education is very popular, and every effort is made to enable every citizen to have some musical knowledge and skills, many young musical geniuses have appeared there. Now, if we want to have musical geniuses appear, we should also work hard to popularize music education.

Amateur Cafe

Talking About "Constancy" 186

— Tao Wang

There is no such thing as "permanence" in the world.

People think that the individual can still be considered alive during the time when it is active, and the world mostly takes life as "constant," so death, which is its opposite, is "impermanent." In fact, according to the so-called theory of cell metabolism, we can know that not only is the "I" of last year not the "I" of this year, but also the "I" of yesterday is not the "I" of today, and not only is the "I" of yesterday not the "I" of today, but even the "I" of the previous second is not the "I" of this second. The cells in the individual are always following one after another, and there is never a "constant" to be found in this. Therefore, when a person dies, his relatives, friends, or other more related people are often shocked by this "impermanent" scene, but no one pays attention to the fact that the person is dying at every moment.

There is no feast in the world that does not end, things change, and stars move, within a hundred years, the sea of ​​yesterday will now be plowed into mulberry fields. Nature is like this, how can human affairs be unique? Therefore, after seeing these things that the Buddhists call "impermanent," no matter how emotional you are as a poet or writer, you will not be able to keep up with the sighs.

In the end, human emotions are mostly calm. Many extraordinary stimuli in life end up with the calm lake of the heart no longer rising with turbulent waves because people are used to seeing flowers, plants, reds, and greens. However, this is hidden, not disappeared. You only need to look at deep and experienced people, who often cannot help but feel lost and sentimental at every victory, and you can know this. Cao Mengde was indeed a hero of the world, but when he was composing poetry on the piled spears, he could not help but feel sad from it?

Although, there are still many people in the world who live muddled and carefree lives. In the play Great Hotel, travelers from all over the world come and go, trying to gain profit, with joys, sorrows, partings, and reunions, making the grand hotel like a grand theater. As one tragic or comedic scene after another is played, the front of the grand hotel is still as busy as usual, with cars flowing like water and horses like dragons. But in this busy state, the rehearsal of the second act of tragedy or comedy is being conceived, and the performances that follow are emerging one after another. In this huge grand hotel, there are no fewer than hundreds or thousands of people, and only one calm and observant mysterious and strange doctor is constantly sighing about this impermanent human world.

Because the human world is impermanent, there is "human suffering." It is precisely because the human world inevitably has various pains that cannot be treated by material things, that art and religion are produced. Therefore, Shirakawa Hakumura said: Literature and art are symbols of depression.

The politics and economy of a country are also constantly changing in the process of impermanence. The facts are very obvious, and we do not need to go far to the Tang and Yu dynasties. Even by picking up current affairs, there are good examples: stores that operate normal businesses collapse like ice cubes in the vortex of impermanence, while only companies and commercial firms that operate prize ticket businesses have the prosperity to carry on the past and open up the future. Therefore, the business that the people of the country regard as a matter of pennies and ounces, its future is also very impermanent.

However, according to the above, there are many grammatical errors, because politics and economics have a proper trajectory to follow in the process of history, and these can only be regarded as "abnormal" phenomena.

It is said that this time is again a "time of emergency." The time of emergency is exactly what our esteemed neighbor is shouting about all day long. For the preparation of the time of emergency, they do not hesitate to destroy the principles and regulations. What a sharp cry that is! However, looking around, it is as if a derailed train is falling from the abyss of abnormality and abnormality!

"Emergency" and "abnormal" both belong to "impermanence," because their opposite "constancy" is the same.

Life

Storytelling Masters 187

— Gu Wu

"Storytelling," is originally a kind of folk art, but because it doesn't quite appeal to the literati class, it's been regarded as a "trivial skill" and "not worth mentioning." In fact, we only need to step into any "storytelling venue" to see the audience to know that its potential power is enough to make you say "great!"

The most popular place for "storytelling" is Jiangsu and Zhejiang provinces, and Shanghai and Suzhou are even more lively. Secondly, it is also very popular in the Yangtze River basin and the northern regions. Of course, there are many "story fans," but compared with Jiangsu and Zhejiang provinces, it seems to be a bit inferior. Storytelling is called "tanci" in Suzhou, "storytelling" in Shanghai, Beijing, Hangzhou, Ningbo and other places, and "xiangsheng" in the north. As for the Yangtze River basin such as Jiangxi, Hubei, Hunan and other provinces, some call it "storytelling" and some call it "telling old tales." Since the name of storytelling varies from place to place, the "storytelling techniques" are also different.

Suzhou's "storytelling" mostly uses "pipa" accompaniment. Sometimes the storyteller is a "double act," and sometimes it is a "single act." The lyrics of the story are either told directly from the original book, or new lyrics are created. In terms of storytelling skills, it all depends on the display of each person's talent. The appropriate use of jokes and banter makes the audience feel as if they are there, forgetting themselves. When "one episode" of the story is finished, they still feel that there is "still an aftertaste" and don't want to leave. There are indeed quite a few storytelling talents like this in Suzhou. In Shanghai, such as the "Oriental Storytelling Theater" and various teahouses, although some storytelling talents are prominent for a while, they all come from Suzhou after all, which is not surprising.

The "xiangsheng" in the north is slightly different from the tanci in the south, that is, one only "speaks" and "acts" but does not "sing," and the other only "speaks" and "sings" but does not "act." Although the "xiangsheng" in the north was as popular as storytelling in Suzhou for a while, the talent is not as "prolific" as in Suzhou. However, according to the elders in the storytelling circle in Suzhou, although storytelling in the south is more common than before, there is still a tendency for "each generation to be inferior to the previous one" in terms of talent. Because in the past, people who learned storytelling mostly put in hard work in classical studies, so when telling stories, they could use the words and sentences quite freely. Moreover, many people did not intend to take "storytelling" as a profession at first, so most of them "did not respect teachers," and only relied on their own talent to perform. However, the situation is different now. Recently, some up-and-coming storytellers haven't even figured out many words in the books, and they still want to "debut" without knowing their own limitations. On the one hand, some elders in the storytelling circle, seeing that they are getting older, are afraid that their life's work cannot be "passed on," so they casually accept one or two apprentices to inherit their "mantle." On the other hand, there are many frustrated storytellers who have learned a lot of "skills," but their fate is not good, and they have been unknown all their lives, so they want to create one or two outstanding apprentices to "show off" and help them regain some face. But there is also a kind of storyteller who, because their own life is not easy to solve, also takes in one or two apprentices to collect a "tuition fee."

Learning storytelling and worshipping a teacher is like learning Peking opera. Most of them start learning from a young age. Although there are some "self-taught" people, they are a very small minority. A friend of mine's child was introduced to worship a storyteller as a "master." The "tuition fee" was one hundred yuan, and a table of wine was prepared to invite the "master." At the banquet, the introducer helped the friend write a "formal apprenticeship contract." The procedure was completed like this. The term of study is three years. After the term expires, the master will introduce the apprentice to "debut" or "partner" with the master. However, there are also apprentices who have studied for three years and their "skills" are still not "up to par," and the master can ignore the apprentice's future. There is also another kind of storyteller who does not necessarily need any "tuition fee" to accept apprentices, and teaches apprentices in the same way. However, this kind of apprentice has no freedom. As the saying goes, "Once a teacher, always a father." All actions after worshipping the teacher must be decided by the master. Apprentices who pay to worship a teacher are just buying "skills." Their actions are extremely casual, and the master does not restrain them at all. Every day "learning skills," the master first sets a time, and most of them are in the afternoon, because storytellers have a habit of using day as night. They are unwilling to get up before three o'clock in the afternoon every day. When learning, the apprentice first copies a "blueprint," and memorizes the words and sentences on it like reading in school. Then the master teaches sentence by sentence like teaching Peking opera, with rhythm and cadence. Most storytellers have many hobbies. In addition to liking to sleep late, eating opium is also indispensable. Therefore, teaching apprentices to learn storytelling is mostly in front of the opium shop, taking a puff of opium and teaching a few sentences. By the time more than a dozen sentences of the book are taught, almost one or two hours have been spent. With this slow and perfunctory teaching method, an apprentice often follows him for three years, but has not learned three books. Many mediocre storytelling talents today are made in this way.

When storytelling first "debuts," it is mostly "partnering" with the master, just like the "supporting old male role" in Peking opera, only singing some simple lyrics, just taking the opportunity to practice. There are also apprentices who "debut" and take charge of the show on their own without relying on the master's reputation, but there are still few apprentices with this kind of courage.

If a newly "debuted" storyteller can "draw a crowd" in a "storytelling venue" once, then he will not have to worry about being hired for three to five years. A "popular" storyteller earns at least one or two hundred yuan a month. Sometimes he also works as a storyteller in three or four "storytelling venues," which is more than that. Their source of income is either a net monthly salary or a "split." The standard for taking a salary depends on the reputation of the storyteller. The highest salary is about sixty to eighty yuan, and the rest, such as forty yuan or so, are very common. Those who do "split" split equally, calculated according to the income of the tickets. It is said that sometimes it is richer than taking a salary, but sometimes it is not certain. "Storytelling venues" such as Shanghai's Dongfang and Wuyuan are almost all doing "split." According to people in the venue, when business is good, a storyteller can earn two or three hundred yuan. In recent years, Shanghai's storytelling talents have been relatively developed, mostly because it is easier to make money than in Suzhou. Listening to a story in Suzhou costs at most one or two hundred coins, including tea money. The teahouse gives the rest to the storyteller except for the tea money. One can imagine how much a storyteller can earn in a day from this. Therefore, some famous storytellers in Suzhou have almost all rushed to Shanghai, which is covered with gold.

Speaking of the life of storytellers in the Yangtze River area, it is even more miserable than that of storytellers in Suzhou. I lived in Jiujiang for a while, and I saw that the storytellers there were miserably poor. I lived in Jiujiang for a while, and I saw that the storytellers there found an open space by the river, and placed a dozen or so long benches crisscross. Each bench could seat about ten people. In the middle of the space, there was a bamboo frame like a fortune-telling stall, with a teapot and a "戒方(clapper)," and a small drum. This was the layout of a "storytelling venue." The listeners were all porters who made a living by the mountains. After carrying the goods, they came to listen to a story. The storyteller was a tall, thin man with a complexion as dark as opium. He walked to the table supported by the bamboo frame, took a few sips of tea, and tapped the small drum with a thin bamboo pole for a while. Then he said a little "introduction" to the audience, and then took a few more sips of tea before "getting back to the point" and continuing the story that he had not finished before. The listeners all lowered their heads and listened attentively. The venue was really "quiet as a grave." Before half an hour had passed, the clapper suddenly sounded, and the storyteller stopped talking. He took a pair of bamboo baskets and walked down to the venue, smilingly saying "Thank you for your patronage" to each listener. Many people searched in their pockets, and for a while, all that could be heard was the clanging of copper coins. After collecting the money, he started telling the story again. In less than half an hour, he "repeated the process." I heard him stop abruptly at a tense part of the story. He told the story for a total of four hours, and looking at the copper coins on the bamboo frame table, there were less than two hundred coins. If you convert it into local dollars, it was only more than five jiao.

Short Special Article

Biology in the 18th Century 188

— Yue Xing

As early as the seventeenth century, entomology can be said to be quite precise; but in the science of life, no major changes occurred as a result. It was not until the eighteenth century that people began to classify organisms, and evolutionary views appeared in biology, and modern biology can be said to have taken shape in general. Therefore, if we want to study modern biology and even general natural science, we must know about biology in the eighteenth century.

The first person to classify organisms was Linnaeus (1707-1778). His greatest achievement was to sort out the many materials that already existed at that time and give them a unified naming; the current naming method of zoology and botany was established by him. He advocated naming the species of organisms with two words: the first word indicates the genus to which it belongs, and the second word indicates the species. He began to adopt this naming method in 1749; in the Species plantarum in 1753 and the tenth edition of "Systema Naturae" in 1758, he generally implemented his advocacy.

Linnaeus' classification is artificial in nature. As Kerner said, Linnaeus did not think that the classification of the twenty-four orders in his plant kingdom was its natural classification; he believed that the highest goal of botanical research was to complete the natural system based on the species of plants shown by the characteristics of the structure. But he only left some fragments and did not complete this so-called natural system.

The second feature of his research is the emphasis on the idea of species. Originally, Ray (1628-1705) was the first to introduce the concept of species in natural history, and he studied its changes. Linnaeus' research was based on Ray's research, but in his early works, he believed that species were fixed and unchanging. He believed that when the earth was formed, various animals were created, and the current species are the unchanged direct descendants of the original species. His position of fixed and unchanging species is an anti-evolutionary position, which only changed slightly until the continued edition of his "Systema Naturae."

Such a theory of biological invariance is combined with religious myths. From ancient times to the Renaissance and even before the eighteenth century, most scholars stood on such a theological position, thinking that all living beings now were purely descendants of past organisms, not from evolution. Of course, there were evolutionary views in ancient times, but they had no practical basis; the establishment of the theory of evolution cannot but be said to be a matter of the eighteenth and even the nineteenth century. We know that the theory of evolution in the modern sense should first be attributed to Lamarck's (1744-1829) theory of variation, the theory of use and disuse, but Lamarck was a figure active in the eighteenth and nineteenth centuries; his predecessors, we can cite Erasmus Darwin (1731-1802) and the poet Goethe (1747-1832), but these two were also figures who lived from the eighteenth century to the beginning of the nineteenth century. Therefore, we say that the beginning of evolutionary thought was in the eighteenth century: this is what we must pay special attention to when talking about biology in the eighteenth century.

The sprouting of evolutionary thought can first be seen in the writings of Buffon, who lived in the same era as Linnaeus. From studying many animals, he got the hint that organisms would change due to various reasons such as weather and geography. From the result of comparing various organisms in terms of their system, he knew that there was a common general plan existing in all organisms, and humans were of course no exception. This means that the natural environment can affect the organizational changes of organisms; the current

Page 23

The life of living things has been changed and evolved, not in such a form from ancient times.

Secondly, the great poet Goethe mentioned the idea of evolution in his "Metamorphosis of Plants" in 1790. When studying the organs of organisms, he specially compared the various organs of each organism, so that he came to the conclusion that the organs of each organism gradually became true due to the influence of the environment; finally, he hinted that the origin of all species conforms to the theory of evolution.

But in this era, the person who integrated the theory of evolution can be said to be Erasmus Darwin, the grandfather of Charles Darwin. In his book "Zoonoma" in 1794, he explained that organisms were not exactly the same as they are today at the beginning, and the shape of today's organisms is the result of gradual evolution. He believed that organisms change with the environment; all kinds of organisms have close blood relations, and the similarities shown between human arms and bird wings show this blood relationship between organisms, and show that all organisms have the same ancestor.

Finally, what should be said is the development of physiology at that time, which is closely related to biology in the eighteenth century.

Physiology can be said to have developed from anatomy. Anatomy can show the complex structure of animals and plants, but when we understand these complex structures, we will inevitably have such questions: What are these organs and tissues for? What role do they actually play? The answer to this question is physiology. Therefore, physiology can be said to supplement anatomy.

Originally, the physiology of animals and plants had been studied since the time of Aristotle, but it was in the eighteenth century that physiology became an independent discipline from anatomy. The person worth noting here is Haller (1708-1777). Based on his own observations and experiments, he organized a huge physiological system, and discovered the fundamental phenomenon of life in the so-called irritability; the result of his experiments further discovered that irritability is in the muscles and sensitivity is in the nerve elements. In this way, he was considered a pioneer in recognizing the autonomy of life.

The above is a general description of biology in the eighteenth century. Of course, the real completion and development of modern biology, strictly speaking, was in the nineteenth century after Lamarck was born, but the growth of biological classification, evolutionary thought, and physiology in the eighteenth century, as mentioned above, stands in a very important position in the development of modern biology and even natural science.

Training and Cultivation

Speaking Without Lying 189

— Guang Chen

The so-called telling the truth means that we speak without lying, and are completely able to tell the facts as they are, and express them absolutely faithfully, without adding any fabrication or forgery. Such a way of speaking seems to be generally considered the best and in accordance with morality by society, and it is also easy for everyone to do. In fact, it is not so. If you examine this issue from a philosophical point of view, telling the truth is a very difficult thing. Even if you examine this issue from the perspective of social science, telling the truth is not always in accordance with moral law.

The reason is very clear. If we only argue from a subjective point of view, the so-called telling the truth means telling what you see and think in your heart as it is, and this is considered telling the truth, and it is also easy to do. However, if we look at it from an objective point of view, the so-called truth must be able to express the reality of the real situation, and be able to explain the essence of real objective things, otherwise it cannot be considered the truth. In terms of such truth, in the field of philosophy, only the philosophy of materialism has been quite capable of telling the truth, and only modern new materialism can completely tell the real truth. As for all subjective, objective, and even dualistic idealistic philosophies, they are not telling the truth. Because in the real and true view of the universe, that is, in the view of the universe that can show the true essence of the universe and its development process, matter originally has self-existing reality, and human beings and their thinking are based on objective matter. Thinking is produced by the way of feeling through the method of experience, which reflects objective real things. Because thinking is the development, movement, and action of matter in the real world, the original laws and even the concepts of things existing in the process of thinking, if they are correct and can explain real things, then they must be reflections, conversions, and transpositions of objective reality, rather than subjective fictional fantasies. However, only materialistic philosophy can make such observations and explanations. In the eyes of idealists, it is just the opposite. In their words, matter originally existing in the objective world, they insist that it only exists in the subjective mind or feeling. Without my mind, there is no matter, and external objects do not exist. Originally, matter is the mother of mind, and existence produces thinking, but they say that mind is the mother of matter, and thinking produces existence, or that mind and matter are unrelated and exist independently. Matter and mind are two independent worlds and are discarded, and mind is not produced by matter. Thinking was originally to pass through the outside world through the sensation, and to obtain it through the method of experience, but they insisted that thinking is the revival of self-sufficient innate concepts, or at most just the synthesis of sensory elements within the subjective sensory bay, and is not a reflection of the outside world. All principles, laws, and concepts of things are grown up in the heart. From this point of view, the words spoken by idealistic philosophy can no longer express the true situation of the world, nor can they show the true process of the universe's development from the natural to the social and finally to the thinking. Saying that matter exists is saying that matter does not exist; saying that matter is knowable is saying that matter is unknowable; saying that thinking is produced by existence is saying that existence is produced by thinking, or that thinking exists independently; saying that the principles, laws, and concepts obtained from the objective world are self-created things of the mind, these are not telling the truth, but a kind of fantasy, a fabricated lie.

As for metaphysical materialists, although they also admit the objectivity of matter itself and real existence in the fundamental premise, and admit that thinking is produced by existence, this can be regarded as a kind of honest philosophical speech that can show the essence of the world, and there is no lying. But their honest words are also not very complete, because they can only honestly explain static and individual real things, but cannot tell the true situation of the dialectical and historical process of the universe. It is not so in the new materialism. It not only admits that matter itself exists and is knowable: it admits that thinking is produced by existence and that the subjective belongs to the objective: all principles, laws, and concepts must be obtained through feeling and experience before they can become reflections and conversions of the outside world; and that the real world is dialectical, and it uses dialectical thinking methods to understand and explain it. Because of this, if telling the truth is to be able to truly explain the true appearance of reality, and to explain it exactly as the real world is without fabricating, adding, or subtracting, then the speech of idealistic philosophy is not telling the truth, and according to its thinking and methods, it cannot tell the truth. The metaphysical materialistic philosophy only tells part of the truth, and according to its thinking and methods, it cannot tell the complete truth. Only new materialism, its own is the most complete truth, and only according to its point of view and method can it tell the most complete and perfect truth.

Of course, we cannot say that human beings have never told a little truth, nor can we imagine that any era can tell an eternally perfect truth. Because telling the truth is also subject to the limitations of time and space, and we cannot tell the kind of complete truth that we subjectively want to tell. In the historical process, if human beings want to be able to tell some real honest words that can show the essence of the objective world, first of all, it is related to the development of human beings' correct scientific knowledge. Primitive and semi-civilized human beings do not have a clear understanding of nature and society, so they say that all things are created by gods, or that the sun, moon, wind, clouds, rain, etc. are gods themselves; the happiness and misfortune of human social life are determined by fate in the dark. Such sayings are myths, lies, not telling the truth. However, when modern science is developed, people no longer say that the sun, moon, stars, and constellations are gods, but say that they are natural things; some people have been able to analyze in their life process that the pain they suffer is due to economic and social relations, and no longer say that it is determined by fate. Such a statement is more able to express the real situation of the real state.
